Chapter on the obligatory acts of ghusl. It is obligatory in ghusl eleven things: washing the mouth, nose, and the body. Chapter on the obligatory acts of ghusl. He mentioned it after wudu following the Noble Book, because the need for wudu is more, or because its place is part of the body, and the place of ghusl is the whole, and the part comes before the whole, and because it is sunnah to perform wudu before ghusl. (It is obligatory in ghusl from janabah, menstruation, and postpartum bleeding eleven things), and all of them revert to one thing: covering the body with water as much as possible without hardship, but he mentioned those counted as an easing and an alert to what is necessary to wash. Among them: (washing the mouth and nose), and it is a ijtihadi obligation, due to the difference of scholars, because Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, says they are sunnah, and we have the saying of the Exalted: 'And if you are in a state of janabah, then purify yourselves' [al-Ma'idah 5:6], i.e., wash your bodies, and the body includes the apparent and the inner, and whatever involves hardship is dropped due to necessity, and they are washed habitually and as worship, supererogatory in wudu, and obligatory in real impurity, so the text of the Book includes them, and it is a hyperbolical form, and His saying: 'Under every hair is janabah, so wet the hair and cleanse the skin' reported by al-Tirmidhi without contradiction. And His saying: 'Whoever leaves a hair of his body unwashed, such and such will be done to him from the Fire.' Ali said: 'Therefore I antagonized my hair and he used to shave it.' And the fact that both are from fitrah does not negate obligation, because fitrah is religion, which is more general, so it does not contradict; unlike them in wudu, because the face is what is encountered, and it is not inside the nose and mouth. (And the body) is an inclusive conjunction after a specific one, and we have previously indicated the condition of removing what prevents water from reaching the body, and the generality of coverage. So if he drinks water swallowing completely covering the mouth, it suffices, but it is better to expel the water because it becomes used water, and it is disliked a second time. And inside a foreskin that is not hard to retract, and navel, and a non-closed piercing, and inside the braided hair of a man absolutely, not the braided hair of a woman, if water reaches its roots... drinking it, because the correct view is that rinsing (maj) – which is expelling water after moving it in the mouth – is not a condition for maddah, even if his tooth is hollow, or there is moist food between his teeth, it suffices, because water is subtle and generally reaches every place, but caution is to remove it. Dry filth in the nose like chewed bread and dough prevents complete washing, like fish skin stuck to it, and what is on the dyer's nail does not prevent, and the fatwa is upon that, and likewise what is between the nails, whether city-dweller or villager, according to the correct view, and likewise flea excrement and fly defilement, i.e., its droppings, does not prevent. And it is obligatory to move a tight ring and earring, and if there is no earring in the piercing, water entering it suffices, and he is not obligated to insert anything other than water like a stick. And it is necessary for her to wash her external private part, because it is like the mouth, not the internal, because it is like the throat, so she does not insert her finger into it, and the attachment of a scab from a healed wound that has not separated from the skin does not harm, except for the exit of pus, even if water does not reach underneath, because it does not exit the ruling of the inner skin to this extent due to necessity. And he washes (once) completely covering, because the command does not require repetition. (And) it is obligatory to wash the inside of the foreskin, that is not hard to retract, according to the correct view; if retraction is impossible or difficult, it is not required, like a closed piercing due to hardship. And the foreskin is the skin covering the glans, and circumcision is cutting it as sunnah. (And) it is obligatory to wash the inside of a hollow (navel), because it is from the outer body, and there is no hardship in reaching water to it. (And) it is obligatory to wash a non-closed (piercing), because there is no hardship in it as well in reaching water to it. (And) it is obligatory to wash (the inside of the braided hair of a man), and he must undo it and wash it, (absolutely) according to the correct view, whether water reaches its roots or not, because it is not an adornment for him, so no hardship in undoing it. (Not) is it obligatory to undo the braided hair of a woman, if water reaches its roots, by agreement, due to the hadith of Umm Salamah: she said, 'I said, O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who braids my hair tightly, should I undo it for ghusl from janabah?' He said: 'It suffices you to pour three handfuls of water over your head, then pour water over the rest of your body, and you become pure.' And because there is hardship for her in undoing it. And similarly for shaving, it is dropped, unlike a man, and unlike if her hair is matted or abundant, because water does not reach its roots. And his saying: 'if water reaches its roots' negates the obligation of wetting her braids (dhawāib) and the thickness of her hair, and this is the most correct view due to the hadith of Umm Salamah, and in al-Hidayah: it is the correct view. And it is a caution against the hanging (hair).
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is a commentary on the chapter on the obligatory acts of ghusl. It begins by stating that there are eleven obligatory acts, but then explains that all of them effectively reduce to one: covering the body with water as much as possible without hardship. The listing of eleven is for clarity and to alert the one washing to what must be washed. The author then specifically addresses the dispute regarding rinsing the mouth and nose. The Hanafi position is that these are obligatory (fard) in ghusl, while Imam al-Shafi'i considers them sunnah. The Hanafi proof includes the Quranic verse 'fa'taharu' (purify yourselves), which is interpreted as washing the body, and the body includes the interior parts that are typically washed (mouth and nose). The hadith 'Under every hair is janabah' and the statement of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) are also cited. The author then addresses the objection that mouth and nose are from the fitrah (natural disposition), arguing that fitrah is broader and does not negate obligation. The difference from wudu is also explained, as the face in wudu is external only. The commentary then proceeds to various details: if one swallows water it suffices, but it is better to expel it; the ruling on tight rings, earrings, piercings, and the foreskin; the obligation to wash the inner parts that are accessible without hardship; the difference between men's and women's braided hair; and the conditions for water reaching the roots. The ruling on braces, scabs, and various impurities is also mentioned. Throughout, the author follows the order of the original text (Nur al-Idah), expanding each point with evidence and practical details.

Key Terms
فَرْض (fard): An obligatory act that is established by definitive evidence (qat'i); omission invalidates the act.
غُسْل (ghusl): Ritual bath to remove major impurity (janabah, hayd, nifas).
مَضْمَضَة (maddah): Rinsing the mouth with water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary evidence that rinsing the mouth and nose are fard in ghusl?
A) The hadith 'Under every hair is janabah' alone.
B) The Quranic verse 'fa'taharu' (5:6) interpreted as washing the body, which includes interior accessible parts.
C) The consensus of the Companions.
D) The statement of Ali that he shaved his hair.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that rinsing the mouth and nose are fard in ghusl based on the inclusive nature of the Quranic command 'fa'taharu' and the hadith emphasizing complete coverage of the body.

Obligations of Ghusl: Washing Body Parts and Hair
Fiqh ruling on obligatory parts of ghusl with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the obligatory parts to wash in ghusl and apply the Hanafi rulings on braided hair, beard, and openings, using the hadith of Umm Salama as proof.

Core Idea
In ghusl, every external body part must be washed, with ease only where hardship is established.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah Sharh Nur al-Idah explains the precise boundaries of the obligation to wash the body during ghusl (full ablution). It clarifies that even the interior of the foreskin, the navel cavity, open piercings, and the skin beneath a thick beard must be washed in ghusl, unlike wudu. A significant portion addresses braided hair, granting women ease based on the hadith of Umm Salama, while men are required to undo braids. Understanding these details ensures one's ghusl is valid and free from common oversights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligatory parts
Scan the passage to list all body parts explicitly mentioned: foreskin (qulfah), navel, open holes (thaqb), braided hair (masfur), skin and hair of beard, mustache, eyebrows, and external genitals. Note that each is ruled fard to wash.
These parts are additional to the general command to wash the entire body.
2
Note exceptions due to hardship
Identify where the obligation is waived if hardship (haraj) exists: a foreskin that cannot be retracted, a navel that has closed, a closed hole. For a woman's braids, if water reaches the roots, she need not undo them. These exceptions follow the Hanafi principle of removing hardship.
Hardship is defined as difficulty that cannot normally be borne.
3
Analyze the proof for women's braids
Examine the hadith of Umm Salama where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said three handfuls on the head suffice for a woman with tight braids. This is the primary dalil for the Hanafi position. Understand how it overrides the general command 'fa-tahharu' through the principle of specification (takhsis).
The hadith is found in Muslim, Tirmidhi, and Abu Dawood.
4
Distinguish ghusl from wudu regarding the beard
The passage contrasts wudu, where only the outer part of a thick beard is washed, with ghusl, where the skin underneath must be washed. The reason is that in wudu, the face is defined by the outer beard, but in ghusl, the entire body includes the skin under hair.
The same applies to the mustache and eyebrows.
5
Apply the cost of water note
The passage adds a fiqhi note: the cost of water for a woman's ghusl is upon her husband, even if she is wealthy, because it is an absolute necessity. This highlights the husband's financial responsibility for his wife's religious duties.
Some later scholars differentiate based on whether the ghusl is for resuming marital relations or for prayer.

(وَ) يفترض غسل داخل سُرَّةٍ مجوفة، لأنه من ظاهر الجسد، ولا حرج في إيصال الماء إليه، (وَ) يفترض غسل ثقب غير مُنْضَمّ ؛ لعدم الحرج فيه أيضاً، بإيصال الماء إليه، (وَ) يفترض غسل داخل المَصْفُورِ مِنْ فتطهرين» ؛ ولأن في النقض حرجاً عليها. وفي الحلق مثله فسقط، بخلاف الرجل، وبخلاف ما إذا كان شعرها ملبداً أو غزيراً؛ لعدم وصول الماء إلى أصوله، وقوله: إن سرى الماء في أصوله، ينفي وجوب بل ذوائبها ، وأثناء الضرورة، وهو احتراز أيضاً عن قول بعضهم يجب بلها، لقولـه عليه الصلاة والسلام: «فبلوا الشعر» . وعما روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة: أنَّها تبلّ ذوائبها ثلاثاً مع كل بلة عصرة؛ ليبلغ الماء شعب قرونها، وعما في صلاة البقالي الصحيح أنه يجب غسل الذوائب، وإن جاوزت القدمين، لأن حديث أم سلمة صريح في عدم النقض فقط، وهذا، أي: قوله : « فبلوا الشعر» ناطق ببلها، مع عدم لحوق الحرج فيه، ولهذا وجب غسل المنقوض من شعرها؛ لعدم الحرج في إيصال الماء إلى أثنائه كاللحية، ولأنه من بدنها، نظراً إلى أصوله، قلنا: قوله : ( إنما يكفيك أن تحثي على رأسك...) صريح في عدم بل الذوائب، لأنها ليست على الرأس، حتى لا يصح مسحها عن فرض الممسوح من الرأس، فإن قيل: قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاطَهَرُوا يتناول الجميع، قلنا: يتناول جميع البدن، والشعر ليس من البدن من كل وجه، بل متصل به، نظراً إلى أصوله، ومنفصل عنه، نظراً إلى أطرافه، فعملنا بأصله في حق من لا يلحقه الحرج، وبطرفه في حق من يلحقه الحرج. والضفيرة بالضاد المعجمة الذؤابة، وهي: الخصلة من الشعر، والصَّفْر : فتل الشعر وإدخال بعضه في بعض، ولا يقال: بالظاء المشالة. تنبيه: ثمن ماء غسل المرأة، ووضوئها على الزوج، وإن كانت غنية، كماء الشرب، لأنه مما لا بد منه مطلقاً، وبعضهم قال: إذا كان انقطاع الحيض لأقل من عشرة، فعلى الزوج، لاحتياجه إلى وطئها بعد الغسل، وإن كان لعشرة، فعليها، لأنها هي المحتاجة للصلاة، (وَ) يفترض غسل بَشَرَةِ اللحية وشعرها، ولو كانت كثيفة كثة، نص عليه، لئلا يتوهم أن حكمها حكم الوضوء، والفرق أن اللحية الكثيفة تحصل المواجهة بظاهرها لا بباطنها، فلا يكلف في الوضوء لغسل غير ظاهرها ، وأما في الاغتسال من الجنابة فهو فرض، لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاطَهَرُوا﴾ ولحديث أم سلمة المتقدم، (و) كذا بَشَرَةِ الشارب، (وَ) بشرة الحاجب، وشعرهما، (والفَرْجِ الخارج) لا الداخل، لما قدمناه.
And it is obligatory to wash the inside of the foreskin if there is no difficulty in retracting it, according to the correct view. But if retracting it is impossible or difficult, he is not obligated, like a hole that has closed due to hardship. The foreskin is the skin covering the glans, and circumcision is cutting it as a sunnah. And it is obligatory to wash the inside of a hollow navel because it is from the outer body and there is no hardship in reaching water to it. And it is obligatory to wash a non-closed hole because there is no hardship in reaching water to it. And it is obligatory to wash the inside of a man's braided hair, and he must undo it and wash it, absolutely according to the correct view, whether water penetrates to its roots or not, because it is not an adornment for him, so there is no hardship in undoing it. It is not obligatory to undo a woman's braided hair if water reaches its roots by agreement, due to the hadith of Umm Salama that she said: 'I said: O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who tightens the braid of my head, shall I undo it for ghusl of janabah? He said: It suffices you that you pour three handfuls of water on your head, then pour water over the rest of your body, and you become purified.' And because there is hardship for her in undoing it. And the same applies to shaving, so it is waived, unlike a man, and unlike if her hair is matted or thick, due to water not reaching its roots. And his statement: 'if water reaches its roots' negates the obligation of wetting her braids and the inner parts of her hair, and this is the most correct view due to the hadith of Umm Salama. In al-Hidayah it is said: this is the correct view. And it is a precaution against the hanging hair of a man, for it is obligatory to deliver water to it, that is the correct view, as stated in Sharh al-Munyah, acting on the implication of exaggeration in the verse with the absence of necessity. And it is also a precaution against the statement of some that it is obligatory to wet it, due to his statement peace be upon him: 'Wet the hair.' And against what was narrated by al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa that she wets her braids three times, squeezing each time, so that water reaches the partings of her locks. And against what is in Salat al-Baqali that the correct view is that washing the braids is obligatory even if they extend beyond the feet, because the hadith of Umm Salama is explicit only about not undoing, and this, i.e., his statement: 'Wet the hair' speaks of wetting it, with no hardship involved. Hence washing the undone part of her hair is obligatory due to no hardship in reaching water to its interior like the beard, and because it is from her body, considering its roots. We say: his statement: 'It suffices you that you pour on your head' is explicit in not wetting the braids because they are not on the head, such that wiping it would not be valid for the obligatory wiping of the head. If it is said: the verse 'and purify yourselves' includes all, we say: it includes all the body, and hair is not part of the body from every aspect; rather it is connected to it considering its roots, and separated from it considering its ends. So we act on its roots for the one who faces no hardship, and on its ends for the one who faces hardship. And al-dafira (with the dotted daad) is the braid, i.e., a lock of hair, and al-safr is twisting hair and inserting some into others, and it is not said with the dotted za. Note: The cost of water for a woman's ghusl and wudu is upon the husband, even if she is wealthy, like drinking water, because it is absolutely necessary. Some said: if the cessation of menses is for less than ten days, it is upon the husband due to his need to have intercourse with her after ghusl, and if for ten days, it is upon her because she is the one who needs prayer. And it is obligatory to wash the skin of the beard and its hair, even if it is thick and dense, as stated, lest one think its ruling is like wudu. The difference is that the thick beard presents its outer side not its inner side, so in wudu one is not obligated to wash other than its apparent part, but in ghusl from janabah it is obligatory due to the verse 'and purify yourselves' and the hadith of Umm Salama mentioned earlier. Likewise the skin of the mustache, and the skin of the eyebrows and their hair, and the external genitals, not the internal, as we have stated earlier.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the obligatory parts to wash in ghusl (full bath) according to the Hanafi school. It covers several specific areas: the foreskin (if easily retracted), the navel, any open hole (like a piercing that has not closed), and braided hair. For a man's braided hair, it must be undone and washed even if water would otherwise reach the roots, because it is not considered adornment and there is no hardship. For a woman, if her hair is braided and water can reach the roots, she does not need to undo it, based on the hadith of Umm Salama. However, if water does not reach the roots (e.g., hair is matted or very thick), then she must undo it. The passage also discusses the skin of the beard, mustache, eyebrows, and external genitals; all must be washed in ghusl, unlike in wudu where only the outer part of a thick beard is required. The ruling about the cost of water for a woman's ghusl being on the husband is also mentioned, with a detail about when menses ends. The commentary by the author resolves a potential objection about the verse 'and purify yourselves' by explaining that hair is partly body (roots) and partly separate (ends), and the obligation is tailored accordingly to avoid hardship.

Key Terms
قُلْفَة (qulfah): The foreskin covering the glans of the penis; it must be washed in ghusl if easily retracted.
المَصْفُور (al-masfur): Braided hair; the passage distinguishes between men's and women's braided hair for ghusl.
ذوائب (dhawa'ib): Braids of hair that hang down; the passage discusses whether they must be wet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is a woman required to undo her braided hair for ghusl?
A) Always, because water must reach every strand.
B) Only if water cannot reach the roots of the hair.
C) Only if the her husband requests it.
D) Never, because braids are considered adornment.

Key Takeaway
Every external part of the body, including creases and hair roots, must be washed in ghusl, with ease granted only where hardship is established.

Obligatory Washing of Skin and Hair in Ghusl
Ruling with proof on obligatory washing of skin and hair in ghusl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligatory parts to wash in ghusl, explain the Hanafi proof for washing skin and hair, and distinguish between wudu and ghusl regarding the beard.

Core Idea
In ghusl, washing both skin and hair is fard; for a thick beard, this differs from wudu.

This lesson examines the obligatory (fard) elements of ghusl from janabah, focusing on the skin and hair of the beard, mustache, eyebrows, and external private parts. The author clarifies the Hanafi position with Quranic and Prophetic evidence, addressing intra-madhhab differences and the distinction from wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligatory parts
List the specific body parts mentioned: skin and hair of the beard, mustache, eyebrows, and external private parts. Note that the internal private parts are excluded.
These are all fard in ghusl from janabah.
2
Understand the proof for hair
Examine the Quranic verse 'fa-tṭahharū' (purify yourselves) and the hadith 'ballū al-sha‘r' (wet the hair) as evidence that water must reach the hair, not just the skin.
The imperative indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
3
Distinguish wudu from ghusl for thick beard
In wudu, only the apparent hair of a thick beard needs washing because the inner skin is not exposed. In ghusl, both skin and hair must be washed because the command is absolute and there is no hardship in ghusl to reach the skin.
This is a key difference many students overlook.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi difference regarding braids
Consider the narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad that women should wet their braids three times with squeezing. The preferred view is that if there is hardship, simply pouring water over the head suffices, provided water reaches the roots.
Hardship (ḥaraj) is grounds for leniency.
5
Apply the ruling
Conclude that for all these parts, water must be delivered. For braided hair, undoing is not required unless water cannot reach the roots. The ruling is fard 'ayn for every Muslim in ghusl.
The cost of water for a woman's ghusl is on the husband if needed due to intercourse.

Source Text

وبَشَرَةِ اللحية، وبَشَرَةِ الشارب، والحاجب، والفرج الخارج.
شعر الرجل، فإنه يفترض إيصال الماء إليه، هو الصحيح، قاله في شرح «المنية» عملاً بمقتضى المبالغة، في الآية مع عدم الضرورة، وهو احتراز أيضاً عن قول بعضهم يجب بلها، لقولـه عليه الصلاة والسلام: «فبلوا الشعر». وعما روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة: أنها تبل ذوائبها ثلاثاً مع كل بلة عصرة؛ ليبلغ الماء شعب قرونها، وعما في صلاة البقالي الصحيح أنه يجب غسل الذوائب، وإن جاوزت القدمين، لأن حديث أم سلمة صريح في عدم النقض فقط، وهذا، أي: قوله: «فبلوا الشعر» ناطق ببلها، مع عدم لحوق الحرج فيه، ولهذا وجب غسل المنقوض من شعرها؛ لعدم الحرج في إيصال الماء إلى أثنائه كاللحية، ولأنه من بدنها، نظراً إلى أصوله، قلنا: قوله: «إنما يكفيك أن تحثي على رأسك...» صريح في عدم بل الذوائب، لأنها ليست على الرأس، حتى لا يصح مسحها عن فرض الممسوح من الرأس، فإن قيل: قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاطّهَرُوا﴾ يتناول الجميع، قلنا: يتناول جميع البدن، والشعر ليس من البدن من كل وجه، بل هو متصل به، نظراً إلى أصوله، ومنفصل عنه، نظراً إلى أطرافه، فعملنا بأصله في حق من لا يلحقه الحرج، وبطرفه في حق من يلحقه الحرج، والضفيرة بالضاد المعجمة الذؤابة، وهي: الخصلة من الشعر، والصَّفْر : فتل الشعر وإدخال بعضه في بعض، ولا يقال: بالظاء المشالة. تنبيه: ثمن ماء غسل المرأة، ووضوئها على الزوج، وإن كانت غنية، كماء الشرب، لأنه مما لا بد منه مطلقاً، وبعضهم قال: إذا كان انقطاع الحيض لأقل من عشرة، فعلى الزوج، لاحتياجه إلى وطئها بعد الغسل، وإن كان لعشرة، فعليها، لأنها هي المحتاجة للصلاة، (وَ) يفترض غسل (بَشَرَةِ اللحية وشعرها، ولو كانت كثيفة كثة، نص عليه، لئلا يتوهم أن حكمها حكم الوضوء، والفرق أن اللحية الكثيفة تحصل المواجهة بظاهرها لا بباطنها، فلا يكلف في الوضوء لغسل غير ظاهرها، وأما في الاغتسال من الجنابة فهو فرض، لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاطّهَرُوا﴾ [المائدة: 6] ولحديث أم سلمة المتقدم، (و) كذا (بَشَرَةِ الشارب)، (وَ) بشرة (الحاجب)، وشعرهما، (والفَرْجِ الخارج) لا الداخل، لما قدمناه.
And the skin of the beard, and the skin of the mustache, and the eyebrow, and the external private part. The hair of the man, for it is obligatory to deliver water to it, that is correct, stated in Sharh al-Munya, acting according to the implication of exaggeration in the verse without necessity, and it is also a precaution against the saying of some that it is obligatory to wet it, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Wet the hair.' And against what al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: that she wets her braids three times, squeezing each time, so that water reaches the roots of her hair; and against what is in Salat al-Baqqali that the correct view is that the braids must be washed, even if they exceed the feet, because the hadith of Umm Salamah is explicit about not untying only; and this, meaning his statement: 'Wet the hair,' speaks of wetting it, without hardship in that, and for this reason, washing the undone part of her hair became obligatory, because there is no hardship in delivering water to its interstices like the beard, and because it is from her body, considering its roots. We said: his statement: 'It suffices you to pour (water) on your head...' is explicit about not wetting the braids, because they are not on the head, so that wiping them would not be valid for the obligation of wiping the head. If it is said: The Almighty's statement: 'Purify yourselves' includes all, we say: It includes all of the body, and hair is not from the body in every respect, but rather it is connected to it, considering its roots, and separated from it, considering its ends; so we act according to its origin for the one who does not suffer hardship, and according to its ends for the one who suffers hardship. And 'al-dufa'irah' (with the dotted dad) means the braid, and it is the lock of hair; and 'al-safr' is twisting the hair and inserting some into some; it is not said with the dotted za. Note: The cost of water for a woman's ghusl and wudu is upon the husband, even if she is rich, like drinking water, because it is absolutely necessary. And some said: If the cessation of menstruation occurs before ten days, it is upon the husband, due to his need to have intercourse with her after the ghusl; if it occurs after ten days, it is upon her, because she is the one who needs prayer. And it is obligatory to wash the skin of the beard and its hair, even if it is thick and dense, it is explicitly stated, lest it be thought that its ruling is the same as wudu. The difference is that the thick beard achieves facing with its apparent part, not its interior, so one is not charged in wudu with washing other than its apparent part. But in ghusl from janabah, it is an obligation, due to the Almighty's statement: 'Purify yourselves' [Al-Ma'idah: 6] and the hadith of Umm Salamah mentioned earlier. And similarly the skin of the mustache, and the skin of the eyebrow, and their hair, and the external private part, not the internal, as we have mentioned earlier.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on Nur al-Idah, explaining the obligatory (fard) parts to wash in ghusl from janabah. The author begins by affirming that the skin and hair of the beard, mustache, eyebrows, and external private parts must be washed. He then addresses the correct view regarding hair: it is obligatory to deliver water to the hair, contrary to some who say only wetting is required. He cites the hadith 'Wet the hair' and discusses a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa that a woman should wet her braids three times with squeezing to ensure water reaches the roots. However, the correct position is that washing braids is obligatory only when there is no hardship; otherwise, it is sufficient to pour water over the head. The text clarifies that the command in the Quran 'Purify yourselves' applies to the whole body, but hair is considered part of the body at its roots and separate at its ends, so hardship is considered. The author then explains the difference between wudu and ghusl regarding the beard: in wudu, washing the apparent part suffices because the thick beard prevents water from reaching the skin underneath, but in ghusl, it is obligatory to wash both the skin and hair because the command is absolute. The passage concludes with a note that the cost of water for a woman's ghusl and wudu is the husband's responsibility, with a nuance regarding the timing of menstruation cessation. This is a complete legal unit covering the fard aspects of washing hair, beard, mustache, eyebrows, and private parts in ghusl.

Key Terms
بَشَرَة (bisharah): The skin, as opposed to hair; here it refers to the skin underlying the beard, mustache, etc.
الذوائب (al-dhawāʼib): Braids or locks of hair, specifically the braided hair of women hanging down.
الضفيرة (al-ḍufayrah): A braid or lock of hair; synonymous with الذؤابة.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on washing the skin and hair of a thick beard in ghusl from janabah in the Hanafi school?
A) It is sunnah to wash both skin and hair.
B) It is obligatory (fard) to wash both skin and hair.
C) It is sufficient to wash the apparent hair only, like in wudu.
D) It is obligatory to wash the skin only, not the hair.

Key Takeaway
In ghusl, it is fard to wash both the skin and hair of the beard, mustache, eyebrows, and external private parts; for braided hair, pouring water over the head suffices if hardship exists.

The Twelve Sunnahs of Ghusl
Lists and explains the twelve sunan of ghusl with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the twelve sunan of ghusl from janabah and explain the basis for each in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The twelve sunan of ghusl elevate the act from mere cleaning to worship, but their omission does not invalidate the ghusl.

Ghusl from janabah is an obligatory act, but the Prophet ﷺ taught us a complete way to perform it that maximizes reward. In this passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah, the author enumerates twelve recommended acts (sunan) that transform ghusl into a supererogatory act of devotion. These include beginning with tasmiyah and intention, washing hands, removing impurity, and performing wudu, with a special ruling about delaying the feet. Let's unpack each sunnah and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling level
Recognize that the twelve acts are sunnah (recommended), not fard (obligatory). Their omission does not invalidate ghusl but reduces reward.
The hukm is 'sunnah' based on the text's opening 'yusannu'.
2
List the twelve sunan in order
From the text, enumerate the acts sequentially: tasmiyah, niyyah, washing hands to wrists, washing impurity separately, washing private part, performing wudu (including thrice washing and wiping head), and delaying washing the feet if water collects.
Memorize the list; it is the core of the lesson.
3
Understand the rationale for each
For each sunnah, explain why it is recommended based on the commentary: e.g., tasmiyah follows the general hadith, intention makes it an act of worship, washing hands is a prophetic practice, etc.
Focus on the commentary's explanations in the passage.
4
Note the exception of delaying feet
Understand that the delay is conditional on standing in a place where water collects. If water does not collect, delay is not needed. This is based on the hadith of Maimunah.
The condition is 'if he stands where water collects'.
5
Appreciate the intra-Hanafi difference about wiping head
The text mentions a difference: some say not to wipe the head during wudu in ghusl, but the correct (mufta bihi) view is to wipe, based on the Prophet's practice.
This shows that even within the school, there can be minor differences resolved by stronger evidence.

فصل في سنن الاغتسال
يُسَنُ في الاغتسال اثنا عَشَرَ شَيئاً: الابتداء بالتسمية، والنِّيَّة، وغسل اليدين إلى الرسغين، وغسل نجاسة، لو كانَتْ بانفرادها وغسلُ فَرْجِهِ، ثمّ يتوضأ كوضوئه للصَّلاةِ، فيثلث الغسل، ويمسح الرأس، ولكنّه يُؤَخِّرُ غَسَلَ الرجلين؛ إنْ كانَ يقف في محل يجتمع فيه الماء..
[شرح:] (يُسَنُ في الاغتسال اثنا عَشَرَ شيئاً :) منها: (الابتداء بالتسمية)، لعموم الحديث «كل أمر ذي بال»، (وَ) الابتداء بـ ( النِّيَّةُ)؛ ليكون فعله قربة يثاب عليها كالوضوء. (و) يسـن في الابتداء (غَسْلُ اليَدين إلى الرُّسْغَين)، لفعله صلى الله عليه وسلم. (وَ) يسن (غَسْلُ نَجَاسَة لَوْ كانَتْ على بدنه) (بانْفِرَادِهَا)، ليقلل في الماء، ويطمئن بزوالها، قبل أن تشيع على الجسد. (وَغَسْلُ فَرْجه) وإن لم یکن به نجاسة كما فعله النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم. وذلك ليطمئن بوصول الماء إلى الجزء الذي ينضم من الفرج حال القيام، وينفرج حال الجلوس ( ثم يتوضأ كوضوئه للصَّلاةِ، فيثلث الغسل، ويمسح الرأس) في ظاهر الرواية. وقيل: لا يمسحها، لأنه يصب عليها الماء، والأول هو الصحيح؛ لأنه صلى الله عليه وسلم «توضأ قبل الاغتسال وضوءه للصَّلاةِ»، وهو اسم للغسل والمسح ( ولكنّه يُؤَخِّرُ غَسْلَ الرَّجْلينِ، إِنْ كَانَ يقف حال الاغتسال (في مَحَلٌّ يَجْتَمِعُ فِيْهِ المَاءُ)؛ لأنه يحتاج إلى غسلهما ثانياً عن غسالته، ولمـا روى الستة عن ابن عباس، قال: حدثتني خالتي ميمونة، قالت: أدنيتُ لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم غسله مِنَ الجَنَابَةِ، فغسل كفّيه مرتين أو ثلاثاً ثمّ أدخل يديه في الإناء، ثم أفرغ على فرجه وغسله بشماله، ثم ضرب بشماله الأرض، فدلكها دلْكاً شديداً، ثمَّ توضأ وضوءه للصلاة، ثمّ أفرغ على رأسه ثلاث حفنات ملء كفيه، ثمّ غسل سائر جسدهِ، ثمّ تنحى عن مقامه ذلك، فغسل رجليه، ثم أتيتُه بالمنديل، فرده. ولكن قال الشيخ أكمل الدين رحمه الله في «العناية»: «قالت: توضأ رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وضوءه للصلاة غير رجلَيْهِ» انتهى. وقال القاضي عياض في شرح مسلم: ليس فيه، أي: في حديث ميمونة ذكر غسل الرجلين. (١) تقدم تخريجه ص (۱۷). (٣) أيضاً انظر حديث ميمونة الآتي. (۲) انظر حديث ميمونة الآتي. (٤) انظر حديث ابن عباس له الآتي. (٥) أخرجه البخاري في الطهارة باب المضمضة والاستنشاق من الجنابة (٢٥٩)، ومسلم في صفة غسل الجنابة (۳۱۷)، واللفظ له. (٦) أخرجه البخاري في الغسل باب الوضوء قبل الغسل (٢٤٩)، والنسائي في الغسل، باب: إزالة الجنب الأذى عنه (٤١٦).
Chapter on the Sunnahs of Ghusl
Twelve things are recommended in ghusl: beginning with tasmiyah (Bismillah), intention, washing the hands up to the wrists, washing any impurity if it is on the body separately, washing his private part, then performing wudu like his wudu for prayer, washing thrice and wiping the head, but he delays washing the feet if he is standing in a place where water collects.
[Commentary:] (Twelve things are recommended in ghusl:) Among them: (beginning with tasmiyah), due to the general hadith 'Every matter of importance that does not begin with Bismillah is cut off,' (and) beginning with (intention); so that his action becomes an act of worship for which he is rewarded, like wudu. (And) it is recommended to begin with (washing the hands up to the wrists), because the Prophet did so. (And) it is recommended (to wash any impurity if it is on his body) (separately), to reduce [use of] water and to be certain of its removal before it spreads over the body. (And washing his private part) even if there is no impurity on it, as the Prophet did. This is to be certain of water reaching the part that contracts while standing and expands while sitting. (Then he performs wudu like his wudu for prayer, washing thrice, and wiping the head) according to the apparent narration. It was also said that he does not wipe it because he pours water over it, but the first is correct because the Prophet performed wudu before ghusl like his wudu for prayer, and wudu includes washing and wiping. (But he delays washing the feet, if he is standing during ghusl in a place where water collects), because he needs to wash them a second time from the water that has collected, and because of the hadith narrated by the Six from Ibn Abbas who said: My aunt Maimunah told me: I brought the Prophet water for his ghusl from janabah, so he washed his hands twice or thrice, then inserted his hands into the vessel, then poured water over his private part and washed it with his left hand, then struck his left hand on the ground and rubbed it hard, then performed wudu like his wudu for prayer, then poured three handfuls of water over his head, then washed the rest of his body, then moved from that place and washed his feet, then I brought him a towel, and he returned it. But Shaykh Akmal al-Din said in al-`Inayah: She said: The Prophet performed wudu like his wudu for prayer except for his feet. The end. And Qadi `Iyad said in Sharh Muslim: There is no mention of washing the feet in the hadith of Maimunah. (1) Its takhrij preceded on p.17. (3) Also see the hadith of Maimunah below. (2) See the hadith of Maimunah below. (4) See the hadith of Ibn Abbas below. (5) Bukhari in Taharah, Chapter: Rinsing mouth and nose from janabah (259), Muslim in Description of Ghusl Janabah (317), wording is his. (6) Bukhari in Ghusl, Chapter: Wudu before ghusl (249), Nasa'i in Ghusl, Chapter: Removal of impurity from the junub (416).
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a legal statement enumerating the twelve recommended acts (sunan) of ghusl from janabah, taken from the commentary on Nur al-Idah. The author first lists them: 1) beginning with tasmiyah, 2) intention, 3) washing hands up to wrists, 4) washing any impurity on the body separately, 5) washing the private part, 6-11) performing wudu-like actions (including gargling, rinsing nose, washing each limb thrice, wiping the head), and 12) delaying washing the feet if water collects where one stands. The commentary then explains each: tasmiyah is based on the general hadith that every important matter must begin with 'Bismillah'; intention makes the act an act of worship; washing hands is a prophetic practice; washing impurity separately reduces water usage and ensures removal; washing the private part follows the Sunnah even in the absence of impurity. Regarding wudu, the author notes a difference: in the apparent narration, one performs full wudu including wiping the head, though some say not to wipe because water is poured; the correct view is to wipe, as the Prophet did. The delay of washing feet is proven by the hadith of Maimunah, where the Prophet washed his feet after moving from his place. However, Shaykh Akmal al-Din interprets the hadith to mean he delayed washing the feet, and Qadi 'Iyad noted that Maimunah's narration does not explicitly mention washing the feet in the initial wudu. The passage concludes with hadith references. This is a complete list of sunan, with practical details.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Saying بسم الله (Bismillah) at the beginning of ghusl.
النِّيَّة (al-niyyah): Intention to perform ghusl for purification from janabah.
الوضوء (al-wudu): Ablution like for prayer, including washing face, hands, wiping head, and washing feet, though feet are delayed here.

A) To ensure removal of any hidden impurity.
B) To be certain water reaches the part that contracts and expands.
C) Because the Prophet did so, and to gain more reward.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
The twelve sunan of ghusl are recommended acts that complete the purification; omitting them does not invalidate but loses reward.

The Sunnah of Delaying Foot Washing in Ghusl
Explanation of the sunnah to delay washing feet and its evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying foot washing in ghusl and explain the evidence from the hadith of Maimuna.

Core Idea
Delaying foot washing in ghusl is sunnah when standing in water — the Prophet's practice is our guide.

When performing ghusl, one follows a sequence of actions prescribed by the sunnah. One of these is the order of washing. This lesson examines the specific sunnah of delaying the washing of the feet until after the full-body wash, especially when standing in a place where water collects. We'll explore the textual evidence from the hadith of Maimuna and understand the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is delaying the washing of the feet during ghusl when one is standing in a place where water collects. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
The matn explicitly states it is sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the hadith of Maimuna (رضي الله عنها) narrated by Ibn Abbas (رضي الله عنه), recorded by the six major hadith collections.
The hadith describes the Prophet's (ﷺ) ghusl sequence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'then he performed wudu like for prayer' followed by 'then he moved and washed his feet' indicates that the feet were not washed in the initial wudu but delayed until after the full-body wash.
This shows the Prophet (ﷺ) intentionally delayed foot washing.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some later scholars (e.g., author of al-Bahr) consider it obligatory (wajib) when standing in water and having impurity on the body, but the majority view is sunnah.
The disagreement is within the Hanafi school.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that it is sunnah, as stated in Zahir al-Riwayah and supported by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.
The view of obligation is not adopted for fatwa.

فصل في سنن الاغتسال (يُسَنُ في الاغتسال اثنا عَشَرَ شيئاً :) منها: (الابتداء بالتسمية)، لعموم الحديث وكل أمر ذي بال، (وَ) الابتداء بـ ( النِّيَّةُ)؛ ليكون فعله قربة يثاب عليها كالوضوء. (و) يســن في الابتداء (غَسْلُ اليَدين إلى الرُّسْغَين)، لفعله (وَ) يسن (غَسْلُ نَجَاسَة لَوْ كانَتْ على بدنه (بانْفِرَادِهَا)، ليقلل في الماء، ويطمئن بزوالها، قبل أن تشيع على الجسد. (وَغَسْلُ فَرْجه) وإن لم یکن به نجاسة كما فعله النبي. وذلك ليطمئن بوصول الماء إلى الجزء الذي ينضم من الفرج حال القيام، وينفرج حال الجلوس (ثم يتوضأ كوضوئه للصَّلاةِ، فيثلث الغسل، ويمسح الرأس) في ظاهر الرواية. وقيل: لا يمسحها، لأنه يصب عليها الماء، والأول هو الصحيح؛ لأنه صلى الله عليه وسلم « توضأ قبل الاغتسال وضوءه للصَّلاةِ ». وهو اسم للغسل والمسح ( ولكنّه يُؤَخِّرُ غَسْلَ الرَّحِلينِ، إِنْ كَانَ يقف حال الاغتسال (في مَحَلٌّ يَجْتَمِعُ فِيْهِ المَاءُ)؛ لأنه يحتاج إلى غسلهما ثانياً عن غسالته، ولمـا روى الستة عن ابن عباس، قال : ( حَدَّثَتْنِي حَالَتِي مَيْمُونَة، قالت: أدنيتُ لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم غسله مِنَ الجَنَابَةِ، فغسلَ كفّيه مرتين أو ثلاثاً ثمّ أدخل يديه في الإناء، ثم أفرغ على فرجه وغسله بشماله، ثم ضرب بشماله الأرض، فدلكها دلْكَاً شديداً، ثمَّ توضأ وضوءه للصلاة، ثمّ أفرغ على رأسه ثلاث حفنات ملء كفيه، ثمّ غسل سائر جسدهِ، ثمّ تنحى عن مقامه ذلك، فغسل رجليه، ثم أتيتُه بالمنديل، فرده. ولكن قال الشيخ أكمل الدين رحمه الله في ( العناية : « قالَتْ: توضأ رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وضوءه للصلاة غير رجلَيْهِ» انتهى. وقال القاضي عياض في شرح مسلم : ليس فيه، أي: في حديث ميمونة، تصريح، بل هو محتمل لأن قولها توضأ وضوءه للصلاة الأظهر فيه إكمال وضوئه، وقولهـا آخراً: ثم تنحى فغسل رجليه يحتمل أن يكون لما نالهما من تلك البقعة. انتهى. وقال صاحب البحر : فعلى هذا يغسلهما بعد الفراغ من الغسل مطلقاً، سواء غسلهما قبله أولاً، وسواء أصابهما طين أو لا، ثم لا يخفى تعين غسلهما، في حق الواحد منا، بعد الفراغ من الغسل إذا كانتا في مستنقع الماء، وكان على البدن نجاسة، من مني أو غيره، والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم. انتهى.
Chapter on the Sunnahs of Ghusl: Twelve things are sunnah in ghusl: starting with the basmalah, intention, washing hands to the wrists, washing impurity if it is on the body separately, washing the private parts, then performing wudu like for prayer, making the washing threefold and wiping the head according to the apparent narration. It is said he does not wipe it because he pours water on it, but the first is correct because the Prophet performed wudu before ghusl like for prayer. And he delays washing the feet if he is standing in a place where water collects, because he needs to wash them a second time due to the water of the place, and due to what the six narrated from Ibn Abbas who said: My aunt Maimuna told me: I brought the Prophet water for ghusl from janabah. He washed his palms twice or thrice, then put his hand in the vessel, then poured water on his private parts and washed them with his left hand, then struck his left hand on the ground and rubbed it vigorously, then performed wudu like for prayer, then poured three handfuls of water on his head, then washed the rest of his body, then moved from that place and washed his feet. Then I brought him a towel and he refused it. But Shaykh Akmal al-Din said in al-`Inayah: 'She said: The Prophet performed wudu like for prayer except for his feet.' Qadi `Iyad said in his commentary on Muslim: There is no explicit statement in the hadith of Maimuna; rather it is probable that her saying 'he performed wudu like for prayer' apparently indicates completing his wudu, and her saying later 'then he moved and washed his feet' may be because of the mud from that place. The author of al-Bahr said: According to this, he washes them after finishing ghusl unconditionally, whether he washed them before or not, and whether mud got on them or not. Then it is obvious that it is obligatory for one of us to wash them after finishing ghusl if they are in a pool of water and there is impurity on the body, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is an expansion of the matn from Nur al-Idah on the sunan of ghusl. It begins by listing the twelve sunnah acts, focusing on those that precede the main washing. The commentator emphasizes the importance of intention (niyyah), washing hands and private parts, and then performing a complete wudu before the full-body wash. A significant point of discussion is whether to wash the feet during this wudu or delay them. The matn states that it is sunnah to delay washing the feet if one stands in water, because the feet will get dirty again. The sharh supports this with the hadith of Maimuna, where the Prophet performed wudu but then after finishing the full-body ghusl, he moved to a dry place and washed his feet. However, there is an ambiguity: did he complete the wudu including the feet or not? The commentary reconciles by noting the possibility that the Prophet’s feet were not washed initially because of the muddy place, but later washed them after moving. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that if one stands in a place where water collects, it is recommended to delay washing the feet until after the ghusl, and then wash them separately. This ruling is based on the practice of the Prophet and avoids the need to rewash them.

Key Terms
سنن الاغتسال (sunan al-ightisal): Recommended acts in the ritual bath (ghusl) that are not obligatory but rewardable.
تثليث الغسل (tathlith al-ghusl): Washing each limb three times in ghusl as a sunnah practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is it sunnah to delay washing the feet during ghusl?
A) When one intends to perform wudu later
B) When one is standing in a place where water collects
C) When one has no impurity on the feet
D) When one uses a towel to dry the body

Key Takeaway
Delaying foot washing in ghusl when standing in water is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) based on the practice of the Prophet, not an obligation.

The Ruling on Using a Towel After Ghusl
Discussion of the ruling on using a towel after ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using a towel after ghusl and explain the evidence and scholarly differences.

Core Idea
Using a towel after ghusl is permissible but not recommended; the Prophet's refusal was situational.

In this passage, the commentator explores the ruling on drying oneself with a towel after ghusl. While some hadiths suggest the Prophet once refused a towel, other reports indicate he used a cloth for drying. By examining the context and weighing the evidence, the Hanafi school arrives at a clear position: it is neither recommended nor disliked, but simply permissible. Let's walk through the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the legal classification (hukm) of using a towel after ghusl or wudu? Look for the conclusion: the commentary states it is not forbidden, not recommended, but permissible (mubah).
The mufta bihi is that it is not disliked.
2
Locate the key evidence
Two sets of evidence are discussed: the hadith of Maimuna where the Prophet refused a towel, and the hadith of Aisha that he used a cloth for drying after wudu. The commentary interprets each.
The weak hadith of Aisha is used to support permissibility in virtuous deeds.
3
Analyze the interpretation of evidence
Why does the Hanafi school not take the refusal as a general prohibition? The commentator cites al-Qadi who says the refusal was due to a specific circumstance (hurry, humility), not a general ruling.
Understanding context is key in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is disagreement among scholars: some early Hanafis considered it disliked (makruh), and Shafi'is recommend not drying (istihbab). The Hanafi response addresses these views.
Al-Nawawi's statement on istihbab is acknowledged but not adopted.
5
Apply the tarjih
The author of al-Bahr and others follow Abu Hanifa's view that it is permissible. The weaker view of karahah is set aside, and the mufta bihi is that there is no harm in using a towel.
The commentary concludes that it is not disliked, but one should not exaggerate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكن قال الشيخ أكمل الدين رحمه الله في ( العناية : « قالَتْ: توضأ رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وضوءه للصلاة غير رجلَيْهِ» انتهى. وقال القاضي عياض في شرح مسلم : ليس فيه، أي: في حديث ميمونة، تصريح، بل هو محتمل لأن قولها توضأ وضوءه للصلاة الأظهر فيه إكمال وضوئه، وقولهـا آخراً: ثم تنحى فغسل رجليه يحتمل أن يكون لما نالهما من تلك البقعة. انتهى. وقال صاحب البحر : فعلى هذا يغسلهما بعد الفراغ من الغسل مطلقاً، سواء غسلهما قبله أولاً، وسواء أصابهما طين أو لا، ثم لا يخفى تعين غسلهما، في حق الواحد منا، بعد الفراغ من الغسل إذا كانتا في مستنقع الماء، وكان على البدن نجاسة، من مني أو غيره، والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم. انتهى. وقال النووي رحمه الله في رده صلى الله عليه وسلم المنديل: استحباب ترك تنشيف الأعضاء، وقال الإمام: لا خلاف في أنه لا يحرم تنشيف الماء عن الأعضاء، ولا يستحب، ولكن هل يكره؟ فيه خلاف بين الصحابة. وقال القاضي: يحتمل رده للمنديل لشيء رآه، أو لاستعجاله في الصلاة، أو تواضعــا وخـلافـاً لـعـادة أهل الترفه، ويكون الحديث الآخر في ( أنَّه كانت له خرقة يتنشف بهَا ) عند الضرورة وشدة البرد، لیزیل برد الماء عن أعضائه. انتهى. والمنقول في «معراج الدراية» وغيرها، أنه لا بأس بالتمسح بالمنديل للمتوضى، والمغتسل، إلا أنه ينبغي أن لا يبالغ ويستقصي فيبقى أثـر الوضوء علـى أعضائه، ولم نر من صرح باستحبابه إلا صاحب « منية المصلي»، فقال: ويستحب أن يمسح بمنديل بعد الغسل. انتهى. واستدل له شارح المنية الحلبي، بما روته عائشة : « قالت: كان للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم خرقة يتنشف بها بعد الوضوء ) رواه الترمذي، وهو ضعيف. ولكن يجوز العمل بالضعيف في الفضائل. انتهى. ولا يخفى أن المدعى التنشيف بعد الغسل، والمروي في الوضوء.
But Shaykh Akmal al-Din said in al-`Inayah: 'She said: The Prophet performed wudu like for prayer except for his feet.' Qadi `Iyad said in his commentary on Muslim: There is no explicit statement in the hadith of Maimuna; rather it is probable that her saying 'he performed wudu like for prayer' apparently indicates completing his wudu, and her saying later 'then he moved and washed his feet' may be because of the mud from that place. The author of al-Bahr said: According to this, he washes them after finishing ghusl unconditionally, whether he washed them before or not, and whether mud got on them or not. Then it is obvious that it is obligatory for one of us to wash them after finishing ghusl if they are in a pool of water and there is impurity on the body, and Allah knows best. And al-Nawawi said regarding his refusal of the towel: It is recommended to leave drying the limbs, and Imam said: There is no disagreement that drying water from the limbs is not forbidden and not recommended, but is it disliked? There is a difference among the Companions. Al-Qadi said: It is possible that he refused the towel due to something he saw, or because he was in a hurry for prayer, or out of humility and opposition to the habit of the luxurious, and the other hadith that 'he had a cloth to dry himself with' is for necessity and severe cold to remove the cold of water from his limbs. What is transmitted in `Ma`arij al-Dirayah' and others is that there is no harm in wiping with a towel for the one performing wudu or ghusl, but one should not exaggerate and overdo it so that the effect of wudu remains on his limbs. We have not seen anyone who explicitly recommended it except the author of `Munyat al-Musalli', who said: It is recommended to wipe with a towel after ghusl. The commentator al-Halabi argued for this with what `A'isha narrated: 'The Prophet had a cloth with which he dried himself after wudu.' It was narrated by al-Tirmidhi, but it is weak. However, it is permissible to use weak hadith for virtuous deeds. And it is obvious that the claim is about drying after ghusl, while what is narrated is about wudu.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the issue of using a towel (mandil) after ghusl. The commentator builds on the earlier discussion of the hadith of Maimuna, where the Prophet refused a towel. By quoting various scholars, the commentary clarifies the Hanafi stance. The general view is that drying oneself after wudu or ghusl is permissible but not recommended (khilaf al-awla). Some scholars consider it disliked (makruh), while others say it is neutral. The hadith of the Prophet refusing a towel is interpreted as specific to him, possibly due to humility or haste. The hadith that he used a cloth for drying is considered weak, but may be acted upon for supererogatory acts. The Hanafi position is that one may use a towel without blame, but it is better not to if one can avoid it, especially to preserve the effect of water on the limbs as a sign of worship. The commentary thus balances the conflicting evidence and settles on permissibility without recommendation.

Key Terms
المنديل (al-mandil): A cloth or towel used to dry the body after washing.
تنشيف (tanshif): Drying the limbs after wudu or ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in the text, what is the ruling on using a towel after ghusl?
A) It is recommended (mustahabb)
B) It is disliked (makruh)
C) It is permissible (mubah) but not recommended
D) It is forbidden (haram)

Key Takeaway
Using a towel after ghusl or wudu is permissible (mubah) according to the Hanafi school, and it is not disliked despite the Prophet's refusal on a specific occasion.

Pouring Water Three Times and Immersion in Ghusl
Explanation of sunnah of three pourings and immersion alternative

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sunnah of pouring water three times in ghusl and explain how immersion fulfills it.

Core Idea
Three pourings in ghusl are sunnah; immersion with sufficient duration achieves the same thoroughness.

This passage explains the sunnah of pouring water three times in ghusl and clarifies that immersion in flowing water can fulfill this sunnah if one remains submerged long enough. The ruling is based on the hadith of Maimuna and the principle of mubalaghah (thoroughness).

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah act
The text states that pouring water three times over the body, covering it completely each time, is sunnah. Recognize that this is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah).
2
Examine the proof
The hadith of Maimuna is cited, where the Prophet poured three handfuls of water on his head. The imams analogized from this to the entire body. Note that the hadith only mentions three pourings on the head, but the principle of thoroughness extends it.
The Arabic key phrase is 'أفرغ على رأسه ثلاث حفنات'.
3
Understand the expansion
The commentary explains that because Maimuna mentioned three pourings on the head and then said 'then he washed the rest of his body,' it is inferred that the three pourings applied to the whole body by analogy (qiyas).
4
Analyze the immersion alternative
The text introduces that immersion in flowing water (or large standing water like ten by ten cubits) for the duration of wudu and ghusl also fulfills the sunnah. The reasoning is that thorough coverage of water is achieved, similar to three pourings.
Flowing water includes rivers; large standing water is considered in its ruling.
5
Apply the ruling
Now you can apply this: a person can choose either method—three separate pourings or a single immersion with sufficient duration—to complete the sunnah of ghusl.
The intention for sunnah is not required to be explicit; the action itself fulfills it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ثُمَّ يُفيضُ المَاءَ عَلَى بَدَنِهِ، ثَلَاثَاً)، يستوعب الجسد بكل واحدة منها، والتثليث سنة، لحديث ميمونة. كذا استدل به الأئمة، وفيه التصريح بأنه أفرغ على رأسه ثلاث حفنات، وليس فيه التصريح بفعله ثلاثاً بعده في سائر جسده، لقولها ثم غسل سائر جسده ثم تنحى، إلا أن يقال: لما ذكرت التثليث في الرأس اكتفت به عن ذكره في باقي الجسد. (وَلُو انْغَمَس) المغتسل (في الماء الجاري، أو) انغمس في (ما) هو (في حُكْمِهِ)، أي: الجاري، كالعشر في العشر، (وَمَكتَ) منغمساً قدر الوضوء والغسل، أو مكث في المطر كذلك، ولو للوضوء فقط، فَقَدْ أكْمَلَ السُّنةَ)، لحصول المبالغة بذلك، كالتثليث.
Then he pours water on his body three times, covering the body completely with each pouring. Making it three times is sunnah due to the hadith of Maimuna. Thus the imams used it as proof, and in it she explicitly says that he poured three handfuls of water on his head, but she does not explicitly say that he did it three times on the rest of his body, because she said: 'then he washed the rest of his body' and then moved away. However, it is said that when she mentioned the three times on the head, that sufficed her from mentioning it for the rest of the body. And if the one performing ghusl immerses himself in flowing water, or in what is like flowing water, such as a large body of water (like ten by ten cubits), and remains submerged for the duration of wudu and ghusl, or remains under rain similarly, even if only for wudu, then he has completed the sunnah, because the thoroughness (mubalaghah) is achieved by that, just like the threefold pouring.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage concludes the section on the sunan of ghusl. It addresses two methods of achieving the sunnah: pouring water three times over the body, and immersion in flowing water. The commentary explains that the threefold pouring is established by the hadith of Maimuna, in which the Prophet poured three handfuls of water on his head, and by analogy (qiyas) the rest of the body is also covered. Some scholars note that the hadith does not explicitly state three pourings on the whole body, but the practice is derived from the head and the general principle of mubalaghah (thoroughness). The second point is that if a person immerses in flowing water (or a large standing body like a reservoir) and stays submerged long enough to perform the actions of wudu and ghusl mentally (e.g., moving hands under water), then the sunnah of three pourings is considered fulfilled because the complete coverage is achieved in a single immersion. This is based on the idea that the purpose of the three pourings—thorough washing—is attained by staying in the water sufficiently. The commentary thus expands on the matn's ruling by providing the rationale and evidence.

Key Terms
إفاضة الماء (ifadatu al-ma'): Pouring water over the body during ghusl.
انغماس (inghimas): Immersion of the entire body in water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how can one complete the sunnah of ghusl through immersion?
A) By immersing briefly and then coming out
B) By immersing and remaining submerged for the duration equivalent to wudu and ghusl
C) By immersing only once without any movement
D) By immersing in any type of water

Key Takeaway
The sunnah of three pourings in ghusl can be fulfilled either by pouring water three times or by immersing in flowing water for a sufficient duration, as both achieve thorough washing.

Sunnahs of Ghusl: Pouring Thrice and Immersion
Explaining the sunnah of thrice pouring, immersion as equivalent, and the permissibility of drying with a towel.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the sunnah of pouring water thrice in ghusl, state how immersion fulfills it, and identify the Hanafi position on drying with a towel after ghusl.

Core Idea
Pouring water thrice and full immersion both fulfill the sunnah of thoroughness in ghusl; using a towel is permissible but not recommended.

Ghusl, like wudu, has sunnan (recommended acts) that enhance its perfection. This lesson explores two key sunnan: pouring water thrice over the body and complete immersion, which the Hanafi school considers equivalent in achieving thoroughness. The passage also addresses a practical question—whether drying with a towel is permissible, recommended, or disliked—clarifying the nuanced Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (pouring thrice, immersion, drying with towel) and the hukm level (sunnah muakkadah, permissible, etc.).
The passage states 'al-tathlith sunnah' and immersion 'aqd akmal al-sunnah'.
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the proof cited—the hadith of Maymunah—and note its content about the Prophet pouring three handfuls on his head.
The text says 'bi-hadith Maymunah'.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the sunnah: the explicit action on the head is extended to the whole body by analogy, and the command implies sunnah not obligation.
The commentators infer that the threefold was done for the whole body.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf on Drying with a Towel
Examine the different views: some Companions disliked it, al-Nawawi recommended leaving it, the author of Munyat al-Musalli considered it recommended after ghusl.
The Hanafi majority position is permissibility without dislike.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
Determine the mufta bihi: pouring thrice and immersion are sunnah muakkadah; using a towel is permissible (mubah) and not disliked, but leaving it is better.
Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and others uphold this view.

(ثُمَّ يُفيضُ المَاءَ عَلَى بَدَنِهِ، ثَلَاثَاً)، يستوعب الجسد بكل واحدة منها، والتثليث سنة، لحديث ميمونة (۳). كذا استدل به الأئمة، وفيه التصريح بأنه و أفرغ على رأسه ثلاث حفنات، وليس فيه التصريح بفعـلـه ثلاثـاً بـعـده في سائر جسده، لقولها ثم غسل سائر جسده ثم تنحى، إلا أن يقال: لما ذكرت التثليث في الرأس اكتفت به عن ذكره في باقي الجسد. And the author of al-Bahr said: accordingly, he washes them after finishing the ghusl absolutely, whether he washed them before or not, and whether mud touched them or not, then it is not hidden that washing them is determined, for each of us, after finishing the ghusl if they are in a pool of water and there is impurity on the body, from semen or other, and Allah knows best. And al-Nawawi said regarding his rejection of the towel: it is recommended to leave drying the limbs, and Imam said: there is no dispute that drying water from the limbs is not prohibited, nor recommended, but is it disliked? There is dispute among the Companions. And al-Qadi said: it is possible his rejection of the towel was for something he saw, or for his haste in prayer, or humility and opposition to the habit of the luxurious, and the other hadith that 'he had a cloth with which he dried himself' (1) out of necessity and severe cold, to remove the cold of water from his limbs. End. And it is transmitted in 'Miraj al-Dirayah' and others that there is no harm in wiping with a towel for the one performing wudu and the one performing ghusl, except that he should not exaggerate and be thorough so that the trace of wudu remains on his limbs, and we have not seen anyone explicitly deeming it recommended except the author of 'Munyat al-Musalli', who said: it is recommended to wipe with a towel after ghusl. End. And the commentator of Munyat al-Halabi argued for it with what Aisha narrated: 'The Prophet had a cloth with which he dried himself after wudu' (2) narrated by al-Tirmidhi, and it is weak, but it is permissible to act on weak hadith in virtues. End. And it is not hidden that the claim is drying after ghusl, while what is narrated is about wudu. (Then he pours water over his body, three times), covering the body with each one, and making it three is sunnah, due to the hadith of Maymunah (3). Thus the imams argued with it, and in it is the explicit mention that he poured three handfuls on his head, but not explicit that he did it three times thereafter over the rest of his body, because of her statement 'then he washed the rest of his body, then moved aside', unless it is said: since she mentioned the threefold on the head, she sufficed with that over mentioning it for the rest of the body. (And if the person performing ghusl immerses himself in running water, or immerses in what is in its ruling, i.e., running, like ten in ten, and remains immersed for the duration of wudu and ghusl, or remains in rain likewise, even if only for wudu, then he has completed the sunnah), because that achieves thoroughness, like the threefold.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the hadith of Maymunah, covering the sunnah of pouring water thrice and the ruling on immersion. The author begins by reiterating the matn: the person performing ghusl pours water over his body three times, and if he immerses in running or standing water and remains long enough, he completes the sunnah. The commentary then discusses a detail from Maymunah's hadith about washing the feet, citing al-Bahr's ruling that the feet must be washed after ghusl if they were in the pool and impurity was on the body. There follows a discussion on the use of a towel (mandil) to dry after ghusl. Al-Nawawi is quoted as saying it is recommended to leave drying, but there is disagreement among the Companions about dislike. The majority view is that it is permissible but not recommended, while the author of Munyat al-Musalli considered it recommended after ghusl based on a weak hadith, which is acceptable for virtues. The passage then returns to the main commentary, explaining that pouring thrice is sunnah based on the hadith of Maymunah, even though the hadith only explicitly mentions three handfuls on the head; the majority infer the same for the rest of the body. Immersion in water, whether running or still, suffices if one remains long enough, as it achieves the same thoroughness as pouring thrice.

Key Terms
تثليث (tathlith): Performing an action three times; here, pouring water thrice in ghusl.
منديل (mandil): A towel or cloth used to dry oneself after wudu or ghusl.
انغماس (in ghamas): Immersion of the entire body in water.

Key Takeaway

Sunnahs of Ghusl: Order and Rubbing
Explaining the sunnah of beginning with the head, then shoulders, and rubbing the body

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts of ghusl (order and rubbing) and explain why rubbing is not wajib in the Hanafi school except in one narration.

Core Idea
Rubbing (dalk) is sunnah in ghusl except in an Abu Yusuf narration; order starts with head then right shoulder.

This passage outlines the recommended acts (sunan) of ghusl, focusing on the sequence of washing and the practice of rubbing the body. While washing the entire body is fard, the Prophet ﷺ taught a preferred method: starting with the head, then the right shoulder, then left, and gently rubbing to ensure thorough coverage. The Hanafi school generally holds rubbing as sunnah, but a minority view from Abu Yusuf considers it obligatory based on the Quranic command 'fatahharu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
The act is ghusl; the sunnah acts mentioned are order (head, right shoulder, left) and rubbing.
2
Locate the evidence for order
The author cites a narration for starting with the head and the principle of tayamun (starting with right) for shoulder order.
3
Analyze the ruling on rubbing
The text states dalk is sunnah except in a narration from Abu Yusuf who argued from Quran 5:6 'fatahharu'.
4
Compare with wudu
In wudu, the word 'ighsilu' is used, so rubbing is not considered wajib by any Hanafi.
5
Note the consequence of omission
If a sunnah act is omitted, ghusl is still valid but reward diminished; if rubbing were wajib (Abu Yusuf view), compensation would be needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبتدئ في صب الماء برأسه، ويغسلُ بعدها مَنْكِبَهُ الأيمن، ثمّ الأَيْسَرَ وَيَدْلُكُ جَسَدَهُ، وَيُوَالِي غَسَلَهُ. ( ويبتدئ في ) حال (صَبَ المَاءِ بِرَأْسِهِ ، لما روينا ) ، (وَيَغْسِلُ بَعْدَهَا) أي: الرأس (مَنْكِبَهُ الأيمن، ثمّ الأَيْسَرَ)، لاستحباب التيامن، وهو قول شمس الأئمة ( الحلواني»، (وَ) يسن أن (يَدْلُكُ) كل أعضاء (جسَدَهُ) في المرة الأولى، ليعم الماء البدن في المرتين الأخيرتين، وليس الدلك بواجب في الغسل، إلا في رواية عن أبي يوسف لخصوص صيغة ﴿فَاطَهَرُوا اللة : ٦] فيه، بخلاف الوضوء، فإنه بلفظ اغسلوا. ولما فرغ من بيان سنن الغسل شرع في بيان آدابه، فقال:
And he begins pouring water on his head, and washes after it his right shoulder, then the left, and rubs his body, and maintains continuity in his washing. (And he begins in) the state of pouring water on his head, as we have narrated, (and he washes after it) i.e., the head (his right shoulder, then the left), due to the recommendation of starting with the right, and it is the statement of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, (and) it is sunnah that he rubs all limbs of his body in the first time, so that water covers the body in the last two times, and rubbing is not obligatory in ghusl, except in one narration from Abu Yusuf due to the specific wording of {so purify yourselves} [5:6] therein, unlike wudu, for it is with the word 'wash'. And when he finished explaining the sunnahs of ghusl, he began explaining its etiquettes, saying:
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the sunan (recommended acts) of ghusl. The author details the preferred order: begin by pouring water on the head, then wash the right shoulder, then the left. This is based on the general principle of starting with the right side (tayamun), as mentioned by Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani. Then one should rub (dalk) the entire body during the first pouring so that water reaches all parts, facilitating coverage in subsequent pourings. Dalk is not obligatory in ghusl, except in a narration from Abu Yusuf who considered it wajib due to the Quranic word 'fattahharu' (so purify yourselves) implying thoroughness. In wudu, the word is 'ighsilu' (wash), so rubbing is not required. The passage concludes with a transition to the next topic: the adab (etiquette) of ghusl.

Key Terms
مَنْكِب (mankib): Shoulder; the area from the base of the neck to the upper arm.
دلك (dalk): Rubbing the body with the hand while washing to ensure water covers the skin.
تيامن (tayamun): Starting with the right side when performing actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) It is haram because it wastes water.
D) It is only for wudu, not ghusl.

Key Takeaway
Rubbing (dalk) in ghusl is sunnah, not wajib, except in one narration from Abu Yusuf; the sunnah order is head, right shoulder, then left.

Sunan of Ghusl: Order and Ruling on Rubbing
Explanation of the sunan of ghusl with a note on rubbing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sunan of ghusl according to the Hanafi school and explain the ruling on rubbing (dalk), including the intra-madhhab difference.

Core Idea
Rubbing the body in ghusl is sunnah, not obligatory, except in a narration from Abu Yusuf.

In this lesson, we examine the recommended acts (sunan) of ghusl as outlined in Nur al-Idah with the commentary of Imdad al-Fattah. The passage details the order of washing and specifically addresses the ruling on rubbing (dalk), highlighting an important intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunan listed
Read the passage and list the specific recommended acts: beginning with the head, then right shoulder, then left shoulder, rubbing the body, and performing them consecutively.
The term 'sunan' here refers to acts that are recommended but not obligatory.
2
Understand the proof for the order
The passage references a hadith (later cited as hadith of Maimunah) and the principle of tayammun (starting with the right) to justify the order.
The hadith provides the direct evidence for these sunan.
3
Analyze the ruling on rubbing (dalk)
The text explicitly states that rubbing is not wajib, except in a narration from Abu Yusuf. Understand the reasoning: the Quranic word 'fattaheru' (purify) in Surah al-Muddaththir is used for ghusl, while 'ighsilu' (wash) is used for wudu, implying that rubbing is not a necessary component in ghusl.
Abu Yusuf's view is based on a specific interpretation of 'fattaheru' as meaning 'rub'.
4
Distinguish from wudu
Note the contrast: in wudu, rubbing is also considered sunnah by many, but the passage highlights that the Quranic wording for wudu is 'ighsilu', which does not imply rubbing, while for ghusl it is 'fattaheru', which could imply rubbing. Yet the majority Hanafi view maintains that rubbing is not obligatory even in ghusl.
This distinction shows how subtle differences in Quranic wording can lead to different rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبتدئ في صب الماء برأسه، ويغسل بعدها منكبه الأيمن، ثم الأيسر، ويدلك جسده، ويوالي غسله. (ويبتدئ في) حال (صب الماء برأسه، لما روينا)، (ويغسل بعدها) أي: الرأس (منكبه الأيمن، ثم الأيسر)، لاستحباب التيامن، وهو قول شمس الأئمة الحلواني، (و) يسن أن (يدلك) كل أعضاء (جسده) في المرة الأولى، ليعم الماء البدن في المرتين الأخيرتين، وليس الدلك بواجب في الغسل، إلا في رواية عن أبي يوسف لخصوص صيغة "فاطهروا" فيه، بخلاف الوضوء، فإنه بلفظ اغسلوا. ولما فرغ من بيان سنن الغسل شرع في بيان آدابه، فقال: (من حديث ميمون 103).
And he begins pouring water on his head, and he washes after it his right shoulder, then the left, and he rubs his body, and he performs them consecutively. (He begins) in the state (of pouring water on his head, due to what we narrated), (and he washes after it) i.e., the head (his right shoulder, then the left), due to the recommendation of starting with the right, and that is the saying of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, (and) it is sunnah that he rubs all limbs of his body in the first time, so that water reaches the body in the last two times, and rubbing is not obligatory in ghusl, except in a narration from Abu Yusuf due to the specific wording of "fattaheru" in it, unlike wudu, for it is with the wording "ighsilu". And when he finished explaining the sunan of ghusl, he began explaining its etiquettes, saying: (From the hadith of Maimunah, 103).
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the sunan (recommended acts) of ghusl. The text states that one should begin pouring water on the head, then wash the right shoulder, then the left, and rub the entire body. It also mentions performing them consecutively. The commentary explains that starting with the head is based on a hadith. Washing the right before the left is due to the recommendation of starting with the right. Rubbing the body in the first pouring is sunnah so that water spreads over the body in the subsequent pourings. Importantly, rubbing (dalk) is not obligatory in ghusl according to the main position, except in a narration from Abu Yusuf, who argued based on the Quranic word 'fattaheru' (purify yourselves) which implies rubbing. This is unlike wudu, where the verse uses 'ighsilu' (wash), so rubbing is not indicated. The author then concludes the section on sunan and transitions to adab.

Key Terms
دلك (dalk): Rubbing the body with hand to ensure water reaches all parts.
تيامن (tayammun): Starting with the right side out of preference.
سنن (sunan): Recommended acts; omission does not invalidate the act but loses reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Sunnah
C) Recommended (mandub)
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, rubbing the body during ghusl is a sunnah act; the relied-upon view is that it is not obligatory, though a narration from Abu Yusuf considers it wajib.

The Exception of Facing Qiblah in Ghusl
Clarifying the exception in ghusl adab regarding qiblah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why facing the qiblah is disliked during ghusl and identify the condition under which it becomes permissible.

Core Idea
Facing qiblah during ghusl is disliked because it often involves uncovering the awrah; covering removes the dislike.

We already learned the etiquettes of wudu. The etiquettes of ghusl are the same, but with one key exception: facing the qiblah. Why the difference? The text explains that ghusl often involves uncovering the private parts, making it disrespectful to face the qiblah. However, if one is properly covered, there is no harm. Understanding this distinction is essential for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Recall the adab of wudu
The text assumes you already know the etiquettes of wudu from a previous lesson. Briefly list them: facing qiblah (recommended in wudu), reciting tasmiyah, using water moderately, etc.
Focus on the fact that facing qiblah is recommended in wudu.
2
Identify the single exception for ghusl
The text states: 'except that he does not face the qiblah.' This is the only difference in adab between wudu and ghusl.
All other etiquettes remain the same.
3
Understand the reason: uncovering awrah
The reason given is 'because ghusl often involves uncovering the private parts.' Facing qiblah while uncovered is considered disrespectful.
The word 'ghaliban' (often) indicates it is the common state, not an absolute rule.
4
Recognize the condition for permissibility
If one is covered with a waist-wrapper (izar), facing qiblah is permissible (‘la ba’sa bihi’). The dislike is conditional upon lack of covering.
This shows the ruling is makruh tanzihi, not tahrimi.
