Chapter on the Etiquettes of Ghusl and Its Disliked Acts. And the etiquettes of ghusl are the etiquettes of wudu, which you already know, except that he does not face the qiblah while performing ghusl, because it often involves uncovering the private parts. So if he is covered with a waist-wrapper, there is no harm in it. And it is recommended that he not speak at all, whether it be human speech or other. As for human speech, it is disliked during uncovering; as for supplication, it is because it is in the place of used water and the location of filth and dirt. And it is recommended that he perform ghusl in a place where no one who is not permitted to look at his private parts can see him, due to the possibility of the private parts becoming exposed during ghusl or dressing, and due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Indeed Allah is Shy and Concealing, He loves shyness and concealment. So when any of you performs ghusl, let him conceal himself.' Narrated by Abu Dawud. And if he cannot find a screen among men, he performs ghusl and chooses what is more concealing. A woman among women is likewise, and among men she delays. And Ibn Wahban organized it in his poem (from the long meter): And washing for a person with no complete screen, so he does it among the people without delay. It is not like istinja, the difference is clear. And a woman among men delays. And if he uncovers his waist-wrapper in the bathhouse to wash and wring it, he does not sin, because it is impossible to clean it otherwise, and the sin is on the onlooker. And it is said: It is not permissible to undress in a small bathhouse room to wring his waist-wrapper or to shave his pubic hair. And it is said: It is permissible for a short duration. And it is said: There is no harm in it. And it is said: It is permissible to undress for ghusl, and he may undress his wife for intercourse as well, if the room is small, about five or ten cubits. (1) Narrated by Abu Dawud in the Book of the Bathhouse, Chapter on the Prohibition of Nudity (4012), and by al-Nasa'i in Ghusl, Chapter on Concealment during Ghusl (404). (2) Perhaps this is not the operative fatwa, because leaving the prohibited takes precedence over performing the commanded, and ghusl has an alternative which is tayammum, so uncovering the private parts for it is not permissible in the view of one who is not permitted to look at them, unlike circumcision. Hashiyah Ibn Abidin (1/104). (3) And likewise among men and women, and she should perform tayammum and pray due to her inability to use water legally. Al-Durr (1/105). (4) He said in al-Hidayah (4/85): The preferred view is that neither of them should look at the other's private parts due to his saying: 'When any of you goes to his wife, let him conceal himself and not undress like the undressing of two wild asses.' Narrated by Ibn Majah in Marriage, Chapter on Concealment during Intercourse (1921). Al-'ayrayn is the dual of 'ayr, which is the wild donkey. (5) The common cubit is the legal standard unit for measuring lengths, and its measure is six spans, each span is four fingers, each finger is six hair widths, and its measure in metric is 46.656 cm. Mu'jam Lughat al-Fuqaha / Dhi'ra /. -1.7- And disliked in it are what is disliked in wudu. And it is recommended to connect it to a tasbih as mentioned in wudu, because it includes wudu and more. (And disliked in it are what is disliked in wudu), and added to it is the dislike of supplication as mentioned. And consensus has been transmitted that it is not necessary to measure water for ghusl and wudu, because people's natures and conditions differ, so exceeding the sa' in ghusl and the mudd in wudu is permissible, as long as it does not lead to waswasa. (1) From the hadith of Bilal p.81. (2) p.106. (3) The sa' is a unit of measurement, and its quantity according to the Hanafis: 4 mudds = 8 ratls = 1028.57 dirhams = 3.362 liters = 3261.5 grams. Mu'jam Lughat al-Fuqaha / Sa'/. (4) The mudd: see p.77.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah expands on the etiquettes (adab) of ghusl and its disliked acts (makruhat). It begins by stating that the adab of ghusl are similar to those of wudu, which were previously explained, with one key exception: one does not face the qiblah during ghusl because it often involves uncovering the private parts. However, if one is covered with a waist-wrapper (izar), facing qiblah is permissible. The commentator then explains that speaking is disliked in general during ghusl—both worldly speech and supplication. The reason is that during ghusl, the body is uncovered, and supplication in a place of used water and impurities is inappropriate. The text then emphasizes the importance of privacy, citing the hadith 'Allah is Shy and Concealing...' recorded by Abu Dawud. It recommends choosing the most concealing spot and notes that if no screen is available, one still must perform ghusl, selecting the most hidden area. For women, the ruling is similar: among women she may perform ghusl, but among men she should delay until she can find privacy. Ibn Wahban's poetic summary reinforces this. The passage then addresses the situation in a bathhouse (hammam): if one uncovers to wash and wring his garment, he does not sin because it is necessary; the sin falls on the onlooker. There are multiple opinions (qila) about undressing in a small bathhouse: some say it is not allowed, some say it is allowed for a short time, some say there is no harm. A footnote clarifies that the preferred view (mufta bihi) may be that undressing is not permissible because preventing the prohibited act takes precedence over performing the commanded act; and ghusl has an alternative (tayammum), so uncovering for ghusl is not allowed when others may see. The passage then returns to the matn, stating that all makruhat of wudu apply also to ghusl, with the addition of supplication being disliked. Finally, it notes consensus (ijma) that there is no fixed quantity of water required for ghusl or wudu; people differ in their needs. Exceeding the sa' (for ghusl) or mudd (for wudu) is permissible as long as it does not lead to obsessive behavior (waswasa). The commentator provides the Hanafi definition of sa' and mudd for reference.

Key Terms
استقبال القبلة (istiqbal al-qiblah): Facing the direction of the Kaaba; in ghusl it is disliked because of the usual state of uncovering.
عورة (awrah): Private parts that must be covered; for men, from navel to knees; for women, whole body except face and hands in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it disliked to face the qiblah during ghusl?
A) Because the Prophet specifically forbade it.
B) Because ghusl often involves uncovering the private parts.
C) Because it is not a form of worship.
D) Because one should not face qiblah when wet.

Key Takeaway
Facing qiblah during ghusl is disliked (makruh tanzihi) because it often involves uncovering the awrah; covering removes the dislike.

Bathhouse Etiquettes and Disliked Acts of Ghusl
Expanding on bathhouse etiquettes, disliked acts, and water quantity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rulings on concealment in a bathhouse, identify the disliked acts of ghusl, and state the Hanafi view on water quantity.

Core Idea
Uncovering the awrah in a bathhouse is prohibited unless necessary; speaking and supplication are disliked; no fixed water measure.

The text now turns to practical scenarios: bathhouses, where uncovering may be unavoidable, and the disliked acts of ghusl. It presents multiple opinions within the Hanafi school and finally establishes the mufta bihi. The lesson also covers the important principle that there is no rigid quantity of water for ghusl or wudu, though moderation is encouraged.

Guided Path
1
Understand the necessity exception in the bathhouse
The text begins: if a man uncovers his waist-wrapper in the bathhouse to wash or wring it, he does not sin because it is necessary; the sin is on the onlooker.
Necessity (darurah) makes the prohibition of uncovering temporarily lifted.
2
Examine the multiple opinions (qila) on undressing
Four opinions are cited: (1) not permissible, (2) permissible for a short time, (3) no harm, (4) permissible for ghusl and intercourse in a small room. The footnote indicates the preferred view is the first.
These are intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is that it is not permissible because prevention takes precedence.
3
Identify the added disliked acts for ghusl
The matn states: 'And disliked in it are what is disliked in wudu, and added to it is the dislike of supplication.' So speaking worldly talk is disliked, and making dua is also disliked due to the impure environment.
This is an addition beyond the wudu adab.
4
Grasp the flexibility of water quantity
The passage concludes with consensus that there is no fixed measure: the sa' (3.36L) for ghusl and mudd (0.84L) for wudu are recommended, but exceeding them is allowed as long as it does not lead to waswasa (obsessive doubts).
This prevents rigid literalism; the focus is on avoidance of waste and obsession.

Source Text

فصل في آداب الاغتسال ومكروهاته

Chapter on the Etiquettes of Ghusl and Its Disliked Acts. And the etiquettes of ghusl are the etiquettes of wudu, which you already know, except that he does not face the qiblah while performing ghusl, because it often involves uncovering the private parts. So if he is covered with a waist-wrapper, there is no harm in it. And it is recommended that he not speak at all, whether it be human speech or other. As for human speech, it is disliked during uncovering; as for supplication, it is because it is in the place of used water and the location of filth and dirt. And it is recommended that he perform ghusl in a place where no one who is not permitted to look at his private parts can see him, due to the possibility of the private parts becoming exposed during ghusl or dressing, and due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Indeed Allah is Shy and Concealing, He loves shyness and concealment. So when any of you performs ghusl, let him conceal himself.' Narrated by Abu Dawud. And if he cannot find a screen among men, he performs ghusl and chooses what is more concealing. A woman among women is likewise, and among men she delays. And Ibn Wahban organized it in his poem (from the long meter): And washing for a person with no complete screen, so he does it among the people without delay. It is not like istinja, the difference is clear. And a woman among men delays. And if he uncovers his waist-wrapper in the bathhouse to wash and wring it, he does not sin, because it is impossible to clean it otherwise, and the sin is on the onlooker. And it is said: It is not permissible to undress in a small bathhouse room to wring his waist-wrapper or to shave his pubic hair. And it is said: It is permissible for a short duration. And it is said: There is no harm in it. And it is said: It is permissible to undress for ghusl, and he may undress his wife for intercourse as well, if the room is small, about five or ten cubits. (1) Narrated by Abu Dawud in the Book of the Bathhouse, Chapter on the Prohibition of Nudity (4012), and by al-Nasa'i in Ghusl, Chapter on Concealment during Ghusl (404). (2) Perhaps this is not the operative fatwa, because leaving the prohibited takes precedence over performing the commanded, and ghusl has an alternative which is tayammum, so uncovering the private parts for it is not permissible in the view of one who is not permitted to look at them, unlike circumcision. Hashiyah Ibn Abidin (1/104). (3) And likewise among men and women, and she should perform tayammum and pray due to her inability to use water legally. Al-Durr (1/105). (4) He said in al-Hidayah (4/85): The preferred view is that neither of them should look at the other's private parts due to his saying: 'When any of you goes to his wife, let him conceal himself and not undress like the undressing of two wild asses.' Narrated by Ibn Majah in Marriage, Chapter on Concealment during Intercourse (1921). Al-'ayrayn is the dual of 'ayr, which is the wild donkey. (5) The common cubit is the legal standard unit for measuring lengths, and its measure is six spans, each span is four fingers, each finger is six hair widths, and its measure in metric is 46.656 cm. Mu'jam Lughat al-Fuqaha / Dhi'ra /. -1.7- And disliked in it are what is disliked in wudu. And it is recommended to connect it to a tasbih as mentioned in wudu, because it includes wudu and more. (And disliked in it are what is disliked in wudu), and added to it is the dislike of supplication as mentioned. And consensus has been transmitted that it is not necessary to measure water for ghusl and wudu, because people's natures and conditions differ, so exceeding the sa' in ghusl and the mudd in wudu is permissible, as long as it does not lead to waswasa. (1) From the hadith of Bilal p.81. (2) p.106. (3) The sa' is a unit of measurement, and its quantity according to the Hanafis: 4 mudds = 8 ratls = 1028.57 dirhams = 3.362 liters = 3261.5 grams. Mu'jam Lughat al-Fuqaha / Sa'/. (4) The mudd: see p.77.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah expands on the etiquettes (adab) of ghusl and its disliked acts (makruhat). It begins by stating that the adab of ghusl are similar to those of wudu, which were previously explained, with one key exception: one does not face the qiblah during ghusl because it often involves uncovering the private parts. However, if one is covered with a waist-wrapper (izar), facing qiblah is permissible. The commentator then explains that speaking is disliked in general during ghusl—both worldly speech and supplication. The reason is that during ghusl, the body is uncovered, and supplication in a place of used water and impurities is inappropriate. The text then emphasizes the importance of privacy, citing the hadith 'Allah is Shy and Concealing...' recorded by Abu Dawud. It recommends choosing the most concealing spot and notes that if no screen is available, one still must perform ghusl, selecting the most hidden area. For women, the ruling is similar: among women she may perform ghusl, but among men she should delay until she can find privacy. Ibn Wahban's poetic summary reinforces this. The passage then addresses the situation in a bathhouse (hammam): if one uncovers to wash and wring his garment, he does not sin because it is necessary; the sin falls on the onlooker. There are multiple opinions (qila) about undressing in a small bathhouse: some say it is not allowed, some say it is allowed for a short time, some say there is no harm. A footnote clarifies that the preferred view (mufta bihi) may be that undressing is not permissible because preventing the prohibited act takes precedence over performing the commanded act; and ghusl has an alternative (tayammum), so uncovering for ghusl is not allowed when others may see. The passage then returns to the matn, stating that all makruhat of wudu apply also to ghusl, with the addition of supplication being disliked. Finally, it notes consensus (ijma) that there is no fixed quantity of water required for ghusl or wudu; people differ in their needs. Exceeding the sa' (for ghusl) or mudd (for wudu) is permissible as long as it does not lead to obsessive behavior (waswasa). The commentator provides the Hanafi definition of sa' and mudd for reference.

Key Terms
حمام (hammam): A bathhouse or public bathing place where people wash; the text discusses rulings on uncovering there.
صاع (sa'): A unit of volume; for Hanafis, 4 mudds = 8 ratls = approximately 3.362 liters, used as a standard for water quantity in ghusl.
مد (mudd): A unit of volume; 1/4 of a sa', approximately 0.84 liters, recommended for wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi (operative fatwa) regarding undressing in a small bathhouse room?
A) It is permissible for a short duration.
B) It is not permissible because preventing prohibition takes precedence.
C) There is no harm in it.
D) It is permissible only if the room is exactly five cubits.

Key Takeaway
Bathhouse undressing is generally not permissible (mufta bihi), and speaking and supplication are disliked during ghusl; water quantity is flexible to avoid waswasa.

The Friday Bath: Sunnah or Obligation? Proofs and the Principle of Abrogation
Establishes Friday bath as sunnah with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the Friday bath, identify the proof from hadith, and explain the principle of abrogation (naskh) used to reconcile conflicting texts.

Core Idea
The Friday bath is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib, because a later hadith abrogated the earlier command.

In this passage, the author of Nur al-Idah establishes that the Friday bath is sunnah (recommended) and not obligatory. He cites a hadith that explicitly presents it as optional, and explains that earlier commands to bathe were abrogated due to a change in circumstances. This lesson will guide you through the proof, the abrogation narrative, and an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the bath's virtue is tied to the prayer or the day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling and its evidence
The author states the bath is sunnah for Friday prayer and provides the hadith: 'Whoever performs wudu on Friday, that is good enough; whoever bathes is better.' Recognize that 'afdal' indicates preference, not obligation.
This is the main proof for the sunnah status.
2
Examine the abrogation argument
The author claims this hadith abrogates earlier commands that seem obligatory. He provides a historical narration from Ibn Abbas showing the reason for the original command (unpleasant smells) and subsequent change (conditions improved).
Abrogation (naskh) is a key usul principle here.
3
Differentiate the two positions on the bath's virtue
Abu Yusuf says the bath is for the prayer, so breaking wudu after the bath loses the virtue. Al-Hasan says the bath is for the day, so virtue remains even after breaking wudu.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Determine the practical consequence
If one bathes, then breaks wudu, then performs wudu for prayer, according to Abu Yusuf the virtue of the Friday bath is lost; according to al-Hasan it remains. Both agree the prayer itself is valid.
The thamarah al-khilaf is about the reward, not the validity of prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل يُسَنُ الاغْتِسَالُ لأربعَةِ أشْيَاءَ: منها صلاة الجمعةِ على الصحيح بقوله: مَنْ تَوَضَّأَ يَوْمَ الْجُمُعَةِ فَبِهَا وَنِعْمَتْ، وَمَنْ اغْتَسَلَ فَهُوَ أفْضَلُ. وهو ناسخ لظاهر قوله: غُسْلُ الْجُمُعَةِ وَاجِبٌ عَلَى كُلِّ مُخْتَلِمٍ. وقوله: إِذَا جَاءَ أَحَدُكُمْ الْجُمُعَةَ فَلْيَغْتَسِل. أو نقول: هو منه للحكم بانتهاء علته. والدليل على تأخره، ما رواه أبو داود عن عكرمة أن أُناساً من أهل العراق جاؤوا فقالوا: يا ابن عباس، أترى الغسل يوم الجمعة واجباً؟ فقال: لا، ولكنه أطهر وخير لمن اغتسل، ومن لم يغتسل فليس بواجب، وسأخبركم كيف بدأ الغسل، كان الناس مجهودين يلبسون الصوف ويعملون على ظهورهم، وكان مسجدهم ضيقاً مقارب السقف إنما هو عريش، فخرج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في يوم حار وعرق الناس في ذلك الصوف حتى ثارت منهم رياح أذى بعضهم بذلك بعضاً، فلما وجد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم تلك الرياح قال: يا أيها الناس، إذا كان هذا اليوم فاغتسلوا وليمس أحدكم أمثل ما يجد من دهنه وطيبه. قال ابن عباس: ثم جاء الله بالخير ولبسوا غير الصوف وكفوا العمل ووسع مسجدهم وذهب بعض الذي كان يؤذي بعضهم بعضاً من العرق. انتهى. وأما كون الغسل للصلاة لا لليوم، فهو قول أبي يوسف، لأن الصلاة أفضل من الوقت، وقيل: لليوم وهو قول الحسن، وثمرته تظهر فيمن اغتسل ثم أحدث وتوضأ وصلى الجمعة لا يكون له فضل غسل الجمعة عند أبي يوسف خلافاً للحسن.
Chapter: Bath is recommended for four things: Friday prayer according to the correct view, due to his saying: 'Whoever performs wudu on Friday, that is good enough, and whoever takes a bath is better.' This abrogates the apparent meaning of his saying: 'Friday bath is obligatory upon every pubescent male.' And his saying: 'When one of you comes to Friday prayer, let him bathe.' Or we say: it is abrogated due to the cessation of its cause. The evidence for its later abrogation is what Abu Dawud narrated from Ikrimah that some people from Iraq came and said: O Ibn Abbas, do you consider the bath on Friday obligatory? He said: No, but it is purer and better for whoever bathes, and whoever does not bathe, it is not obligatory, and I will inform you how the bath began. The people were struggling, wearing wool and working on their backs, and their mosque was narrow with a low ceiling, only a canopy. The Messenger of Allah came out on a hot day, and the people sweated in that wool until unpleasant smells arose from them, bothering each other. When the Messenger of Allah found those smells, he said: O people, when this day comes, bathe and let each of you apply the best of what he finds of oil and perfume. Ibn Abbas said: Then Allah brought good, and they wore other than wool, and they ceased working, and their mosque was expanded, and some of the annoyance that came from sweat disappeared. End. As for the bath being for the prayer and not for the day, that is the statement of Abu Yusuf, because the prayer is superior to the time. And it is said: for the day, which is the statement of al-Hasan. Its practical implication appears in one who bathed, then broke his wudu, performed wudu, and prayed Friday: he does not have the virtue of the Friday bath according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to al-Hasan.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The author establishes that the Friday bath is sunnah (recommended) not obligatory, based on a hadith that presents it as optional and better. He explains that the earlier command to bathe was abrogated. The narration from Ibn Abbas provides historical context: the initial command was due to unpleasant smells from sweat and wool, but later when conditions improved, the obligation was lifted. Then an intra-Hanafi dispute is presented: Abu Yusuf holds that the bath is for the prayer, so if one breaks wudu after bathing and then makes wudu, the virtue of the Friday bath is lost. Al-Hasan holds that the bath is for the day itself, so its virtue remains even after breaking wudu. The text follows the author's order, first giving the ruling and proof, then the ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
غسل الجمعة (ghusl al-jumu'ah): The recommended full-body bath on Friday before the Friday prayer.
ناسخ (nasikh): A later text (Quran or hadith) that abrogates an earlier ruling.
مختلم (mukhtalim): A male who has reached puberty and experienced nocturnal emission or similar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of the Friday bath?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah
C) Fard 'ayn
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Friday bath is an emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) for the prayer, based on hadith and abrogation of earlier commands.

The Sunnah Baths for Eid, Ihram, and Arafah
Ruling with proof for three sunnah baths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each of the three sunnah baths (Eid, ihram, Arafah), cite the prophetic proof, and explain why the ihram bath is a bath of cleanliness (tanzif) not purification.

Core Idea
Three sunnah baths established by the Prophet's practice: for Eid, for ihram (cleanliness), and for the pilgrim at Arafah after noon.

This lesson covers three non-obligatory baths that the Prophet (peace be upon him) regularly performed: the baths for the two Eids, for entering the state of ihram, and for standing at Arafah. Each has its own ruling and conditions. The passage also highlights an important Hanafi distinction: the ihram bath is for cleanliness, not for removing ritual impurity, so it is valid even for a menstruating woman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three baths
Locate in the passage the three occasions for sunnah ghusl: Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, and for ihram (Hajj/Umrah), and the bath at Arafah.
The Arafah bath is only for the pilgrim present at Arafah after noon.
2
State the ruling and its evidence
For each bath, note that the ruling is sunnah (recommended). The proof is the Prophet's habitual practice (كان يغتسل). Identify the Hadith quoted: 'He used to bathe on the day of Fitr, Adha, and Arafah.'
The Hanafis classify these as sunnah mu'akkadah based on the Prophet's continuous practice.
3
Analyze the distinction for the ihram bath
The passage explicitly states that the ihram bath is a 'ghusl tanzif' (cleansing) not 'taharah' (purification). Understand the consequence: it is valid without intention and for women with menstruation/postpartum bleeding. Also, one does not perform tayammum if water is lacking.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the conditions for the Arafah bath
Note the restrictions: it is only sunnah for the pilgrim who is present at Arafah, not for others; it must be performed after noon (zawal), not before; and it is to be done at Arafah, not outside.
The purpose is to attain the virtue of standing at Arafah in a state of cleanliness.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the Eid bath
Abu Yusuf held that the Eid bath is for the prayer (like the Friday bath), not for the day itself. The passage mentions this view without explicit tarjih.
The relied-upon position is still that it is sunnah for the day, but Abu Yusuf's view is considered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصلاة العيدين الفطر والأضحى لأن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يغتسل يوم الفطر والأضحى وعرفة، وكونه للصلاة قول أبي يوسف كما في الجمعة. وللإحرام بحج أو عمرة أو بهما، لأنه تجرد لإهلاله واغتسل. وهو غسل تنظيف لا تطهير، فتغتسل ولو كان بها الحيض والنفاس؛ ولهذا لا يتيمم مكانه بفقد الماء. ويسن للحاج لا لغيرهم في عرفة لا خارجاً عنها بعد الزوال لا قبله، لينال فضل الغسل للوقوف، قيد به لما قال ابن أمير حاج: ما أظن أحداً ذهب إلى استنانه ليوم عرفة من غير حضور عرفات.
And the two Eid prayers (Fitr and Adha), because the Messenger of Allah used to bathe on the day of Fitr, Adha, and Arafah. And it being for the prayer is the statement of Abu Yusuf, as in Friday. And for ihram for Hajj or Umrah or both, because he disengaged for his talbiyah and bathed. It is a bath of cleanliness, not purification, so a woman bathes even if she is menstruating or postpartum; therefore, one does not perform tayammum in its place due to lack of water. And it is sunnah for the pilgrim, not for others, at Arafah, not outside it, after noon, not before, to attain the virtue of the bath for the standing. It is restricted by what Ibn Amir Hajj said: I do not think anyone goes to its recommendation for the day of Arafah without being present at Arafat.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage presents three sunnah baths with their proofs. First, the bath for the two Eids (Fitr and Adha) is sunnah because the Prophet practiced it. Abu Yusuf's view that the bath is for the prayer, not the day, is mentioned. Second, the bath for ihram is a bath of cleanliness (ghusl tanzif) not purification (taharah), so a menstruating woman performs it. This distinction means it does not require water for tayammum if water is unavailable. Third, the bath for Arafah is specifically for the pilgrim at Arafah after noon, not for others and not before noon. The text follows the same pattern as the Friday bath discussion.

Key Terms
غسل الإحرام (ghusl al-ihram): The recommended bath before entering the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
غسل عرفة (ghusl Arafah): The recommended bath for the pilgrim at Arafah after noon on the day of Arafah.
تنظيف (tanzif): A bath for cleanliness, not for removing ritual impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the bath for ihram is classified as:
A) Ghusl wujub (obligatory bath)
B) Ghusl tanzif (cleanliness bath)

D) Ghusl nadb (optional bath)

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's practice shows that ghusl is recommended for Eid, ihram (as cleanliness), and for a pilgrim at Arafah after noon.

Recommended Baths (Mandub): Times and Occasions
Lists recommended baths with brief proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended occasions for ghusl mentioned in the passage and explain that they are mandub (recommended), not obligatory.

Core Idea
Ghusl is recommended on many occasions, not just obligatory ones—rewarded but not sin upon omission.

In this passage, the author begins listing the sixteen occasions when a bath (ghusl) is recommended (mandub). While the full list is not present, we see seven clear examples covering conversion, puberty, recovery from illness, cupping, washing the deceased, and two blessed nights. Understanding that these are recommended, not obligatory, helps prioritize worship without undue burden.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm level
The word 'yundab' indicates the ruling is mandub (recommended). Note that mandub is lower than sunnah mu'akkadah in reward but still meritorious.
Hanafis distinguish mandub from sunnah; mandub is rewarded but not stressed.
2
List the occasions mentioned
Read the text and extract each occasion: (1) new Muslim pure from janabah, (2) reaching puberty at 15, (3) recovering from insanity, (4) after cupping, (5) after washing a deceased, (6) night of Bara'ah, (7) night of Qadr (if certain).
Only seven of sixteen are present due to OCR truncation.
3
Identify the evidence for each
For each occasion, note the provided proof: hadith for the new Muslim (command to Qays and Thumamah), analogy for others, and general recommendation for the nights.
Some proofs are explicit, others implicit.
4
Apply the hanafi_position_box
Confirm that all listed are mandub according to Zahir al-Riwayah, no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and mufta bihi is that they are recommended.
The box pre-populated from the source confirms this.
5
Distinguish from obligatory baths
Compare with obligatory ghusl (janabah, menstruation, postpartum). Mandub baths are virtuous but not required.
This clarifies the legal hierarchy.

And bath is recommended (yundab) on approximately sixteen things: for one who accepts Islam while pure from janabah, menstruation, and postpartum bleeding – because the Prophet commanded Qays ibn Asim and Thumamah to do so when they accepted Islam, and that is interpreted as recommendation. And for one who reaches puberty by age, which is fifteen years according to the mufta bihi view for both boy and girl. And for one who recovers from insanity, and it is appropriate for one who recovers from unconsciousness. And upon completion of cupping. And washing a deceased, to exit from the disagreement of it being obligatory for them. And on the night of Bara'ah, which is the night of mid-Sha'ban, as an act of devotion and veneration and reviving it, for on it are apportioned provisions and lifespans. And the night of Qadr if one sees it with certainty, or acting on following what has been reported about its time, to revive it.

Commentary
This passage lists some of the recommended baths (mandub). The author mentions them with brief proofs or reasons. The list is part of a longer enumeration of sixteen occasions. The baths mentioned include: for a new Muslim (if already pure), for one reaching puberty, for recovery from insanity or unconsciousness, after cupping, after washing a deceased, on the night of Bara'ah (mid-Sha'ban), and on Laylat al-Qadr if one is certain of it. The proofs are from hadith and analogy. The author also notes that the bath for washing the deceased is to avoid disagreement that it might be obligatory.

Key Terms
مندوب (mandub): An act that is recommended but not obligatory; its doer is rewarded, its abandoner is not punished.
ليلة براءة (laylat al-bara'ah): The night of mid-Sha'ban, considered a night of blessing and forgiveness.
ليلة القدر (laylat al-qadr): The Night of Decree in Ramadan, better than a thousand months.

Sunnah Baths: Friday, Eid, Ihram, and Arafah
Lists four sunnah baths with proofs and intra-madhhab ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunnah baths according to the Hanafi school, identify their proofs, and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the Eid bath.

Core Idea
Four baths are sunnah muakkadah: Friday, Eid, ihram, and Arafah — proven by the Prophet's practice.

This passage from Nur al-Idah and its sharh presents the four occasions where ghusl (full body wash) is sunnah muakkadah. It also discusses the purpose (removing odor) and an intra-Hanafi difference regarding whether the Eid bath is for the day or the prayer. The proofs are ahad hadith, which in Hanafi usul indicates sunnah, not obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage lists four occasions for ghusl: Friday, Eid (Fitr and Adha), ihram (for Hajj or Umrah), and Arafah (for the pilgrim after noon). The ruling for all is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
Sunnah muakkadah is a recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed; omitting it is not sinful but is discouraged.
2
Locate the dalil
For Eid and Arafah, the hadith: 'The Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to bathe on the day of Fitr, Adha, and Arafah.' For ihram, the proof is the Prophet's practice when he disengaged for ihram and bathed. For Friday, the purpose (removing odor) is mentioned implicitly via Miraj al-Diraya.
The Friday bath is not explicitly cited here; the passage relies on the broader ruling from other sources.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verb 'كان يغتسل' (he used to bathe) indicates habitual action. In Hanafi usul, a habitual action of the Prophet indicates nadb (sunnah) unless there is evidence of obligation (wujub). Since the hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), it cannot establish fard.
This distinguishes the Hanafi position from those who consider Friday ghusl wajib (e.g., Hanbali) based on a different interpretation of command hadith.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
For Eid, Abu Yusuf holds that the bath is for the prayer itself (by analogy with Friday), while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold it is for the day. The text appears to side with Abu Yusuf ('as in Friday'). Also, within the Hanafi school, there is a discussion about the timing of the Friday bath: it can be done on Thursday or Friday night according to Miraj al-Diraya.
The practical difference: if the bath is for the prayer, it is best done close to prayer time; if for the day, any time on the day suffices.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that all four baths are sunnah muakkadah. The text's phrasing 'as in Friday' suggests that for Eid, the prayer-focused view (Abu Yusuf) is accepted. The bath for ihram is a cleansing bath, not purifying, so it is valid even for a menstruating woman, and tayammum cannot substitute it. The Arafah bath is restricted to the pilgrim present at Arafah after noon.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah from the core Hanafi texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاغتسال
وصلاة العيدين، وللإحرام، وللحاج في عَرَفَةَ، بعد الزَّوَالِ
وفي «معراج الدراية»: لو اغتسل يوم الخميس، أو ليلة الجمعة استن بالسنة لحصول المقصود، وهو قطع الرائحة. (وَصَلاةُ العِيْدينِ)، الفطر والأضحى « لأنَّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يغتسلُ يومَ الفطر والأضحى وعرفة» (۱)، وكونه للصلاة، قول أبي يوسف كما في الجمعة. وللإحْرَامِ) بحج أو عمرة أو بهما، « لأنَّهُ ، تَجرد لإهلاله، واغْتَسَـل» . وهـو غسـل تنظيـف لا تطهير، فتغتسل ولو كان بها الحيض والنفاس؛ ولهذا لا يتيمم مكانه بفقد الماء، (وَ) . يسن ( للحاج، لا لغيرهم، في عَرَفَةَ، لا خارجاً عنها (بَعْدَ الزَّوَال)، لا قبله، لينــال فـضـل الـغـســل للوقوف، قيد ،به لما قال ابن أمير حاج » : ما أظن أحداً ذهب إلى استنانه ليوم عرفة، من غير حضور عرفات.
The bath: and for the two Eid prayers, for ihram, and for the pilgrim at Arafah after noon. And in Miraj al-Diraya: if one bathes on Thursday or Friday night, he follows the sunnah because the purpose (removing odor) is achieved. (And for the two Eid prayers), Fitr and Adha, because the Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to bathe on the day of Fitr, Adha, and Arafah. And that it is for the prayer is the saying of Abu Yusuf, as in Friday. And for ihram for Hajj or Umrah or both, because he disengaged for his talbiyah and bathed. It is a cleansing bath, not purifying, so even a menstruating or postpartum woman may bathe; thus one does not do tayammum in place of it if water is absent. And it is sunnah for the pilgrim, not others, at Arafah, not outside it, after noon (zawal), not before, to attain the virtue of the bath for standing. This is restricted by what Ibn Amir Haj said: I do not think anyone went to its being sunnah for the day of Arafah without being at Arafat.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage states the sunnah baths (ghusl masnun) with their proofs. The first bath mentioned is for Friday, as referenced in the commentary from Miraj al-Diraya; it is sunnah, and the purpose is removing odor. Then the bath for the two Eid prayers (Fitr and Adha) is established by the hadith that the Prophet ﷺ bathed on those days. Abu Yusuf holds it is for the prayer itself, analogous to Friday. Next, the bath for ihram (for Hajj or Umrah) is proven by the Prophet's practice when he disengaged for ihram. This bath is for cleanliness, not ritual purification, so it is valid even for a woman in menstruation or postpartum; thus tayammum cannot substitute. Finally, the bath for standing at Arafah is sunnah specifically for the pilgrim, done after noon (zawal) at Arafah, not before or elsewhere. Ibn Amir Haj notes that no one considers it sunnah for the day of Arafah without being present at Arafat.

Key Terms
الاغتسال (al-ightisal): The act of washing the entire body with water; in this context, a ritual bath recommended for specific occasions.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah; entering ihram involves intention and certain restrictions.
عرفة (Arafah): The second day of Hajj (9th Dhul Hijjah) when pilgrims stand at the plain of Arafat; the bath is specifically for the pilgrim at that location after noon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Friday morning only
B) Thursday or Thursday night
C) Saturday
D) Any day before Friday

Key Takeaway
The four sunnah baths (Friday, Eid, ihram, Arafah) are recommended but not obligatory; their evidence lies in the Prophet's habitual practice, which in Hanafi usul indicates sunnah.

The Sixteen Recommended Baths (Mandub Ghusl)
Lists sixteen recommended baths with brief reasons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sixteen occasions for recommended ghusl and explain why they are mandub (not wajib) in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Sixteen occasions warrant a recommended bath — performing it is meritorious, omitting it is not sinful.

The author enumerates specific times when performing a full bath (ghusl) is recommended (mandub) rather than obligatory. This lesson walks through the list, noting the underlying reasons and the legal ruling (mandub). Understanding this list helps distinguish between obligatory, sunnah, and recommended baths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general category
All baths in this list are mandub — recommended but not required. The text begins with 'yundabu' (it is recommended).
Mandub is lower than sunnah muakkadah; omitting it is not sinful.
2
List the occasions with reasons
Work through each of the sixteen items. For each, note the rationale given in the commentary: honoring, revival of virtuous nights, avoiding disagreement, etc.
The list includes conversion to Islam, puberty, recovery from insanity, cupping, washing a dead body, special nights, ritual places, acts of worship, and natural phenomena.
3
Examine the proof for the first item
The author cites the Prophet's command to Qays ibn Asim and Thumamah upon embracing Islam. This command is interpreted as recommendation (nadb) because it was not made binding on all new Muslims.
Hadith evidence is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah, so it yields mandub, not wajib.
4
Note the exceptions and disagreements
For cupping and washing a dead body, the recommended bath avoids the disagreement of those who consider it obligatory. Also, the age of puberty is given as fifteen (mufta bihi).
The text acknowledges legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Apply the ruling to new scenarios
The principle is that any occasion associated with spiritual significance, fear, or rejoicing may warrant mandub ghusl. This allows analogy to similar situations.
Modern examples: entering a historic Islamic site, before a major supplication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُنْدَبُ الاغتسال في ستةَ عَشَرَ شيئاً تقريباً لِمَنْ أَسْلَمَ طَاهِراً) عن جنابة وحيض ونفاس؛ لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أمــر قيس بن عاصم وثمامة بذلك، حين أسلما (۳)، وحمل ذلك على الندب ، ولِمَنْ بَلَغَ بالسِّنِّ)، وهـو خمسة عشر سنة على المفتى به في الجارية والغلام ( ولمَنْ أفاق مِنْ جُنون)، وينبغي ذلك لمـن أفاق من إغماء، (وَعِنْدَ) الفراغ من ( حِجَامَةٍ)، (وغُسلِ ميت) () ، خروجاً للخلاف من لزوم الغسل بهما، (وفي ليلة بَرَاءةَ) ()، وهي ليلة النصف من شعبان، تقرباً وتعظيماً لشأنها، وإحيائها، إذ فيها تقسم الأرزاق والآجال، (وَليلةِ القَدْرِ إِذَا رَآهَا) يقيناً، أو عملاً باتباع ما ورد في وقتها، لإحيائها،
(وَلِدُخُولِ مَدِينَةِ سَيِّدِنَا النّبيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم)، تعظيماً لها لحرمتها، وقدومه على حضرة المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم، (وَلِلوقوف بمُزْدَلِفَة ) ()، لأنه ثاني الجمعين، وفيه غفرت الدماء والمظالم، بدعائه لأمته، واستجاب الله تعالى دعاءه فيها (غَداةَ يومِ النَّحْرِ)، يعني: بعد طلوع فجر يوم النحر ؛ لأنه وقت الوقوف بالمزدلفة، ويخرج قبیل طلوع الشمس، (وَعِنْدَ دُخُولِ مَكّةَ)، شرفها الله تعالى و (لِطَوافِ الزِّيَارَةِ)، فيؤدي الـفـرض بأكمل الطهارتين، ويقوم بتعظيم حرم رمة المكان، وكذا عند دخولها لأداء نسك (ولصَلاةِ كُسُوف) الشمس، وخسوف القمر، لتخويف الله العباد بهما، وأقرب أحوال الابتهال الطهارة الكاملة في الصلاة لهما، ( واستسقاء) لطلب استنزال الغيث رحمة للخلق، بالاستغفار والتضرع، والصلاة بالطهارة الكاملة، وفَزَع) من أي شيء كان التجأ إلى عفو الله وكرمه بالوقوف بين يديه بالذلة والافتقار لكشف الكرب، (وظلمة) حصلت نهاراً، (وَرِيحٍ شَدِيدٍ) في أي وقت، لأن الله تعالى أهلك بالريح من طغى كـــوم عــاد، فيلتجئ الناس إلى الله تعالى، وأقرب أحوالهم الوقوف في الصلاة بأكمل الطهارتين، ويندب للتائب مـــن ذنب، وللقادم من سفر، وللمستحاضة إذا انقطع دمها () ، ولمن يراد قتله، ولرمي الجمار، ويندب غسل جميع بدنه، أو ثوبه إذا أصابته نجاسة وخفي مكانها.
And it is recommended (mandub) to bathe in approximately sixteen things: for one who becomes Muslim while pure (from janabah, menstruation, postpartum) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded Qays ibn Asim and Thumamah to do that when they embraced Islam, and that is interpreted as recommendation; for one who attains puberty by age, which is fifteen years according to the fatwa for both girl and boy; for one who recovers from insanity (and similarly from fainting); upon finishing from cupping; after washing a dead body, to avoid the disagreement about the necessity of bathing for these; on the night of Bara'ah (mid-Sha'ban) to honor and revive it, as it is when provisions and lifespans are apportioned; on Laylat al-Qadr if one sees it with certainty or follows what is reported about its time; for entering the city of our master the Prophet ﷺ out of respect; for standing at Muzdalifah on the morning of the Day of Sacrifice after dawn; upon entering Mecca; for Tawaf al-Ziyarah (the obligatory circumambulation); for the eclipse prayer (solar and lunar); for the prayer for rain (istisqa'); for the prayer of fear (faza') from any cause; when darkness occurs during the day; during a severe wind at any time. And it is recommended for one who repents from a sin, for one returning from a journey, for a mustahadah (woman with chronic uterine bleeding) when her bleeding stops, for one who is to be executed, for stoning the jamarat, and it is recommended to wash the entire body or clothes if they are touched by impurity whose location is unknown.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage lists recommended (mandub) baths, i.e., those that are meritorious but not sunnah muakkadah. The first is for a new Muslim who is already in a state of purity; the Prophet commanded Qays and Thumamah to bathe after embracing Islam. Next is at puberty by age (fifteen years, which is the mufta bihi). Then upon recovering from insanity or fainting. After cupping and washing a dead body, to avoid the disagreement that these require obligatory ghusl. On the night of mid-Sha'ban (Bara'ah) and Laylat al-Qadr (if one is certain or follows the reported time) to revive them. For entering Madinah to honor it. For standing at Muzdalifah on the morning of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. Upon entering Mecca. For the obligatory Tawaf al-Ziyarah. For eclipse prayers (solar and lunar). For the prayer for rain (istisqa'). For the prayer during fear (faza') from any calamity. During daytime darkness and severe wind. Additional recommended baths: for a repentant person, a traveler returning, a mustahadah when bleeding stops, a person about to be executed, and for stoning the jamarat. Also, if an impurity hits the body or clothes but the spot is unknown, it is recommended to wash the whole body or garment.

Key Terms
مندوب (mandub): An act that is recommended but not obligatory; performing it is meritorious and omitting it is not sinful.
ليلة براءة (Laylat al-Bara'ah): The night of the 15th of Sha'ban; it is considered a night of forgiveness and decreeing of destinies.
المستحاضة (al-mustahadah): A woman with chronic uterine bleeding (istihadah) that is irregular; she is treated as in a state of perpetual minor impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Inner Dimension of Purification: Ikhlas as the Condition for Taharah
A reminder that physical purity must be accompanied by spiritual sincerity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi scholars link ritual purity (taharah shariyyah) to sincerity of intention (ikhlas) and identify the spiritual impurities that nullify its benefit.

Core Idea
Ritual purity without sincerity is like a body without a soul – the outward act is incomplete.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah refines the Hanafi understanding of taharah. While the earlier lessons covered the physical conditions of wudu and ghusl, this note reminds us that the ultimate purpose of purification is to make the servant worthy of standing before Allah. Without purifying the heart from spiritual diseases, the physical purification does not achieve its full benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ritual purity (taharah shariyyah). The author states it is 'prescribed' (shurtat) – meaning it is a condition for worship.
Shurtat implies it is wajib as a prerequisite for prayer.
2
Identify the condition that gives it benefit
Sincerity (ikhlas) and purification of the heart from spiritual impurities are described as necessary for the physical purity to benefit in reality.
The phrase 'la yanfa'uhu dhalika haqiqatan' (does not benefit in reality) indicates that without sincerity, the outward act is incomplete.
3
List the spiritual impurities (adnas ma'nawiyyah)
The text explicitly mentions rancor (ghill), deceit (ghish), spite (hiqd), hatred (bughd), and envy (hasad) as examples of spiritual impurities that are more harmful than physical impurity.
These are diseases of the heart that destroy the sincerity of worship.
4
Understand the transformation
The heart must be purified from attachment to anything other than Allah, including desire for Paradise and fear of Hell, to achieve true worship for Allah alone.
This is the station of ihsan – worshipping Allah as if you see Him.
5
See the evidence
The author cites Quran 51:56 ('I did not create jinn and mankind except to worship Me') to prove that the purpose of creation is worship, and it must be sincere.
The verse is a dalil that worship is the ultimate aim, and sincerity is integral to achieving that aim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیه عظیم: شرطت الطهارة الشرعية ليصير العبد أهلاً للعبودية والقيام بخدمة الربوبية، ولا ينفعه ذلك حقيقة، إلا بإخلاص الطوية، وتطهيرها عن الأدناس المعنوية، إذ هي أضر من النجاسة الحقيقية، كالغل والغش والحقد والبغض والحسد ويصلح ,قلبه ليصلح به سائر الجسد، فيطهر قلبه عما سوى الله من الكونين، كون الدنيا والآخرة، بقطع العلائق عن جملة الخلائق، وما تطمح إليه النفوس، فلا يقصد إلا الله، يعبده لاستحقاقه العبادة لذاته تعالى وامتثال أمره، ملاحظاً جلالته وكبرياءه، لا رغبة في جنته، ولا رهبة من نار، بل لأنه تعالى من حقه أن يُعبد، كما قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا خَلَقْتُ الْجِنَّ وَالْإِنسَ إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُونَ ﴾ [الذاريات: ٥٦] فيخلص الطاعة له. ثم يسأله حاجته الدينية والدنيوية، إظهاراً للفاقة، والاضطرار إلى المولى الغني عن كل شيء، بعد تطهيره لسانه مــن اللـغـو، فضلاً عــن الكذب، والغيبة والنميمة، والبهتان، وتزيينه بالتقديس، والتهليل، والتسبيح، وتلاوة القرآن، لعل أن
An important reminder: Ritual purity is prescribed so that the servant becomes worthy of servitude and standing in the service of Lordship, but that does not benefit him in reality except with sincerity of intention and purifying it from spiritual impurities, for they are more harmful than physical impurity, such as rancor, deceit, spite, hatred, and envy. And he reforms his heart so that the rest of his body becomes sound. So he purifies his heart from other than Allah from the two worlds, the world of this life and the hereafter, by cutting attachments from all creatures and what souls aspire to. He intends only Allah, worshiping Him because He deserves worship for His own sake and to obey His command, observing His majesty and grandeur, not desiring His Paradise nor fearing His Fire, but because it is His right to be worshiped, as He said: 'And I did not create the jinn and mankind except to worship Me' (Quran 51:56). So he makes his obedience sincere. Then he asks Him for his religious and worldly needs, showing need and dependence on the Lord who is free of all need, after purifying his tongue from idle talk, let alone lying, backbiting, slander, and falsehood, and adorning it with glorification, declarations of oneness, tasbih, and recitation of the Quran, perhaps that...
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This 'Important Note' (tanbih) refines the concept of purification by linking it to its spiritual purpose. The author states that ritual purity (taharah shariyyah) is prescribed to make the servant fit for worship, but without sincere intention (ikhlas) and purification of the heart from spiritual diseases (like rancor, deceit, envy), physical purity alone is ineffective. The heart must be cleansed of all attachment to this world and the next except for Allah. True worship is for Allah's sake alone, not for reward or fear of punishment, as He is worthy of worship. The verse from Surah al-Dhariyat is cited as evidence. After purifying the heart and tongue, one seeks from Allah both religious and worldly needs, acknowledging complete dependence. This passage is a classical Sufi-oriented exhortation common in Hanafi fiqh works, emphasizing that the outward fiqh rulings are a means to inward spiritual realization.

Key Terms
الطهارة الشرعية (al-taharah al-shariyyah): Ritual purity as prescribed by Islamic law, including wudu and ghusl.
الإخلاص (al-ikhlas): Sincerity of intention in worship, doing deeds solely for Allah.
الأدناس المعنوية (al-adnas al-ma'nawiyyah): Spiritual impurities like envy, hatred, pride etc., which are more harmful than physical najasah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the tanbih, what is the ultimate purpose of ritual purity (taharah shariyyah)?
A) To remove physical impurity
B) To make the servant worthy of servitude and worship with sincerity
C) To avoid punishment in the grave
D) To be accepted by society

Key Takeaway
Ritual purity (taharah) must be accompanied by sincerity of intention and purification of the heart from spiritual diseases; otherwise it does not fulfill its purpose.

Recommended Occasions for Performing Ghusl
Lists occasions when ghusl is recommended (mandub)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the Hanafi recommended occasions for ghusl and explain why they are mandub rather than wajib.

Core Idea
Ghusl is recommended (mandub) for acts of high spiritual significance, not obligatory.

In this lesson, we explore the occasions when the Hanafi school recommends performing a full body wash (ghusl). The text from Nur al-Idah enumerates these instances, linking them to worship, sacred places, natural phenomena, and personal states. Understanding the ruling (mandub vs. wajib) is crucial to applying them correctly in practice.

Guided Path
1
Classify the legal category
Identify the Arabic term 'yundab' (يندب) which indicates the act is recommended (mandub) and not obligatory.
The Hanafi school uses 'mandub' synonymously with sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
2
Extract the occasions and rationales
List each occasion mentioned and note the brief rationale given for its recommendation.
Focus on the connection between the act and complete purification.
3
Identify the underlying principle
Recognize that the common thread is seeking complete purification (akmal al-taharatayn) for acts of worship or moments of spiritual dependency on Allah.
This principle explains why these are recommended but not obligatory.
4
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., entering a mosque for the first time), determine if ghusl is recommended by analogy to the listed occasions.
Consider if the rationale (veneration, complete purification) applies.
5
Distinguish from obligatory ghusl
Explain why these are not wajib or fard, referencing the Hanafi criterion that obligatory acts require a definitive proof (dalil qat'i).
The evidence here is based on general encouragement, not a command.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولدخول مدينة سيدنا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، تعظيماً لها لحرمتها، وقدومه على حضرة المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم، وللوقوف بمزدلفة، لأنه ثاني الجمعين، وفيه غفرت الدماء والمظالم، بدعائه لأمته، واستجاب الله تعالى دعاءه فيها غداة يوم النحر، يعني: بعد طلوع فجر يوم النحر؛ لأنه وقت الوقوف بالمزدلفة، ويخرج قبل طلوع الشمس، وعند دخول مكة، شرفها الله تعالى، ولطواف الزيارة، فيؤدي الفرض بأكمل الطهارتين، ويقوم بتعظيم حرمة المكان، وكذا عند دخولها لأداء نسك، ولصلاة كسوف الشمس وخسوف القمر، لتخويف الله العباد بهما، وأقرب أحوال الابتهال الطهارة الكاملة في الصلاة لهما، واستسقاء لطلب استنزال الغيث رحمة للخلق، بالاستغفار والتضرع، والصلاة بالطهارة الكاملة، وفزع من أي شيء كان التجأ إلى عفو الله وكرمه بالوقوف بين يديه بالذلة والافتقار لكشف الكرب، وظلمة حصلت نهاراً، وريح شديد في أي وقت، لأن الله تعالى أهلك بالريح من طغى كقوم عاد، فيلتجئ الناس إلى الله تعالى، وأقرب أحوالهم الوقوف في الصلاة بأكمل الطهارتين، ويندب للتائب من ذنب، وللقادم من سفر، وللمستحاضة إذا انقطع دمها، ولمن يراد قتله، ولرمي الجمار، ويندب غسل جميع بدنه، أو ثوبه إذا أصابته نجاسة وخفي مكانها.
And for entering the city of our master the Prophet - peace be upon him - as a veneration for its sanctity and his arrival at the presence of the Chosen One - peace be upon him - and for standing at Muzdalifah, because it is the second of the two gatherings, and in it blood debts and injustices were forgiven through his supplication for his nation, and Allah answered his supplication there. On the morning of the Day of Sacrifice, meaning after the dawn of the Day of Sacrifice, because that is the time for standing at Muzdalifah, and one leaves before sunrise. And upon entering Makkah - may Allah honor it - and for the Tawaf al-Ziyarah, so that one performs the obligatory act with the most complete form of purification, and one magnifies the sanctity of the place. Similarly, when entering it to perform a ritual. And for the eclipse prayer of the sun and moon, because Allah frightens His servants with them, and the nearest state of supplication is complete purification in prayer for them. And for the prayer for rain, to seek the sending down of rain as a mercy for creation, through seeking forgiveness and supplication, and prayer with complete purification. And for fear of anything, seeking refuge in Allah's pardon and generosity by standing before Him with humility and need to remove distress. And for darkness occurring during the day. And for a strong wind at any time, because Allah destroyed with the wind those who transgressed like the people of 'Aad, so people seek refuge in Allah, and their nearest state is standing in prayer with the most complete of the two purifications. And it is recommended for the repentant from a sin, for the one coming from a journey, for the mustahadah when her bleeding stops, for the one intended to be killed, and for stoning the jamarat. And it is recommended to wash his entire body, or his garment, if a najasah touches him and its location is hidden.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary on Nur al-Idah, detailing the occasions when performing ghusl (full body ablution) is recommended (mandub). The list includes both spiritual and practical scenarios: entering the sacred cities of Madinah and Makkah, standing at Muzdalifah during Hajj, performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah, eclipse prayers, prayer for rain, moments of fear, natural phenomena like darkness and strong winds, repentance, returning from travel, cessation of istihadah (chronic bleeding), imminent execution, and stoning the jamarat. Additionally, it recommends washing the entire body or garment when a najasah (impurity) is present but its exact location is unknown. Each occasion is justified with a brief rationale, such as veneration, dependence on Allah, or seeking protection. The Hanafi school considers these ghusls as sunnah (recommended), not obligatory, though they are highly meritorious.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Full washing of the body with water with the intention of purification.
يندب (yundab): It is recommended (mandub); an action that is not obligatory but rewarded if performed and not punished if omitted.
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): A place between Makkah and Mina where pilgrims stand after returning from 'Arafah during Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) After eating
B) Before sleeping
C) For entering Makkah
D) After using the restroom

Key Takeaway
Performing ghusl on the recommended occasions is a meritorious sunnah that enhances worship but remains non-obligatory in the Hanafi school.

Taharah — Purification

Inner Purification: The True Purpose of Taharah
Warns that outer purification must be accompanied by inner purity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why outer purification (taharah) must be accompanied by inner purification (ikhlas and moral purity) in the Hanafi tradition, citing the purpose of creation (Quran 51:56).

Core Idea
Physical purification without inner sincerity is futile; true worship requires purifying the heart from all but Allah.

This passage from Imdad al Fattah reminds us that the Shariah's prescription of taharah is not merely about water and dust. It is a means to achieve the ultimate purpose of creation: sincere servitude to Allah. The author warns that without sincerity (ikhlas) and purification from moral vices, the outer purification does not truly benefit the servant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim
The passage states that taharah was stipulated to make the servant worthy of servitude. Recognize that this claim ties legal purification to spiritual purpose.
The Arabic phrase 'ليصير العبد أهلاً للعبودية' is key.
2
Recognize the condition of benefit
The passage specifies that outward purification benefits only 'بإخلاص الطوية وتطهيرها عن الأدناس المعنوية' – with sincerity of intention and purification from moral impurities. Understand that sincerity is a necessary condition for true benefit.
Moral impurities include grudges, deceit, hatred, envy.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
The author quotes Quran 51:56 to establish that the purpose of creation is worship. This verse serves as evidence that all actions, including purification, must be directed towards this end.
The Hanafi school uses this verse to emphasize intention (niyyah) in acts of worship.
4
Understand the spiritual hierarchy
The passage contrasts physical impurities with spiritual impurities, stating the latter are more harmful. Grasp that purifying the heart is more critical than external cleanliness for achieving true servitude.
Refer to the poem by Hasan al-Basri for illustration.
5
Apply the lesson
Conclude that taharah is not an end in itself but a means to cultivate sincere devotion (ikhlas) and detachment from worldly desires, leading to the station of true servitude (ubudiyyah).
The goal is to worship Allah for His sake alone, not for reward or fear.

تنبیه عظیم: شرطت الطهارة الشرعية ليصير العبد أهلاً للعبودية والقيام بخدمة الربوبية، ولا ينفعه ذلك حقيقة، إلا بإخلاص الطوية، وتطهيرها عن الأدناس المعنوية، إذ هي أضر من النجاسة الحقيقية، كالغل والغش والحقد والبغض والحسد ويصلح قلبه ليصلح به سائر الجسد، فيطهر قلبه عما سوى الله من الكونين، كون الدنيا والآخرة، بقطع العلائق عن جملة الخلائق، وما تطمح إليه النفوس، فلا يقصد إلا الله، يعبده لاستحقاقه العبادة لذاته تعالى وامتثال أمره، ملاحظاً جلالته وكبرياءه، لا رغبة في جنته، ولا رهبة من نار، بل لأنه تعالى من حقه أن يعبد، كما قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا خَلَقْتُ الْجِنَّ وَالْإِنسَ إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُونَ﴾ [الذاريات: ٥٦] فيخلص الطاعة له. ثم يسأله حاجته الدينية والدنيوية، إظهاراً للفاقة، والاضطرار إلى المولى الغني عن كل شيء، بعد تطهيره لسانه من اللغو، فضلاً عن الكذب، والغيبة والنميمة، والبهتان، وتزيينه بالتقديس، والتهليل، والتسبيح، وتلاوة القرآن، لعل أن يتصف ببعض صفات العبودية، إذ هي الوفاء بالعهود، والحفظ للحدود، والرضا بالموجود، والصبر المفقود، فتكون فرداً من الأفراد، لا يسترقك شيء من الدنيا، ولا يميلك شيء من الهوى. قال الحسن البصري رحمه الله تعالى ونفعنا ببركته: [من بحر الرمل]
رب مستور سبته شهوته قد عرى من سترها وانهتكا صاحب الشهوة عبد فإذا ملك الشهوة أضحى ملكا
(١) قوله: (رب مستور) أي: كثيراً ما يقع ذلك وهو من الرمل. وقوله: (سبته شهوته) أي: جعلته مسبياً لها وأسيراً والمقصود أنه صار لا يخالفها. قوله: (قد عري) بكسر الراء بمعنى نزع ثيابه والياء ساكنة للضرورة، قوله: ( وانهتكا) ألفه للإطلاق وهو عطف لازم على عري قوله: (صاحب الشهوة عبد ) أي: ملازمها والمتصف بها كالعبد في الانقياد إلى غيره والذل له قوله: (فإذا ملك الشهوة بأن خالف النفس والشيطان فيما يأمران به. قوله. (أضحى ملكاً) أي : في الدارين وهو بكسر اللام لذكر العبد أولاً ويحتمل أن يكون بفتحها وهو على التشبيه يعني: أنه في الدرجة كالملائكة، وقد خلق الله تعالى عالم الأرواح، وقسمه أقساماً ثلاثة: فمنهم من جعل فيه العقل دون الشهوة، وهم الملائكة. ومنهم عكسه وهم البهائم. ومنهم من جمعهما فيه: وهو بنو آدم فإن غلب عقله شهوته ألحق بالأول، بل قد يكون أفضل، وإن غلبت شهوته عقله الحق بالثاني بل قد يكون أرذل إِنْ هُمْ إِلا كَالأَنْعَامِ بَلْ هُمْ أَضَل [الفرقان: ٤٤]. ط.
Important warning: Shariah purification was stipulated so that the servant becomes worthy of servitude and performing the service of lordship, but it does not benefit him in reality except with sincerity of intention and purifying it from moral impurities, for they are more harmful than physical impurity, such as grudges, deception, malice, hatred, and envy. And he should correct his heart so that through it the rest of the body is corrected, so he purifies his heart from other than Allah from the two worlds, the world of this life and the Hereafter, by cutting ties with all creatures and what souls aspire to. So he intends only Allah, worshiping Him because He deserves worship for His essence and obeying His command, observing His majesty and grandeur, not out of desire for Paradise nor fear of Hell, but because it is His right to be worshipped, as Allah said: 'And I did not create the jinn and mankind except to worship Me' [Quran 51:56]. So he devotes obedience to Him. Then he asks Him for his religious and worldly needs, showing need and necessity to the Master who is Rich beyond all need, after purifying his tongue from idle talk, let alone lying, backbiting, slander, and calumny, and adorning it with glorification, declaring His oneness, tasbih, and recitation of the Quran, so that perhaps he may be characterized by some attributes of servitude, which are fulfilling covenants, preserving boundaries, being content with what exists, and patience with what is lost. Then you become an individual among individuals, nothing of this world enslaves you, and nothing of desire inclines you. Al-Hasan al-Basri - may Allah have mercy on him and benefit us through his blessings - said: [in the meter of rajaz] 'Many a concealed person whose desire captivated him, he became stripped of its covering and exposed. The one with desire is a slave; but when he masters desire, he becomes a king.' (Footnote commentary explains the poem.)
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a spiritual admonition (tanbih) within the commentary on Nur al-Idah, emphasizing that the outer purification (taharah) prescribed by the Shariah is not an end in itself but a means to achieve inner purity and true servitude to Allah. The author warns that physical purification is futile without sincerity (ikhlas) and purification of the heart from moral vices like grudges, deception, hatred, and envy. He stresses that the ultimate purpose of creation is worship (Quran 51:56), and this worship must be done solely for Allah's sake, not for Paradise or fear of Hell. The passage includes a poem by Al-Hasan al-Basri illustrating that mastering one's desires elevates a person from slavery to spiritual kingship. The commentary on the poem clarifies the metaphor: a person enslaved by desire is like a stripped captive, while one who controls desire becomes like a king or even angelic. This lesson integrates legal purification with tasawwuf (spiritual purification), showing that Hanafi fiqh is not merely external but deeply connected to inner states.

Key Terms
طهارة شرعية (taharah shar'iyyah): Ritual purification according to Islamic law, including wudu, ghusl, and tayammum.
إخلاص (ikhlas): Sincerity; performing actions solely for the sake of Allah, free from any worldly or selfish motives.
النجاسة المعنوية (al-najasah al-ma'nawiyyah): Spiritual impurity, such as sins and bad character traits, as opposed to physical impurity (najasah hissiyyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Intention (Niyyah) in Tayammum: Why Obligatory?
Explains the first condition of tayammum: intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that intention is fard in tayammum and explain the proof and reasoning behind this obligation.

Core Idea
Earth does not purify by itself; intention makes it a purifier – thus niyyah is fard in tayammum.

Tayammum, the dry ablution, substitutes for wudu when water is absent. But unlike water, earth is not inherently purifying. This lesson explores why intention (niyyah) becomes obligatory in tayammum, based on a clear distinction between the two purifiers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The author states that intention is the first of eight conditions for the validity of tayammum. The ruling is that intention is fard (obligatory).
2
Understand the rationale: earth vs water
Earth is described as inherently impure (najis) and not a purifier (mutahhir) by itself. It only becomes purifying through the intention of a specific act of worship (qurbah). Water, by contrast, was created purifying and cleanses by mere contact.
This distinction follows the principle that the substitute (khalaf) may differ from the original (asl) in some rulings.
3
Define intention and its timing
The legal definition of niyyah is 'the heart's resolve upon performing the action' (عقد القلب على الفعل). Its time is at the moment of striking the hand on the earth.
Definition and timing are taken from the text.
4
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The hadith 'The earth was made for me a mosque and a purification...' is cited. The word 'طهوراً' indicates earth is a purifying agent, but this purification becomes effective through intention, as argued by the author.
The proof is zanni in both transmission and meaning.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dimension
This ruling is mukhtalaf fih: some other schools do not make intention obligatory in tayammum. The Hanafi position is rooted in the inherent nature of earth, distinguishing it from water.
Awareness of difference enriches understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التيمم
يصح بشروط ثمانية: الأوَّلُ: النَّيَّةُ. وحقيقتها: عَقْدُ القلب على الفعل. ووقتها: عندَ ضَرْب يده على ما يَتَيَمَّمُ بِهِ.
باب التيمم
لما فرغ من ذكر الطهارة بالماء، شرع في بيانها بالتيمم، إذ من حق الخلف أن يتبع الأصل، وقدم على مسح الخف، لثبوته بالكتاب)، وذاك بالسنة)، وقد شرع التيمم في غزوة بني المصطلق بالمريسيع، وهو ماء بناحية قديد بين مكة والمدينة المنورة (۳)، وهو من خصائص هذه الأمة. قال : جُعِلَتْ لي الأرض مسجداً وطهوراً أينما أدركتني الصَّلاةُ تيممت وصليت . ولــه سبب، وشرط، وحكم، وركن وصفة، وكيفية. والباب لغة: النوع. وعرفاً نوع من المسائل اشتمل عـلـيـهـا كتـاب، وليست بفصل. والتيمم لغة القصد مطلقاً بخلاف الحج، فإنه القصد إلى معظم، وشرعاً مسح الوجه واليدين عن الصعيد الطاهر ، والقصد شرط لأنه النية. وسبب مشروعيته: نزول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بأصحابه على غير ماء في تلك الغزوة، وقيل: غير ذلك. وسبب وجوبه سبب وجوب أصله المتقدم، وشرطه: كذلك إلا فيما ستعلمه وحكمه: حل ما كان ممتنعاً ،قبله، وركنه استيعاب المحل بالمسح. وصفته: أنه فرض للصلاة مطلقاً. ويندب لدخول المسجد محدثاً، كما ستعلمه، وكيفيته: مسح اليمني باليسرى، وقلبه مستوعباً. ولما كانت الشروط أهم قدم بيانها فقال: (يَصحُ) التيمم (بشروط ثَمَانِيَة) : (الأوَّلُ ) منها: (النَّيَّةُ)، لأن التراب ملوث بذاته، وليس بمطهر بالأصالة، وإنما يصير مطهراً بنية قربة مخصوصة، فلذا كانت النية فيه فرضاً، بخلاف الوضوء ، لأن الماء خلق مطهراً، فإذا أصاب المحل طهره، وقد يفارق الخلف الأصل لاختلاف حالهما، ألا ترى أن الوضوء بأربعة أعضاء، وهـو باثنين منها، ويسن التكرار في الوضوء لا فيه (وَحَقِيقتُهَا)، أي: النية شرعاً، (عَقْدُ القَلْبِ عَلَى) إيجاد (الفعل) جزماً، وتقدم الكلام عليها في سنن الوضوء. ووقتها : عندَ ضَرْبِ يَدِهِ عَلَى مَا يَتَيَمَّمُ بِهِ)
Chapter of Tayammum. It is valid with eight conditions: the first: intention. Its reality: the heart's resolve upon the action. Its time: at the striking of his hand upon that with which he performs tayammum. Chapter of Tayammum. When he finished mentioning purification with water, he began explaining it by tayammum, for it is the right of the successor to follow the original, and he gave precedence over wiping the khuff because it [tayammum] is established by the Book, and that [wiping] by the Sunnah. Tayammum was legislated in the campaign of Banu al-Mustaliq at al-Muraysi', which is water in the region of Qudayd between Mecca and Medina, and it is a characteristic of this nation. He (ﷺ) said: 'The earth was made for me a mosque and a purification; wherever the prayer overtakes me, I perform tayammum and pray.' It has a cause, condition, ruling, pillar, description, and modality. 'Bab' linguistically: a type. Technically: a type of issues that a book comprises, not a chapter. Tayammum linguistically: absolute intent, unlike hajj which is intent towards a venerated place. Technically: wiping the face and hands with pure earth; and intent is a condition because it is the intention. The cause of its legislation: the Prophet's (ﷺ) descent with his companions at a place without water in that campaign, and it is said other than that. The cause of its obligation is the cause of the obligation of its original mentioned earlier, and its condition likewise except what you will learn. Its ruling: permitting what was prohibited before it. Its pillar: encompassing the area with wiping. Its description: it is a duty for prayer absolutely. It is recommended for entering the mosque in a state of minor impurity, as you will learn. Its modality: wiping the right [hand] with the left, turning it over, encompassing. Since the conditions were most important, he began their explanation, saying: Tayammum is valid (with eight conditions: the first of them: intention), because earth is inherently impure and not purifying originally, but becomes purifying by the intention of a specific act of worship. Hence intention was obligatory in it, unlike wudu', because water was created purifying, so when it touches the limb it purifies it. And the successor may differ from the original due to difference of their states; do you not see that wudu' has four limbs, while this has two of them, and repetition is recommended in wudu' but not in it. And its reality (i.e., intention legally) is the heart's resolve upon performing the action decisively, and discussion on this preceded in the sunan of wudu'. And its time: at the striking of his hand upon that with which he performs tayammum.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the first condition of tayammum: intention. The author begins by listing the eight conditions of tayammum, stating that the first is intention. He then provides a detailed commentary on why intention is required: earth is inherently impure (najis) and not purifying in itself; it becomes a purifier only through the intention of a specific act of worship. This differs from wudu' because water is created as a purifier—it purifies by contact regardless of intention. This distinction follows the Hanafi principle that the substitute (khalaf) may differ from the original (asl) in some rulings, as seen also in the number of limbs (four in wudu', two in tayammum) and the non-recommendation of repetition in tayammum. The definition of intention (niyyah) is given as the heart's resolve to perform the action, and its time is at the moment of striking the hands on the earth. The author also provides background on the legislation of tayammum in the campaign of Banu al-Mustaliq and cites the hadith making the earth a mosque and purification. This passage is an expansion probe that clarifies the first condition with proofs from the Quran (implied) and Sunnah.

Key Terms
النِّيَّةُ (an-niyyah): The heart's resolve upon performing the action of tayammum; a condition (shart) for its validity.
التَّيَمُّمُ (at-tayammum): Linguistically: absolute intent. Technically: wiping the face and hands with pure earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
الصَّعِيدُ (as-saʿīd): Pure earth (turab tahir) that can be used for tayammum; it includes anything that grows from the earth or is dust-like.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is intention (niyyah) obligatory in tayammum but not in wudu according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because water is pure by itself, while earth is not.
B) Because tayammum is a substitute and therefore requires intention.
C) Because the Prophet (ﷺ) specifically commanded intention for tayammum.
D) Because earth is inherently purifying, unlike water.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, intention (niyyah) is obligatory (fard) in tayammum because earth does not purify by itself; it only does so through the intention of an act of worship.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The Intention (Niyyah) for Tayammum: Conditions and Specifics
Explains the first condition of Tayammum: intention, its definition, timing, and sub-conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions and timing of intention in Tayammum, and apply the three valid intentions that permit prayer.

Core Idea
Intention in Tayammum is a duty because earth is not purifying; it must be for an act requiring purification.

In this passage, the commentator unpacks the first condition of Tayammum: intention (niyyah). He explains why intention is required, when it must occur, and what makes it valid for prayer. Understanding these details is crucial because Tayammum, unlike wudu, is a dispensation that only becomes effective through proper intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The passage states that intention is a condition for Tayammum because earth is not inherently purifying. Note the Quranic proof (5:6) and the hadith about the earth as a purifier.
This establishes the fard status of intention.
2
Understand the definition and timing
Intention is defined as the heart's resolve on the action, and its time is at the moment of striking the hands on the earth. This timing is specific to Tayammum.
Compare with wudu where intention is recommended at the start.
3
List the three general conditions of any intention
The passage specifies: Islam, discrimination (tamyiz), and knowledge of what is intended. These apply to all intentions in worship.
Non-Muslims cannot attain reward; the insane lack valid intention.
4
Apply the three valid intentions for Tayammum
For Tayammum to permit prayer, the intention must be one of: purification from hadath, permission for prayer (istibahah), or a purposeful act of worship that requires purification (e.g., prayer, funeral prayer, sujood al-tilawah, reading Quran while junub).
Intending only Tayammum without linking to a permissible act invalidates it for prayer.
5
Identify invalid intentions
If one intends only Tayammum, or intends it for reading Quran while in minor hadath (which is permissible anyway), the Tayammum does not permit prayer because the intended act does not require purification.
The intention must align with an act that necessitates wudu or ghusl.
