باب التيمم
يصح بشروط ثمانية: الأوَّلُ: النَّيَّةُ. وحقيقتها: عَقْدُ القلب على الفعل. ووقتها: عندَ ضَرْب يده على ما يَتَيَمَّمُ به.
باب التيمم
لما فرغ من ذكر الطهارة بالماء، شرع في بيانها بالتيمم، إذ من حق الخلف أن يتبع الأصل، وقدم على مسح الخف، لثبوته بالكتاب، وذاك بالسنة، وقد شرع التيمم في غزوة بني المصطلق بالمريسيع، وهو ماء بناحية قديد بين مكة والمدينة المنورة، وهو من خصائص هذه الأمة. قال : جُعِلَتْ لي الأرض مسجداً وطهوراً أينما أدركتني الصَّلاةُ تيممت وصليت . ولــه سبب، وشرط، وحكم، وركن وصفة، وكيفية. والباب لغة: النوع. وعرفاً نوع من المسائل اشتمل عـلـيـهـا كتـاب، وليست بفصل. والتيمم لغة القصد مطلقاً بخلاف الحج، فإنه القصد إلى معظم، وشرعاً مسح الوجه واليدين عن الصعيد الطاهر ، والقصد شرط لأنه النية. وسبب مشروعيته: نزول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بأصحابه على غير ماء في تلك الغزوة، وقيل: غير ذلك. وسبب وجوبه سبب وجوب أصله المتقدم، وشرطه: كذلك إلا فيما ستعلمه وحكمه: حل ما كان ممتنعاً ،قبله، وركنه استيعاب المحل بالمسح. وصفته: أنه فرض للصلاة مطلقاً. ويندب لدخول المسجد محدثاً، كما ستعلمه، وكيفيته: مسح اليمني باليسرى، وقلبه مستوعباً. ولما كانت الشروط أهم قدم بيانها فقال: (يَصحُ) التيمم (بشروط ثَمَانِيَة) : (الأوَّلُ ) منها: (النَّيَّةُ)، لأن التراب ملوث بذاته، وليس بمطهر بالأصالة، وإنما يصير مطهراً بنية قربة مخصوصة، فلذا كانت النية فيه فرضاً، بخلاف الوضوء ، لأن الماء خلق مطهراً، فإذا أصاب المحل طهره، وقد يفارق الخلف الأصل لاختلاف حالهما، ألا ترى أن الوضوء بأربعة أعضاء، وهـو باثنين منها، ويسن التكرار في الوضوء لا فيه (وَحَقِيقتُهَا)، أي: النية شرعاً، (عَقْدُ القَلْبِ عَلَى) إيجاد (الفعل) جزماً، وتقدم الكلام عليها في سنن الوضوء. ووقتها : عندَ ضَرْبِ يَدِهِ عَلَى مَا يَتَيَمَّمُ بِهِ)،
(۱) وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿ فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً فَتَيَمَّمُوا ﴾ [المائدة: ٦ ]. (۲) انظر التعليق التالي. (۳) شرع التيمم في غزوة المريسيع، وهو بناحية قديد بين مكة والمدينة، وهـي غزوة بني المصطلق، لما أضـلـت عائشة عقدها، فبعث رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في طلبه، فحانت الصلاة، وليس معهم ماء، فأغلظ أبــو بـكــره علـى عائشة وقال: حبست رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم والمسلمين على غير ماء، فنزلت: ﴿فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيداً طيباً [المائدة: ٦ ]، فجاء أسيد بن حضير فجعل يقول: ما أكثر بركتكم يا آل أبي بكر، وفي رواية يرحمك الله يا عائشة، ما نزل بك أمـر تكرهينه إلا جعل الله للمسلمين فيه فرجاً. أخرجه البخاري في التيمم (٣٣٦)، وأبو داود في الطهارة (٣١٧). (٤) أخرجه البخاري في الصلاة، باب : قول النبي : جعلت لي الأرض مسجداً) (٤٣٨).

وشروط صحة النية ثلاثة: الإسلام، والتمييز، والعلم بما ينويه. ويُشترط لصحة نيةِ التَّيْمُمِ للصَّلاة به أحد ثلاثة أشياء: إمّا نِيَّةُ الطَّهارة، أو استباحة الصلاة، أو نية عبادة مقصودة لا تصح بدون طهارة، فلا يصلي به إذا نوى التيمم فقط، أو نواه لقراءة القرآن، ولم يكن جُنُباً..
مسح
أو عند أعضائه بتراب أصابها. ولما كان للنية شروط في حد ذاتها بينها بقوله: (وَشُرُوطُ صِحَّةِ النية ثلاثة: الإسلام)؛ لأن النية تُصَيِّر الفعل منتهضاً سبباً للثواب، ولا يقع فعل من الكافر كذلك، لعدم أهليته للثواب. (وَ) الثاني: (التَّمييز ) لأن غير المميز وإن نطق بكلام، فهو لا يفهم معناه. (و) الثالث: ( العِلْمُ بِمَا يَنْوِيهِ)؛ لأن النية معنى وراء العلم فيشترط سبق علمه بالمنوي، ولما كانت النية في التيمم مفتقرة إلى شرط خاص بها، بينه بقوله: (ويُشترط لصحة نية التيمم)، ليكون مفتاحاً للصَّلاةِ) فتصح (به أحد ثلاثة أشياء: إمّا نيّةُ الطَّهارة من الحدث أو الجنابة، ولا يشترط التعيين الجنابة والحدث، في الصحيح، وإنما اكتفى بنية التطهير، لأن الطهارة شرعت للصلاة، وشرطت بين لإباحتها، فكانت نيتها نية إباحة الصلاة. فلذا قال: ( أوِ اسْتِبَاحَةُ الصَّلاة)، لأنها برفع الحدث د، فتصح بإطلاق النية، وأما إذا قيد النية بشيء، فلابد وأن يكون خاصاً، أشار إليه في الشرط الثالث بقوله: أوْ نَيَّةُ عِبَادَةٍ مَقْصُودَةٍ)، وهي التي لا تجب في ضمن شيء آخر بطريق التبعية، فتكـــون قـد شـرعـت ابتداء تقرباً إلى الله تعالى، وتكون أيضاً ( لا تَصُحُ بِدُونِ طَهَارَةٍ)، فيكون المنوي إمــا صـلاة أو جزءاً للصلاة في حد ذاته، كقوله: نويت التيمم للصلاة، أو لصلاة الجنازة أو سجدة التلاوة، أو لقراءة القرآن وهو جنب، أو نوثه لقراءة القرآن بعد انقطاع حيضها أو نفاسها، فإن كلا منها قربة مقصودة بذاتها، متوقفة على الطهارة، أما الصلاة فظاهر، وأما غيرها فلأنه كالصلاة، لكونه جزءاً لها، وصلاة الجنازة صلاة من وجه، وسجود التلاوة من جنس أركان الصلاة، فنيتها كنيتها، (فَلا يُصَلِّي بِهِ) أي: التيمم، ( إذا نَوى التّيمُّمَ فَقَط)، أي: من غير ملاحظة كونه للصلاة ونحوها، مـن عـبـادة مقصودة، لا تصح بدون طهارة، لأن التيمم ليس عبادة في ذاته، أو نواه)، أي: التيمم (لقِرَاءةِ القُرْآن وَ) هو محدث حدثاً أصغر ولمْ يَكُنْ جُنُباً)، كما لو نوته للقراءة، ولم تكن مخاطبة بالاغتسال مــن حـيـض أو نفاس، فإذا نوى المحدث التيمم للقراءة لا يصلي به لجواز قراءته مع الحدث الأصغر، لـفــوات أحد الشرطين، وهو كون المنوي صلاة أو جزءاً لها، مع الطهارة الخاصة في نيته، وهي منعدمة، ولذا لو تيمم هو، أو الجنب، لمس المصحف أو دخول المسجد لا تصح به الصلاة، في الصحيح، لأن المس والدخول ليس من أركان الصلاة، فلا تصير نيته كنيتها، وكذا لو تيمم لتعليم الغير، لا تجوز
Chapter of Tayammum. It is valid with eight conditions: the first is intention. Its reality: the heart's resolve on the action. Its time: when he strikes his hand on what he performs tayammum with. Chapter of Tayammum. When he finished mentioning purification with water, he began explaining it by tayammum, for the successor should follow the original. He gave it precedence over wiping the khuff because it is established by the Book, and that by the Sunnah. Tayammum was legislated in the expedition of Banu al-Mustaliq at al-Muraysi', which is water in the area of Qadid between Makkah and Madinah. It is a special characteristic of this ummah. He said: 'The earth was made for me a mosque and a purifier, wherever prayer overtakes me I perform tayammum and pray.' It has a cause, condition, ruling, pillar, description, and manner. 'Bab' linguistically: type. Conventionally: a category of issues that a book comprises, not a chapter. Tayammum linguistically: absolute intent, unlike hajj which is intent toward a venerated object. Legally: wiping the face and hands with pure earth; intent is a condition because it is the intention. The cause of its legislation: the Prophet's descent with his companions without water in that expedition, and it is said otherwise. The cause of its obligation: the cause of the obligation of its original as previously mentioned. Its condition: likewise except what you will learn. Its ruling: making permissible what was forbidden before it. Its pillar: covering the area with wiping. Its description: that it is a duty for prayer absolutely. It is recommended for entering the mosque in a state of hadath, as you will learn. Its manner: wiping the right with the left, turning it over while covering. Since the conditions are most important, he gave precedence to explaining them and said: (It is valid) tayammum (with eight conditions): (the first of them): (the intention), because earth is intrinsically impure, not originally purifying; it becomes purifying only by an intention of a specific act of worship, so intention in it is a duty, unlike wudu, because water is created purifying; when it touches a place it purifies it. The successor may differ from the original due to their differing states. Do you not see that wudu has four limbs, and it has two of them, and repetition is sunnah in wudu but not in it. (And its reality), i.e., intention legally, (is the heart's resolve on) performing (the action) decisively. The discussion on it has preceded in the sunan of wudu. (And its time: when he strikes his hand on what he performs tayammum with). (1) And it is His saying: 'Then if you do not find water, perform tayammum' [al-Ma'idah: 6]. (2) See the following note. (3) Tayammum was legislated in the expedition of al-Muraysi', which is in the area of Qadid between Makkah and Madinah, and it is the expedition of Banu al-Mustaliq, when A'ishah lost her necklace, so the Messenger of Allah sent people in search of it, and the time for prayer came, and they had no water. Abu Bakr spoke harshly to A'ishah and said: 'You have detained the Messenger of Allah and the Muslims without water.' So the verse was revealed: 'Perform tayammum with pure earth' [al-Ma'idah: 6]. Then Usayd ibn Hudayr came and kept saying: 'How great is your blessing, O family of Abu Bakr!' In another narration: 'May Allah have mercy on you, O A'ishah, no matter happens to you that you dislike except that Allah makes a relief for the Muslims in it.' Narrated by al-Bukhari in Tayammum (336) and Abu Dawud in Taharah (317). (4) Narrated by al-Bukhari in Prayer, Chapter: The Prophet's saying: 'The earth was made for me a mosque' (438). -112- [PAGE_114] And the conditions for the validity of the intention are three: Islam, discrimination, and knowledge of what he intends. And for the validity of the intention of tayammum for prayer with it, one of three things is required: either the intention of purification, or permission for prayer, or the intention of a purposeful act of worship that is not valid without purification. So he does not pray with it if he intends only tayammum, or he intends it for reading the Qur'an while not being junub. Wiping or on his limbs with dust that touched them. Since the intention has conditions in itself, he explained them by his saying: (And the conditions for the validity of the intention are three: Islam), because the intention makes the action effective as a cause for reward, and the action of a disbeliever is not so, due to his lack of eligibility for reward. (And) the second: (discrimination), because the non-discerning person, even if he utters words, does not understand their meaning. (And) the third: (knowledge of what he intends), because the intention is a meaning beyond knowledge, so prior knowledge of the intended is required. Since the intention in tayammum requires a specific condition, he explained it by his saying: (And it is required for the validity of the intention of tayammum), to be a key for prayer, so it is valid with it (one of three things: either the intention of purification from hadath or janabah, and specification of janabah or hadath is not required according to the correct view; he is satisfied with the intention of purification because purification is legislated for prayer and is prescribed for its permission, so its intention is the intention of permitting prayer. Therefore he said: (or the permission of prayer), because it lifts the hadath, so it is valid with absolute intention. But if he restricts the intention to something, it must be specific. He indicated this in the third condition by his saying: (or the intention of a purposeful act of worship), which is not obligatory within something else by way of subordination, but is legislated initially as an approach to Allah, and also (is not valid without purification). So the intended is either prayer or a part of prayer in itself, such as his saying: I intend tayammum for prayer, or for the funeral prayer or the prostration of recitation, or for reading the Qur'an while junub, or she intends it for reading the Qur'an after the cessation of her menses or postpartum bleeding, for each of these is a purposeful act of worship in itself, dependent on purification. As for prayer, it is apparent; as for others, because it is like prayer, being a part of it. The funeral prayer is prayer in a sense, and the prostration of recitation is akin to the pillars of prayer, so its intention is like its intention. (So he does not pray with it), i.e., with tayammum, (if he intends only tayammum), i.e., without considering it for prayer or the like of a purposeful act of worship that is not valid without purification, because tayammum is not an act of worship in itself. (Or he intends it), i.e., tayammum, (for reading the Qur'an while) he is in minor hadath and is not junub), as if he intends it for reading while not being addressed with ghusl from menses or postpartum bleeding. So if the one in minor hadath intends tayammum for reading, he does not pray with it because it is permissible for him to read with minor hadath, due to the loss of one of the two conditions: that the intended is prayer or a part of it, with the specific purification in his intention, which is absent. Therefore, if he, or the junub, performs tayammum for touching the mushaf or entering the mosque, prayer with it is not valid, according to the correct view, because touching and entering are not among the pillars of prayer, so his intention does not become like its intention. Similarly, if he performs tayammum for teaching others, it is not permissible.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Nur al-Idah, opening the chapter on Tayammum (dry ablution). The author begins by listing the eight conditions for the validity of Tayammum, starting with the most important: intention (niyyah). He explains that Tayammum is a special dispensation for this ummah, established by the Qur'an (5:6) and the hadith that the earth was made a mosque and a purifier. The intention is a duty (fard) in Tayammum because earth is not inherently purifying; it becomes so only by intending a specific act of worship, unlike water which is created purifying. The definition of intention is the heart's resolve on the action, and its time is at the moment of striking the hands on the earth. The author then delves into the conditions for the validity of the intention itself: Islam (because only a Muslim's intention makes an act worthy of reward), discrimination (tamyiz, i.e., sanity and comprehension), and knowledge of what one intends (one must know what act one is performing). For Tayammum to permit prayer, the intention must be one of three: (1) purification from hadath (minor or major), (2) seeking permission for prayer (istibahah al-salah), or (3) a purposeful act of worship that requires purification, such as prayer itself, funeral prayer, prostration of recitation, or reading the Qur'an while in a state of janabah. If one intends only Tayammum without any reference to a permissible act, or intends it for reading the Qur'an while only in minor hadath (since that is permissible), then prayer with that Tayammum is invalid. The reasoning is that Tayammum is not an end in itself; it is a means to an end (prayer or equivalent acts). The author emphasizes that the intention must align with a valid purpose that requires purification.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intention; the heart's resolve on performing an action. In Tayammum, it is a condition that must be present at the moment of striking the hands.
تيمم (tayammum): Legally: wiping the face and hands with pure earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
استباحة الصلاة (istibahah al-salah): Seeking permission for prayer; this is a valid intention for Tayammum, meaning the person intends to make prayer permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the three general conditions for the validity of any intention (niyyah) according to this passage?
A) Islam, adulthood, and knowledge of the act
B) Islam, discrimination (tamyiz), and knowledge of what is intended
C) Purity, facing the qiblah, and time
D) Sincerity, mindfulness, and saying the intention aloud

Key Takeaway
Intention in Tayammum is a fard condition; it must be for purification, permission for prayer, or a purposeful act of worship that requires purification, or else the Tayammum is invalid for prayer.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Conditions for Valid Intention in Tayammum
Explains general conditions of intention and specific intentions validating tayammum for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three general conditions of intention, list the three specific intentions that validate tayammum for prayer, and apply the Hanafi position that tayammum for entering Islam does not permit prayer.

Core Idea
Tayammum is not an act of worship in itself; it requires an intention linked to a worship that needs purification.

When performing tayammum, the intention (niyyah) must meet both general conditions and a specific condition linking it to prayer or an equivalent act. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies those conditions and the dispute regarding tayammum for entering Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify general conditions for intention
The text states three prerequisites for any valid intention: being Muslim (Islam), possessing discernment (tamyiz), and knowing what one intends (al-ilm bima yanwihi). Each condition is justified: Islam is needed because intention makes an act a cause for reward; discernment ensures understanding; knowledge is a prerequisite for meaning.
These apply to all worship acts in Hanafi fiqh.
2
List the three specific intentions for tayammum
For tayammum to permit prayer, the intention must be one of: (1) purification (taharah) from hadath, (2) permission of prayer (istibahah al-salah), or (3) a specific worship that requires purification (e.g., prayer, funeral prayer, prostration of recitation, Quran recitation for a junub). The text explains that tayammum is valid with absolute intention of purification because purification is a condition for prayer.
Hanafis do not require specification of minor vs. major impurity.
3
Understand why mere tayammum intention fails
Intending only tayammum, or tayammum for an act that does not require purification (e.g., Quran recitation for non-junub), does not make prayer valid. The reason is that tayammum is a means, not a worship in itself; it must be directed toward an end that necessitates purification.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on entering Islam
Abu Yusuf holds that tayammum for entering Islam suffices for prayer because Islam is the greatest worship. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad disagree, citing the hadith 'al-turāb ṭahūr al-muslim' (earth is the purification of the Muslim), which restricts tayammum to those already Muslim. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
This shows how a hadith restricts a ruling established contrary to analogy (khilaf al-qiyas).
5
Apply the rules to other borderline cases
Tayammum for teaching, visiting graves, adhan, greeting, etc., does not permit prayer because those acts do not require purification for their validity. The text mentions these as examples.
Two nawadir narrations suggest that mere intention of tayammum may suffice, but the relied-upon position is stricter.

جزءاً لها، مع الطهارة الخاصة في نيته، وهي منعدمة، ولذا لو تيمم هو، أو الجنب، لمس المصحف أو دخول المسجد لا تصح به الصلاة، في الصحيح، لأن المس والدخول ليس من أركان الصلاة، فلا تصير نيته كنيتها، وكذا لو للصلاة، لعدم صحتها منه في الحال، ولم يعتبره أبو حنيفة، ومحمد لإسلامه، وهو الأصح، لقوله : ( التراب طهور المسلم ) جعله طهوره، فيقتصر عليه لثبوتـه، عـلـى خـلاف القياس، ولو تيمم لسجدة الشكر، لا يصلي به، And the conditions for the validity of intention are three: Islam, discernment, and knowledge of what one intends. And for the validity of the intention of tayammum for prayer, one of three things is required: either the intention of purification, or the permission of prayer, or the intention of an intended worship that is not valid without purification. So one does not pray with it if he intended only tayammum, or intended it for reciting the Quran while not being in a state of major impurity. And when intention has conditions in itself, he explained them by his saying: (And the conditions for the validity of intention are three: Islam) because intention makes the act a cause for reward, and no act of the disbeliever occurs as such, due to his lack of eligibility for reward. (And) the second: (discernment) because the non-discerning person, even if he utters words, does not understand their meaning. (And) the third: (knowledge of what one intends) because intention is a meaning beyond knowledge, so prior knowledge of the intended is required. And when the intention in tayammum is in need of a special condition, he explained it by his saying: (And it is required for the validity of the intention of tayammum) to be a key for prayer, so it is valid with it (one of three things: either the intention of purification from minor or major impurity, and specification of minor or major is not required in the correct view, and he sufficed with the intention of purification because purification is legislated for prayer and is a condition for its permissibility, so its intention is the intention of permitting prayer. Therefore he said: (or the permission of prayer) because it removes the impurity, so it is valid with absolute intention. But if he restricts the intention to something, then it must be specific, indicated by him in the third condition by his saying: (or the intention of an intended worship) which is not obligatory within something else by way of subordination, and it is legislated initially as an act of drawing near to Allah, and it is also (not valid without purification), so the intended is either prayer or a part of prayer in itself, like his saying: I intend tayammum for prayer, or for funeral prayer, or for the prostration of recitation, or for reciting the Quran while in major impurity, or intending it for reciting the Quran after the cessation of menstruation or postpartum bleeding, for each of these is an intended act of worship in itself, dependent on purification. As for prayer, it is apparent; as for others, they are like prayer because they are part of it, and funeral prayer is a prayer in some respects, and the prostration of recitation is from the kind of the pillars of prayer, so its intention is like its intention. (So he does not pray with it), i.e., tayammum, (if he intended only tayammum), i.e., without regard to it being for prayer and the like, from intended worship that is not valid without purification, because tayammum is not a worship in itself. (Or), i.e., tayammum, (he intended it for reciting the Quran, and) he is in minor impurity and not in major impurity, as if he intended it for recitation and was not addressed with ghusl from menstruation or postpartum. So if the one in minor impurity intends tayammum for recitation, he does not pray with it because recitation is permissible with minor impurity, due to the loss of one of the two conditions: that the intended be a prayer or part of it, with the specific purity in his intention, which is absent. So likewise, if he, or the one in major impurity, makes tayammum for touching the Mushaf or entering the mosque, prayer is not valid with it, in the correct view, because touching and entering are not from the pillars of prayer, so his intention does not become like its intention. Similarly, if he makes tayammum for teaching others, prayer is not valid with it in the most correct view, and likewise for visiting graves, the call to prayer and iqamah, and returning the greeting, like the greeting or entering Islam, prayer is not valid with it according to the generality of the mashayikh, because it is not part of prayer, and its validity does not depend on purification, even if it is an intended worship. And Abu Yusuf said: His prayer is valid with his tayammum for entering Islam, because he intended an intended act of worship that is valid from him immediately, so his tayammum is valid, since Islam is the head of acts of worship, and all others are considered by it, unlike the tayammum of a disbeliever for prayer, due to its lack of validity from him immediately. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad did not consider it for Islam, and it is the most correct, because of his saying: (The earth is the purification of the Muslim) He made it his purification, so it is restricted to that due to its being established contrary to analogy. And if he makes tayammum for the prostration of thanks, he does not pray with it, contrary to Muhammad, because it is an act of worship according to him, not according to them. We will mention the difference in it, Allah willing. And it is narrated in al-Nawadir: that if he wipes his face and arms intending tayammum, prayer is permitted with it. And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa regarding one who makes tayammum for returning the greeting: it is permissible. According to these two narrations, mere intention of tayammum is considered.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage breaks down the conditions for a valid intention (niyyah) in tayammum. The author first states the three general conditions for any intention in Islamic law: the person must be Muslim, have discernment (tamyiz), and know what he intends. For tayammum specifically, the intention must be one of three: to achieve purification (taharah), to permit prayer (istibahah al-salah), or to perform a specific act of worship that is not valid without purification (like prayer, funeral prayer, prostration of recitation, or reciting Quran while in major impurity). This is because tayammum is not a worship in itself but a means to an end. The commentary then elaborates on each condition, using the matn as a framework. It clarifies that if one intends only tayammum itself, or intends it for an act that does not require purification (like Quran recitation when not junub), prayer becomes invalid with that tayammum. The passage then addresses borderline cases: tayammum for teaching, visiting graves, adhan, iqamah, returning greetings, or entering Islam. Regarding entering Islam, Abu Yusuf holds that tayammum validifies prayer because Islam is the greatest act of worship, but Abu Hanifa and Muhammad disagree because the hadith restricts tayammum to Muslims. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. The passage ends with two nawadir narrations suggesting that mere intention of tayammum may suffice.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention that distinguishes acts of worship from habits; here, it must be present for tayammum to be valid.
تمييز (tamyīz): The ability to distinguish between good and bad, typically reached at age 7; a condition for valid intention.
استباحة الصلاة (istibāḥat al-ṣalāh): Intention to make prayer permissible by removing ritual impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Tayammum for prayer requires the intention to be purification, permission of prayer, or a specific worship needing purification; mere tayammum or intentions for permissible acts do not suffice.

The Mile As an Excuse for Tayammum: Juristic Determination of Distance
Defines the mile and settles the relied-upon distance for tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the distance that permits tayammum, identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position, and explain the basis of ghalabat al-zann in estimating the distance.

Core Idea
Tayammum is permitted when water is at least a mile away, estimated by strong presumption, not certainty.

The second condition for the validity of tayammum is the existence of a valid excuse. One such excuse is the distance to water. In this passage, the author of Nur al-Idah defines the mile and discusses the differing opinions within the Hanafi school on the exact distance. The chosen position is one mile, based on the principle of hardship (mashaqqah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the excuse and its proof
The passage states that distance from water is an excuse. The standard for estimating distance is ghalabat al-zann (strong presumption), not certainty.
This is because exact measurement is often impossible in travel.
2
Define the mile in classical terms
A mile is one-third of a farsakh (farsakh = 12,000 steps, each step = 1.5 common cubits = 24 fingers). It is also described as the limit of eyesight.
This definition is rooted in Arab custom and landmarks on the Mecca road.
3
Record the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad has two narrations: one mile or two miles. Abu Hanifa reportedly said two miles if water is ahead, otherwise one mile. Another opinion ties it to shouting distance.
None of these are from Zahir al-Riwayah, which sets no fixed limit.
4
Recognize the mufta bihi position
The text declares 'al-mīl huwa al-mukhtār' (the mile is the chosen opinion). The majority of later mashayikh adopt one mile as the operative ruling.
This avoids excessive strictness while still requiring hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني: العُدْرُ المُبيحُ للتّيمم، كبُعْدِهِ مِيلاً . والمعتبر غلبة الظن في تقديره به، لأنها كتحقق بعده ميلاً، والميل في كلام العرب منتهى مد البصر، وقيل للأعلام المبنية في طريق مكة أميال؛ لأنها بنيت على مقادير منتهى مد البصر، والمراد هنا: ثلث الفرسخ ، والفرسخ : اثنا عشر [ ألف ] خطوة، وهي ذراع ونصف بذراع العامة)، وهو : أربع وعشرون إصبعاً بعدد حروف لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله ، والتقدير بالميل هو المختار؛ لأنه لم يذكر في ظاهر الروايـة حــداً في حالـة الـعـلـم بـه، فقدره محمد في رواية بميل ، وفي أخرى بميلين، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه ميلان إن كان أمامه، وإلا فميل، وقيل: بما لو صاح بأعلى صوته لم يسمعه أهل الماء، والميل هو المختار، لأنه يتحقق
The second: the excuse that permits tayammum, such as one being a mile away. And what is considered is the preponderance of opinion in estimating it, because it is like certainty of being a mile away. And a mile in the speech of the Arabs is the limit of eyesight, and it is said that the landmarks built on the road to Mecca are miles because they were built at distances of the limit of eyesight. And what is meant here is one-third of a farsakh. And a farsakh is twelve thousand steps, and it is one and a half cubits of the common cubit, and that is twenty-four fingers, according to the number of letters of 'la ilaha illa Allah Muhammad Rasul Allah'. And estimation by the mile is the chosen opinion because a limit is not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah in the case of knowledge of it, so Muhammad estimated it in one narration as a mile, and in another as two miles. And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that it is two miles if the water is in front of him, otherwise one mile. And it is said: as if he shouted at the top of his voice and the people of the water did not hear him. And the mile is the chosen opinion, because it is confirmed.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage addresses the second condition for the validity of tayammum: the existence of a valid excuse that permits it, specifically the distance to water. The ruling is that if water is a mile away, and one has a strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) that it is that far, tayammum is allowed. The author defines a mile in classical terms: the distance at which one's eyesight ends, roughly one-third of a farsakh (a farsakh being about 12,000 steps or 1.5 common cubits, i.e., 24 fingers). There is disagreement among the Hanafi imams about the exact distance: Muhammad al-Shaybani has two narrations—one mile or two miles; Abu Hanifa reportedly said two miles if water is ahead, otherwise one mile; another opinion ties it to the distance where one cannot hear a shout from the water source. The chosen opinion (al-mukhtar) is one mile, as it is the most consistently reported and leaves no other alternative. This passage emphasizes that tayammum is a concession (rukhsah) limited to circumstances of genuine hardship.

Key Terms
عذر (ʻudhr): A valid excuse that permits performing tayammum instead of wudu or ghusl.
ميل (mīl): A unit of distance equivalent to the limit of eyesight, approximately 1.86 km or one-third of a farsakh.
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-ẓann): Preponderance of opinion; the standard for estimating distance in the absence of certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon distance that excuses one from using water according to the Hanafi school in this passage?
A) Two farsakhs
B) One mile
C) Two miles when water is behind
D) The distance one can shout

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a distance of one mile (approximately 1.86 km) permits tayammum, estimated by strong presumption.

Tayammum for Non-Salah Acts: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum's scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tayammum for acts other than obligatory prayer and explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding entering Islam and prostration of thanksgiving.

Core Idea
Tayammum is only valid for prayer; Abu Yusuf's view that it suffices for entering Islam is overruled by the hadith.

This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Idah addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: is tayammum valid for acts other than salah, such as returning a greeting or entering Islam? The majority view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad restricts tayammum to prayer, based on the hadith 'Earth is the purifier of the Muslim.' Abu Yusuf argues that tayammum for entering Islam is valid because Islam is the head of worship. We will examine the proofs and the practical consequences of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and the primary ruling
The passage lists acts such as visiting graves, adhan, iqamah, returning greetings, and entering Islam. The general ruling according to 'most scholars' is that tayammum is not valid for these acts because they are not part of prayer and do not require ritual purity.
Note that the ruling applies to acts that are not themselves acts of worship requiring purification.
2
Locate Abu Yusuf's objection and his proof
Abu Yusuf argues that if a person performs tayammum with the intention to enter Islam, his prayer later is valid. He reasons that Islam is the head of all acts of worship, and since entering Islam is an act of worship valid immediately, the tayammum is valid.
Abu Yusuf's analogy: if tayammum can be done for prayer, it should be valid for any act of worship that is valid in that state.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad reject Abu Yusuf's view. Their proof is the hadith 'Earth is the purifier of the Muslim,' which restricts tayammum to the Muslim's prayer. They also note that entering Islam is not an act that requires purity in the same way as prayer.
The hadith is understood to limit tayammum to acts that are essentially prayer or its substitutes (like funeral prayer and prostration of recitation).
4
Note the secondary dispute on sujood al-shukr
Muhammad considers the prostration of thanksgiving a valid act of worship requiring purity, so tayammum for it is valid. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf disagree, as they do not consider it an act of worship that requires purification.
This is a separate ikhtilaf within the school; the preferred view is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (not valid).
5
Examine the subordinate variance from al-Nawadir
Two narrations suggest that mere intention of tayammum (without specifying the purpose) may suffice, allowing prayer with that tayammum. However, these are from al-Nawadir (less authoritative) and do not override the established view.
These narrations show that intention is a key factor, but the standard ruling requires intention for the specific act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني: العُدْرُ المُبيحُ للتّيمم، كبُعْدِهِ مِيلاً . به الصلاة في الأصح، وكذا لزيارة القبور، والأذان والإقامة، والسلام ورده، كالسلام، أو الإسلام، لا تجوز به الصلاة، عند عامة المشايخ، إذ ليس جزءاً من الصلاة، ولا يتوقف صحته على الطهارة، وإن كان عبادة مقصودة، وقال أبو يوسف: تصح صلاته بتيممه لدخوله في الإسلام، لأنه نوى قربة مقصودة، تصح منه في الحال، فيصح تيممه، إذ الإسلام رأس القرب، واعتبار سائرها به، بخلاف تيمم الكافر للصلاة، لعدم صحتها منه في الحال، ولم يعتبره أبو حنيفة، ومحمد لإسلامه، وهو الأصح، لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ( التراب طهور المسلم ) جعله طهوره، فيقتصر عليه لثبوته، على خلاف القياس، ولو تيمم لسجدة الشكر، لا يصلي به، خلافاً لمحمد، لأنها قربة عنده، لا عندهما، وسنذكر الخلاف فيها، إن شاء الله تعالى. وروى في ( النوادر ) : أنه لو مسح وجهه وذراعيه، ينوي التيمم تجوز به الصلاة. وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة فيمن تيمم لرد السلام يجوز فعلى هاتين الروايتين يعتبر مجرد نية التيمم.
Second: The excuse that permits tayammum, like his being a mile away from water. With it, prayer is valid in the most correct view, and similarly for visiting graves, the adhan and iqamah, and the greeting and its return, like the greeting, or entering Islam. Prayer is not valid with it, according to most scholars, since it is not part of prayer, nor does its validity depend on ritual purity, even if it is an intended act of worship. Abu Yusuf said: His prayer is valid with his tayammum for entering Islam, because he intended an intended act of worship that is valid from him immediately, so his tayammum is valid, for Islam is the head of acts of worship, and the rest are considered by it, unlike the tayammum of a disbeliever for prayer, due to its not being valid from him immediately. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad did not consider it for his Islam, and that is the most correct, because of his ﷺ saying: 'Earth is the purifier of the Muslim.' He made it his purifier, so it is restricted to that due to its being established contrary to analogy. And if one performs tayammum for the prostration of thanksgiving, he does not pray with it, unlike Muhammad, because according to him it is an act of worship, but not according to the two. We will mention the disagreement concerning it, if Allah wills. And it is narrated in al-Nawadir: that if he wipes his face and forearms intending tayammum, prayer is permissible with it. And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa concerning one who performs tayammum to return a greeting: it is permissible. According to these two narrations, mere intention of tayammum is considered.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Idah addresses the second condition that permits tayammum: the excuse. It begins by stating that being a mile from water is an excuse. Then it discusses the validity of tayammum for acts other than the obligatory prayer, such as visiting graves, adhan, iqamah, returning greetings, and entering Islam. The majority of scholars hold that tayammum is not valid for these acts because they are not part of the prayer and do not require ritual purity. However, Abu Yusuf argued that tayammum for entering Islam is valid because Islam is a great act of worship that is valid immediately. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad disagreed, and the most correct view is that tayammum is only valid for prayer, based on the hadith 'Earth is the purifier of the Muslim.' The passage then notes a disagreement over tayammum for the prostration of thanksgiving, with Muhammad considering it a valid act of worship, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf do not. Finally, two narrations from al-Nawadir and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad indicate that the mere intention of tayammum (without specifying the purpose) may be sufficient, allowing prayer with that tayammum.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Ritual purification with earth (or dust) as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or its use is harmful.
ميل (mīl): A unit of distance, approximately 1.866 km (4000 cubits), used as the minimum distance from water that permits tayammum.
سجدة الشكر (sajdat al-shukr): A prostration performed as a voluntary act of thanksgiving to Allah for a blessing or relief from calamity.
النوادر (al-Nawādir): A collection of rare or non-standard transmissions in Hanafi fiqh, as opposed to zahir al-riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is only valid for obligatory prayer (and its substitutes) according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, and intention for the specific act is crucial.

The Excuses that Permit Tayammum in Hanafi Fiqh
Explains the list of excuses for tayammum from the matn: distance, illness, cold, fear, thirst, kneading, and lack of tools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven excuses for tayammum, state the conditions for each, and apply the Hanafi principle of hardship (haraj) to determine when tayammum is valid.

Core Idea
Tayammum is permitted to avoid certain hardship: distance, illness, cold, enemy, thirst, kneading, or lack of tools, each with specific conditions.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah elaborates on the second condition of tayammum: the existence of a legitimate excuse. The author systematically lists seven excuses, each with precise conditions derived from the Quranic principle of removing hardship. Understanding these excuses is essential for correctly applying tayammum in diverse situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching principle
Recognize that tayammum is founded on the Quranic principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj). The verse 'And He has not placed upon you in the religion any hardship' (Al-Hajj 22:78) is cited as the basis. All excuses must be analyzed through this lens.
The principle of hardship underlies every excuse and shapes the conditions.
2
List the excuses and their specific conditions
Work through each excuse in order: distance (measured by mile, with ghalabat al-zann), illness (fear of worsening or delayed recovery), cold (outside built-up area, no heated water), enemy (fear for self, property, or trust), thirst (for self, companion, or animal), kneading (not cooking broth), and lack of tools (rope/bucket). For each, identify the condition that must be met.
Note that 'kneading' is essential; cooking broth is not because it can be done without water.
3
Analyze the role of ghalabat al-zann
The commentary emphasizes that overwhelming probability (ghalabat al-zann) is the standard for fear-based excuses (illness, cold, enemy). This is the 'basis of the ruling' as stated in the text. Understand that mere possibility is insufficient; a reasonable likelihood of harm is required.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi differences on the mile definition
There are varying narrations: Muhammad estimated the mile as one mile in one narration and two miles in another; Abu Hanifa reportedly said two miles if water is ahead, otherwise one mile. The chosen view (al-mukhtar) is one mile (1/3 farsakh). This is the operative definition.
The mile is defined as 1/3 farsakh = 12,000 common cubits = approximately 1.866 km.
5
Apply the rule to borderline cases
The passage gives a key distinction: if a person is threatened with death for leaving wudu and performs tayammum, he must repeat the prayer later (i'ada). However, if he is imprisoned while traveling, he does not repeat, because the norm in travel is lack of water. Apply this logic to other scenarios.
The repetition is required only when the excuse is a direct threat for abandoning wudu, not when it is a general constraint.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني: من شرائط التيمم: ( العُدْرُ المُبيحُ للتّيمم)، وهو على أنواع، أشار إليه بقوله: (كبُعْدِهِ)، أي: الشخص (ميلا)، والمعتبر غلبة الظن في تقديره به، لأنها كتحقق بعده ميلاً، والميل في كلام العرب منتهى مد البصر، وقيل للأعلام المبنية في طريق مكة أميال؛ لأنها بنيت على مقادير منتهى مد البصر، والمراد هنا: ثلث الفرسخ، والفرسخ : اثنا عشر ألف خطوة، وهي ذراع ونصف بذراع العامة، وهو : أربع وعشرون إصبعاً بعدد حروف لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله، والتقدير بالميل هو المختار؛ لأنه لم يذكر في ظاهر الرواية حداً في حالة العلم به، فقدره محمد في رواية بميل، وفي أخرى بميلين، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه ميلان إن كان أمامه، وإلا فميل، وقيل: بما لو صاح بأعلى صوته لم يسمعه أهل الماء، والميل هو المختار، لأنه يتحقق عن ماء، ولو في المصر، وحصولِ مرض، وبرد، يَخافُ مِنْهُ التَّلف، أو المرض، وخوف عدو، وعطش، واحتياج لعجن، لا لطَبْخِ مرق، ولفقدِ آلةٍ في طهور. لزوم الحرج، بالذهاب إليه، بالنظر إلى جنس المكلفين، وما شرع التيمم إلا لدفع الحرج، ولذا قدم الآية المرضى على المسافرين، لأنهم أحوج إلى الوضوء من غيرهم، فيجوز ببعده (عَنْ مَاء) (وَلَو) كان بعده عنه ( في المِصْرِ ) على الصحيح للحوق الحرج. (و) من العذر (حُصُولِ مَرَضِ) يخاف منه اشتداد المرض أو بطء البرء باستعمال الماء، كالمحموم، وذي الجدري، أو بحركه كالمبطون، ومشتكي العرق المدني، (وَبَردٍ، يَخافُ مِنْهُ) بغلبة الظن (التلف) لبعض أعضائه، (أوِ المرض) إذا كان خارج المصر، يعني العمران، ولو القرى التي يوجد بها الماء المسخن، أو ما يسخن به سواء كان جنباً، أو محدثاً، وإذا عدم الماء المسخن، أو ما يسخن به في المصر، فهي كالبرية، والقول بمنع المحدث حدثاً أصغر من التيمم لم يكن إلا لعدم تحقق الضرر في الوضوء عادة. وما منع الجنب المقيم منه، إلا لكونه مبنياً على مجرد الوهم فتصحيح المنع فيهما غير متجه، فلذا لم نتبعه، واعتبرنا غلبة الظن الضرر مطلقاً، لأنه المدار لمبنى الحكم، وَمَا جَعَلَ عَلَيْكُمْ فِي الدِّينِ مِنْ حَرَج [ الحج: ۷۸ ]. (وَخَوفِ عَدُوٌّ) سواء كان آدمياً أو غيره، وسواء خاف على نفسه أو ماله أو أمانته، أو خافت فاسقاً عند الماء، أو خاف المديون المفلس الحبس، ولا إعادة عليهم، بخلاف من توعد بقتل ونحوه، لترك الوضوء، فتيمم، فإنه يعيد، ولو حبس في السفر لا يعيد، لأن الغالب في السفر عدم الماء، وقد انضم إليه عذر الحبس، (وَعَطش) سواء خافه على نفسه أو رفيقه، ولو رفيق القافلة، فضلاً عن رفيق الصحبة، أو دابته، ولو كلباً وسواء خاف العطش في الحال أو المآل؛ لأن المعد للحاجة كالمعدوم. واحْتِيَاجُ لِعَجْنِ)، لأنه من الأمور الضرورية ( لا لطبخ مرق)، لاندفاع الحاجة بدونها، (وَلفَقْدِ آلَة)، كحبل ودلو، لتحقق العجز، فصار وجود البئر كعدمها، وإذا أمكنه إيصال ثوب طاهر، وإخراج الماء به قليلاً قليلاً، ولا ينقص أكثر من قيمة الماء ببله لا يتيمم، وإلا تيمم. تنبيه: الماء الموضوع في الفلوات، بحب، أي: خابية، لا يمنع التيمم؛ لأنه لم يوضع إلا
Second: Among the conditions of tayammum is the excuse that permits tayammum. It is of various types, which [the author] indicated by his saying: (such as his being) (a mile away). What is considered is overwhelming probability in estimating it by that, for it is as if he is verified to be a mile away. In Arab speech, a mile is the extremity of eye sight; and the landmarks built on the road to Mecca are called miles because they were built according to measures of the extremity of eye sight. What is intended here is one-third of a farsakh, and the farsakh is twelve thousand steps, which is one and a half cubits by the common cubit, and that is twenty-four fingers by the number of letters of 'La ilaha illa Allah, Muhammad Rasul Allah.' Estimation by the mile is the chosen view, because no limit is mentioned in the apparent transmitted ruling in the case of knowing it, so Muhammad estimated it in one narration as a mile, and in another as two miles. Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that it is two miles if water is ahead of him, otherwise a mile. And it is said: as if he shouted at the top of his voice and the people of the water did not hear him. The mile is the chosen view, because it is verified concerning water, even if he is in the city, and the occurrence of illness, and cold from which he fears destruction or illness, and fear of an enemy, and thirst, and need for kneading, not for cooking meat broth, and for lack of a tool for purification. Hardship is incurred by going to it, considering the generality of those obligated. And tayammum was legislated only to remove hardship, and therefore the verse (Al-Ma'idah: 6) presents the sick before the travelers because they are more in need of wudu than others. So it is permissible by his distance from water even if he is in the city, according to the correct view, due to hardship. And from the excuse is the occurrence of illness from which one fears worsening of the illness or delay of cure by using water, like a feverish person and one with smallpox, or by moving it like one with diarrhea, and those suffering from Madinian sweat. And cold from which he fears, by overwhelming probability, destruction of some of his limbs, or illness, if outside the city, meaning the built-up area, even if there are villages where heated water or means to heat it exist, whether he is junub or had minor impurity. If heated water or means to heat it are not found in the city, then it is like the desert. The statement preventing one with minor impurity from tayammum was only due to the lack of verified harm from wudu normally. And what prevents a resident junub from it is only because it is based on mere illusion, so correcting the prevention in both is not sound, therefore we did not follow it, and we considered overwhelming probability of harm absolutely, because it is the basis of the ruling. And Allah says: 'And He has not placed upon you in the religion any hardship' (Al-Hajj: 78). And fear of an enemy, whether human or other, and whether he fears for himself, his property, or his trust; or if he fears a transgressor at the water, or if the debtor fears prison for his insolvency; and there is no repetition upon them, unlike one who is threatened with killing or the like for leaving wudu, so he performs tayammum; then he repeats. If he is imprisoned while traveling, he does not repeat, because the norm in travel is lack of water, and the excuse of imprisonment has been added to it. And thirst, whether he fears it for himself or his companion, even a companion of the caravan, let alone a close companion, or his riding beast, even a dog; and whether he fears thirst immediately or in the future, because what is prepared for need is like nonexistent. And need for kneading, because it is from necessary matters, not for cooking meat broth, because the need is removed without it. And for lack of a tool, like a rope and bucket, due to confirmed inability, so the existence of the well becomes like its non-existence. And if he can reach a pure garment and extract water with it little by little, and it does not decrease more than the value of the water by its wetness, he does not perform tayammum; otherwise he performs tayammum. Caution: Water placed in deserts, in a habb (i.e., a jar), does not prevent tayammum; because it was only placed for [a specific need]
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the second condition (shart) of tayammum: the excuse that permits it. It begins by defining the first type of excuse: being a mile away from water. The commentary explains the measurement of a mile, noting that the preferred definition is one-third of a farsakh (twelve thousand common cubits). There is a difference of opinion: Muhammad estimated it as a mile or two miles in different narrations, and al-Hasan narrates Abu Hanifa's view that it is two miles if water is ahead, otherwise one mile. The commentary emphasizes that the mile is chosen because it is verified. Then it lists the remaining excuses from the matn: being in a city but far from water, illness (with examples like fever, smallpox, diarrhea, and Madinian sweat), cold weather outside the city that could lead to destruction or illness, fear of an enemy (including harm to property or trust), thirst (for oneself, companions, or animals), need for kneading (not cooking), and lack of tools (like rope and bucket) to draw water. The commentary provides detailed rules for each excuse, often referencing Quranic verses (4:43, 22:78) and the principle of removing hardship. For illness, it clarifies that the harm must be likely, not merely imagined, and that the same applies to cold, enemy, thirst, etc. The commentary also distinguishes between travel and residence, and notes that if one is threatened with death for leaving wudu, he must repeat the prayer after performing tayammum, but not if imprisoned in travel. Finally, it addresses a warning about water stored in jars in the desert: such water does not prevent tayammum because it is not put there for general use.

Key Terms
ميل (mīl): A unit of distance equal to 4000 common cubits, approximately 1.866 km, used as the threshold for distance from water permitting tayammum.
فرسخ (farsakh): A unit of distance equal to 3 miles, about 5.598 km.
مصر (misr): A large city with judicial authority, administrative power, and markets.
مبطون (mabṭūn): A person suffering from diarrhea or stomach ailment.
خابية (khābiyah): A large earthenware jar used for storing water, oil, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) If he is threatened with death for leaving wudu
C) If he fears thirst for his dog
D) If he lacks a tool to draw water

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is a substitute for wudu when one of seven specific excuses is met, each with conditions grounded in the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj).

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Excuses for Tayammum: Distance, Illness, Cold, Enemy, Thirst, Dough, Equipment
Listing excuses for tayammum with conditions and principle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the excuses that permit tayammum according to the Hanafi school and apply the principle of predominant probability of harm (ghalabat al-zann) to determine its validity in given scenarios.

Core Idea
Tayammum is permitted to remove hardship, defined by predominant probability of harm, not certainty.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah expands on the excuses that allow a Muslim to perform tayammum instead of wudu or ghusl. While many know tayammum is permitted in travel or illness, the Hanafi school details a broader range of excuses, including cold, fear of enemy, thirst, need for dough, and lack of equipment. The overarching principle is the removal of hardship (haraj), grounded in the Quranic verse 'And He has not placed upon you in the religion any hardship' (al-Hajj 22:78). The author also addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether minor hadath and residency are valid excuses, affirming that predominant probability of harm suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
The passage clarifies that tayammum is permissible when water is unavailable or its use causes harm. The overarching principle is the removal of hardship (haraj). State the ruling in your own words.
The ruling is mubah (permissible) but can become wajib if no water is found or using water is harmful.
2
List each excuse and its condition
Work through the passage and extract each distinct excuse: distance from water, illness, cold, fear of enemy, thirst, need for kneading dough (not cooking soup), and lack of equipment. For each, note the specific condition that triggers the excuse (e.g., fear of death or illness from cold, fear for property or person from enemy).
Pay attention to exceptions: cooking soup is not an excuse, and threatened killing for not performing wudu requires repeating the prayer.
3
Understand the principle of predominant probability
The author rejects the view that tayammum is prohibited for minor hadath and resident junub based on mere illusion. Instead, he adopts the position that predominant probability (ghalabat al-zann) of harm justifies tayammum. Identify the Quranic evidence cited and explain how it supports this principle.
The verse 'And He has not placed upon you in the religion any hardship' is used to base the ruling on removing hardship.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The passage mentions that some earlier Hanafi scholars prevented a person with minor hadath and a resident junub from performing tayammum. The author states 'we did not follow it' (lam nattabi'hu). Determine why the author rejects this view and what criterion he uses instead.
The rejection is based on the principle that rulings are built on predominant probability of harm, not certainty or mere illusion.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a scenario where a person is in a city and water is available but extremely cold, such that using water is likely to cause illness, should he perform tayammum? Trace the reasoning: is water present? Is there predominant probability of harm? What does the passage say about cold inside vs outside the city?
The passage states that cold inside the city with heated water still permits tayammum if there is no means to heat water, as it becomes like the wilderness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(وَخَوفِ عَدُوٌّ ) سواء كان آدمياً أو غيره، وسواء خاف على نفسه أو ماله أو أمانته، أو خافت فاسقاً عند الماء، أو خاف المديون المفلس الحبس، ولا إعادة عليهم، بخلاف مــن توعد بقتل ونحوه، لترك الوضوء، فتيمم، فإنه يعيد، ولو حبس في السفر لا يعيد، لأن الغالب في السفر عدم الماء، وقد انضم إليه عذر الحبس، (وَعَطش) سواء خافه على نفسه أو رفيقه، ولو رفيق القافلة، فضلاً عن رفيق الصحبة، أو دابته، ولو كلباً وسواء خاف العطش في الحال أو المآل؛ لأن المعد للحاجة كالمعدوم. واحْتِيَاجُ لِعَجْنِ)، لأنه من الأمور الضرورية ( لا لطبخ مرق)، لاندفاع الحاجة بدونها، (وَلفَقْدِ آلــة)، كحبل ودلو، لتحقق العجز، فصار وجود البئر كعدمها، وإذا أمكنه إيصال ثوب طاهر، وإخراج الماء به قليلاً قليلاً، ولا ينقص أكثر من قيمة الماء ببله لا يتيمم، وإلا تيمم.
Due to water [being far], even if in the city, and occurrence of illness, and cold from which one fears death or illness, and fear of enemy, and thirst, and need for kneading [dough], not for cooking soup, and lack of equipment for purification. Necessity of hardship by going to it, considering the generality of the obligated persons, and tayammum was legislated only to remove hardship. Hence the verse (1) placed the sick before travelers, because they are more in need of wudu than others. So it is permitted due to distance from water, even if it is in the city, according to the correct opinion due to hardship. And among the excuses: occurrence of illness from which one fears worsening or slow recovery by using water, like a feverish person or one with smallpox, or by movement like one with diarrhea and one suffering from Madani sweat; and cold from which one fears by predominant probability death of some limbs or illness if outside the city, meaning the inhabited area, even villages where heated water exists or something to heat it, whether one is junub or hadath. And if heated water or means to heat it are absent in the city, then it is like the wilderness. The saying preventing a minor hadath from tayammum was only due to the lack of actual harm in wudu usually. And what prevented a resident junub from it was only because it is based on mere illusion, so confirming prohibition in both is not appropriate; hence we did not follow it, and we considered predominant probability of harm absolutely, because it is the basis of the ruling: 'And He has not placed upon you in the religion any hardship' [al-Hajj 78]. And fear of enemy, whether human or otherwise, whether he fears for himself, his property, or his trust, or a woman fears a transgressor at the water, or a debtor fears imprisonment, and there is no repetition upon them, unlike one who is threatened with killing or similar for leaving wudu and performs tayammum, for he must repeat. And if imprisoned on a journey, he does not repeat, because the usual in travel is lack of water and the excuse of imprisonment is added. And thirst, whether he fears for himself or his companion, even a companion of the caravan, let alone a companion of companionship, or his animal, even a dog, whether he fears thirst immediately or eventually, because what is prepared for need is like non-existent. And need for kneading dough, because it is a necessary matter, not for cooking soup, because the need is fulfilled without it. And lack of equipment like rope and bucket, due to actual inability, so the existence of the well is like its non-existence. And if he can reach a pure cloth and extract water little by little, and the decrease does not exceed the value of the water by wetting it, he does not perform tayammum; otherwise he performs tayammum.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the excuses that permit tayammum. The author begins by stating that tayammum is permitted when water is far away, even if that distance is within a city, due to hardship. He then lists specific excuses: illness where using water may worsen the condition or delay recovery, including fevers, smallpox, diarrhea, and Madani sweat; intense cold that threatens loss of limbs or illness, especially outside the city even if heated water is available; fear of an enemy, whether human or animal, or fear for property, trust, or imprisonment—with the nuance that if a person is threatened for leaving wudu and performs tayammum, he must repeat the prayer, but if imprisoned on a journey, he does not repeat; thirst for oneself, a companion, or even an animal; the need to knead dough for bread (a necessity) but not for cooking soup; and lack of equipment like a rope or bucket to draw water, making the well effectively non-existent. The passage also discusses the principle that tayammum is based on predominant probability of harm, citing the Quranic verse on hardship.

Key Terms
تَيَمُّم (tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
حرج (haraj): Hardship or difficulty that the Shariah aims to remove.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a valid excuse for tayammum?
A) Fear of an enemy taking one's property
B) Need to cook soup
C) Lack of a rope to draw water from a well
D) Fear of worsening an illness by using water

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is permitted for a wide range of hardships beyond travel and illness, all governed by the principle of removing hardship (haraj) based on predominant probability of harm.

Water Stored in Deserts and Tayammum
Ruling on water stored in deserts for drinking and its effect on tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on water placed in deserts for drinking and determine when tayammum is permitted based on the water's designation.

Core Idea
Water reserved for drinking in the desert does not block tayammum — its purpose restricts its use.

When traveling in the desert, you may come across water stored in jars. Is this water available for wudu or tayammum? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling based on the water's intended use. In this lesson, we explore the distinction between water placed for drinking and water placed for wudu, and how it affects the permissibility of tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the location and container
The water is in desert (falawat) and stored in a container (khabiyah). Note the context: water is scarce.
2
Determine the water's purpose
The water was placed only for drinking (shurb). This purpose restricts its use.
3
Apply the ruling on tayammum
Because it's reserved for drinking, it does not prevent tayammum. The presence of water does not automatically make tayammum invalid.
4
Consider the abundance exception
If the water is abundant (kathir), one might infer unrestricted use, so tayammum is not allowed, and wudu is required.
5
Differentiate between water for drinking vs wudu
Water placed for drinking can be used for wudu, but water placed for wudu cannot be drunk per Imam Abu Bakr al-Fadl. This distinction is important for practical applications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه: الماء الموضوع في الفلوات ،بحب، أي: خابية، لا يمنع التيمم؛ لأنه لم يوضع إلا للشرب، وإن كان كثيراً، يستدل بكثرته على إطلاق الاستعمال، لا يتيمم. وعن الإمام أبي بكر محمد بن الفضل، أن الماء الموضوع للشرب يجوز التوضؤ منه، والموضوع للوضوء لا يباح منـه الشرب. وفي « الخلاصة : ثلاثة في سفر : جنب، وحائض طهرت، أو محدث، وميت، ومعهم ما يكفي لأحدهم، إن الماء لأحدهم فهو أحق به في الأصح، وإن كان الماء لهم، لا ينبغي لأحد أن يغتسل به، وإن كان مباحاً فالجنب أحق به في الأصح، فتتيمم المرأة وييمم الميت. وقال عامة المشايخ: الميت أولى. وفي ( المحيط » : ينبغي أن يصرفا نصيبهما إلى الميت، ويتيمما إذا كان مشتركاً.
Note: Water placed in deserts in a container, i.e., a jar, does not prevent tayammum because it is only placed for drinking. Even if it is plentiful, one might deduce from its abundance that it is unrestricted in use; one does not perform tayammum [if it is abundant]. And from Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl: water placed for drinking is permissible to make wudu from, and water placed for wudu is not permissible to drink from. And in al-Khulasa: Three people on a journey: a junub, a menstruating woman who has become pure, or a person with hadath, and a deceased, and they have water sufficient for one of them. If the water belongs to one of them, he is most entitled to it according to the most correct view. If the water is for all of them, none of them should take a full bath with it. If it is available (mubah), then the junub is most entitled to it according to the most correct view; then the woman performs tayammum and the deceased is given tayammum. And the generality of the mashayikh said: the deceased is more entitled. And in al-Muhit: It is better that the two [the junub and the woman] give their share to the deceased and perform tayammum if the water is shared.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This note discusses two issues: first, water stored in desert areas for drinking purposes does not prevent tayammum because it is reserved for drinking; however, if the water is abundant and unrestricted, then wudu from it is permissible and tayammum is not allowed. Second, when a group of people have limited water sufficient for only one person—including a junub, a menstruating woman who has become pure, a person with minor hadath, and a deceased—the ruling of priority is given. If the water is owned by one individual, he has the first right. If it is communal, the best course is for the deceased to be given priority according to the majority of scholars, as mentioned in al-Muhit. The junub is also entitled in some views, but the woman and the deceased should perform tayammum.

Key Terms
فَلَوات (falawat): Deserts or open lands where water is scarce.
خابية (khabiyah): A large jar or container for storing water or oil.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ritual purification using clean earth when water is unavailable or its use is harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If water in the desert is placed in a jar for drinking and is scarce, what is the ruling?
A) Tayammum is not allowed because water exists
B) Tayammum is allowed because it is reserved for drinking
C) Wudu must be performed from it
D) The water must be used for wudu first

Key Takeaway
The purpose for which water is stored determines its permissibility for purification: drinking water does not invalidate tayammum, but abundant water may require wudu.

Priority for Limited Water Among Multiple People
Priorities for using limited water among multiple people needing purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi priority rules for sharing limited water among a junub, menstruating woman, and deceased, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When water is scarce and multiple people need purification, the deceased takes priority over the living in the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Imagine three travelers in the desert: one is in a state of major impurity (junub), another is a menstruating woman who has become pure, and the third is a deceased person. They have only enough water to purify one of them. Who gets the water? The Hanafi school addresses this delicate ethical and legal dilemma with nuanced rules. In this lesson, we explore the different scenarios — owned water, communal water, and mubah water — and the preference for the deceased according to the majority of Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties involved
There are three people: a junub, a woman who was menstruating (now pure) or a person with minor hadath, and a deceased body.
2
Determine the water ownership
Is the water owned by one of them, communal, or mubah (ownerless)? The ruling changes.
3
Apply the priorities for owned water
If water belongs to one, that person has the highest right (ahq).
4
Apply for communal or mubah water
If communal, none should do ghusl. For mubah, the junub is most entitled in the most correct view from al-Khulasa, but the majority of mashayikh say the deceased is more entitled.
The ikhtilaf is resolved in favor of the deceased.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The text states 'wa qala 'ammatu al-mashayikh: al-mayyitu awla', so the relied-upon view is that the deceased has priority. The living should perform tayammum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه: الماء الموضوع في الفلوات ،بحب، أي: خابية، لا يمنع التيمم؛ لأنه لم يوضع إلا للشرب، وإن كان كثيراً، يستدل بكثرته على إطلاق الاستعمال، لا يتيمم. وعن الإمام أبي بكر محمد بن الفضل، أن الماء الموضوع للشرب يجوز التوضؤ منه، والموضوع للوضوء لا يباح منـه الشرب. وفي « الخلاصة : ثلاثة في سفر : جنب، وحائض طهرت، أو محدث، وميت، ومعهم ما يكفي لأحدهم، إن الماء لأحدهم فهو أحق به في الأصح، وإن كان الماء لهم، لا ينبغي لأحد أن يغتسل به، وإن كان مباحاً فالجنب أحق به في الأصح، فتتيمم المرأة وييمم الميت. وقال عامة المشايخ: الميت أولى. وفي ( المحيط » : ينبغي أن يصرفا نصيبهما إلى الميت، ويتيمما إذا كان مشتركاً.
Note: Water placed in deserts in a container, i.e., a jar, does not prevent tayammum because it is only placed for drinking. Even if it is plentiful, one might deduce from its abundance that it is unrestricted in use; one does not perform tayammum [if it is abundant]. And from Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl: water placed for drinking is permissible to make wudu from, and water placed for wudu is not permissible to drink from. And in al-Khulasa: Three people on a journey: a junub, a menstruating woman who has become pure, or a person with hadath, and a deceased, and they have water sufficient for one of them. If the water belongs to one of them, he is most entitled to it according to the most correct view. If the water is for all of them, none of them should take a full bath with it. If it is available (mubah), then the junub is most entitled to it according to the most correct view; then the woman performs tayammum and the deceased is given tayammum. And the generality of the mashayikh said: the deceased is more entitled. And in al-Muhit: It is better that the two [the junub and the woman] give their share to the deceased and perform tayammum if the water is shared.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This note discusses two issues: first, water stored in desert areas for drinking purposes does not prevent tayammum because it is reserved for drinking; however, if the water is abundant and unrestricted, then wudu from it is permissible and tayammum is not allowed. Second, when a group of people have limited water sufficient for only one person—including a junub, a menstruating woman who has become pure, a person with minor hadath, and a deceased—the ruling of priority is given. If the water is owned by one individual, he has the first right. If it is communal, the best course is for the deceased to be given priority according to the majority of scholars, as mentioned in al-Muhit. The junub is also entitled in some views, but the woman and the deceased should perform tayammum.

Key Terms
فَلَوات (falawat): Deserts or open lands where water is scarce.
خابية (khabiyah): A large jar or container for storing water or oil.
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
ميت (mayyit): A deceased person, whose body requires ritual washing (ghusl) for burial.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ritual purification using clean earth when water is unavailable or its use is harmful.
غسل (ghusl): Full body ritual washing required for janabah, menstruation, and washing the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The junub
B) The menstruating woman
C) The deceased
D) They should share equally

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when water is scarce for multiple people needing purification, the deceased's washing takes priority over the living's ghusl, according to the majority of later scholars.

Imprisoned Person Without Purification: Can One Imitate Prayer?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on imitation of prayer without purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether an imprisoned person without water or soil may imitate prayer and explain the internal dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Purification is a condition for prayer eligibility; without it, imitation is invalid even in confinement.

This passage addresses a pressing fiqh scenario: a prisoner who has no access to water or soil for purification. Does the Shariah permit such a person to simply mimic the movements of prayer to honor the time? The Hanafi school has an internal debate on this, with Abu Hanifa taking a strict position and Abu Yusuf offering a concession. Understanding this ruling clarifies the foundational role of purification in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine the act (imitation of prayer) and its legal status according to Abu Hanifa: prohibited (haram). Note that he says the person should not imitate the prayer performers.
The text uses 'لا يتشبه بالمصلين' — he does not imitate.
2
Understand the basis
Abu Hanifa argues that purification is a condition for eligibility (shart al-ahliyyah) to perform prayer. Without it, imitation is invalid, just as a menstruating woman cannot imitate prayer.
The analogy (qiyas) to the menstruating woman is key: she lacks eligibility, so imitation would be meaningless.
3
Contrast with Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf allows imitation with gestures (ima) to honor the time of prayer, but he cautions against actual prostration on impure ground. His correct view is that he gestures.
The phrase 'والصحيح عنده أنه يومى' indicates the correct view according to Abu Yusuf is gestures, not full sujud.
4
Resolve the ikhtilaf
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the imprisoned person should pray with the imam if possible. If not, the strict prohibition of imitation stands.
The text says 'والاعتماد على أنه مع الإمام' — reliance is that he is with the imam.
5
Apply the principle
Reflect on how this ruling underscores that purification is a non-negotiable condition for valid prayer, regardless of circumstance. The exception of joining a congregation provides a practical way out.
This reinforces the Hanafi emphasis on taharah as a constitutive condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه آخر: المحبوس الذي لا يجد طهوراً من ماء أو تراب لا يتشبه بالمصلين عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن الطهارة شرط أهلية أداء الصلاة، فإن الله جعل أهل مناجاته من هو طاهر لا محدث، والتشبه إنما يصح من الأهل، ألا ترى أن الحائض لا تتشبه بالمصلين؛ لعدم الأهلية، وقال أبو يوسف: يتشبه إقامة لحق الوقت بركوع وسجود، إن وجد مكاناً يابساً والصحيح عنده أنه يومى، لأنـه لـو سـجـد لـصـار مستعملاً للنجاسة، بعدم وجود الطاهر واختلفت الرواية عن محمد، والاعتماد على أنه مع الإمام.
Another note: The imprisoned person who does not find any purifier of water or soil does not imitate the prayer performers according to Abu Hanifa; because purification is a condition for the eligibility to perform prayer. Indeed, Allah has made those who are pure, not those with hadath, as the people of His private conversation. Imitation is only valid from the eligible. Do you not see that the menstruating woman does not imitate the prayer performers due to lack of eligibility? And Abu Yusuf said: He imitates to fulfill the right of the time, with bowing and prostration, if he finds a dry place. The correct [view] according to him is that he gestures, because if he prostrates, he would become a user of impurity due to the absence of pure [ground]. And there is a difference in narration from Muhammad, and the reliance is that he is with the imam [i.e., follows the congregation when possible].
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This note addresses the situation of a prisoner who has no access to water or soil for tayammum. According to Abu Hanifa, such a person should not imitate the movements of prayer (like bowing and prostrating) because purification (taharah) is a condition for the validity of prayer. Without it, the person is not eligible for prayer at all. He compares to a menstruating woman who is also not eligible. Abu Yusuf, however, says he should imitate to honor the time, but the correct view is that he gestures (i.e., indicates the movements without actual prostration on the ground because it is impure). There are two narrations from Muhammad; the relied-upon position is that he prays with the imam if possible. This shows the Hanafi internal ikhtilaf on whether eligibility for prayer can be waived in extreme circumstances.

Key Terms
التشبه بالمصلين (al-tashabbuh bi al-musallin): Imitating the physical postures of prayer (like bowing and prostrating) without proper purification.
أهلية (ahliyyah): Legal eligibility or capacity to perform an act of worship.
محبوس (mahbus): Imprisoned person who is confined and cannot access purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why should an imprisoned person without water or soil not imitate prayer?
A) Because the prayer would be too difficult
B) Because he lacks the condition of purification for eligibility
C) Because he is sinful
D) Because he might miss the congregation

Key Takeaway
Purification is a non-negotiable condition for prayer eligibility; even in confinement, imitation without purification is invalid unless one can join a congregation.
