Tayammum and Ability Through Another
Ruling on tayammum for someone who cannot use water but can get assistance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum for a person who can get assistance for wudu, identify the intra-madhhab disagreement, and explain the underlying principle of qudrah bi al-ghayr.

Core Idea
Ability through another is not true ability in Abu Hanifa's view, but the relied-upon position obligates using help.

This lesson examines a nuanced fiqh scenario: a person who cannot perform wudu due to physical incapacity but can find someone to assist them. While one might think tayammum is an option, the Hanafi school holds that if assistance is available, tayammum is not allowed. However, there is an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the principle of 'ability through another' (al-qudrah bi al-ghayr), which affects not only wudu but also other obligations like hajj. We will trace this disagreement and see how the later authorities resolved it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its categories
Identify the act as tayammum. Note the three scenarios: no helper (tayammum allowed by consensus), servant helper (tayammum not allowed by agreement), non-servant helper (apparent school view prevents tayammum).
The text says 'اتفاقاً' for the first two scenarios, and 'ظاهر المذهب' for the third.
2
Understand the basis: Quraysh (ability)
The central question is whether ability through another (al-qudrah bi al-ghayr) counts as genuine ability. Abu Hanifa says no; the two companions say yes.
The text explains: 'لأن الإنسان يعد قادراً إذا اختص بحالة يتهيأ له الفعل متى أراد' (a person is considered able if the act is ready whenever he wants).
3
Trace the intra-madhhab dispute
Abu Hanifa has a narration allowing tayammum; his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that tayammum is not allowed if assistance exists. Husam al-Din chose the companions' view.
The text says 'واختار حسام الدين قولهما' (Husam al-Din chose their view).
4
Apply the principle to other cases
The principle extends to hajj (son offering wealth and obedience does not obligate father according to Abu Hanifa) and to qibla direction or moving from a najis bed (if one can be aided, they must accept help).
The text uses analogy: 'ولهذا قلنا لو بذل الابن لأبيه المال والطاعة لا يلزمه الحج'.
5
Note Muhammad's exception
Muhammad adds a nuance: in a city, tayammum is not allowed unless the person has both hands cut off, because such a person is unlikely to find help and the inability is lasting.
This shows the school's attention to circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه آخر: العاجز عن استعمال الماء بنفسه، ولا يجد من يوضئه تيمم اتفاقاً، وإن وجد خادماً، كعبده وولده وأجيره لا يجوز له التيمم، اتفاقاً كما في ( المحيط » ، بناء على اختيار بعضهم، وإن وجد غير خادمه لو استعان به أعانه، ولو زوجته فظاهر المذهب أنه لا يتيمم، مـن غـيـر خـلاف بـيـن أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه، لقدرته على الوضوء، وعن أبي حنيفة أنه يتيمم، وعلى هذا إذا عجز عن التوجه إلى القبلة، أو عن التحول عن فراش نجس، ووجد من يوجهه ويحوله، بناء على أن القدرة بالغير لا تعد قدرة عنده، لأن الإنسان يعد قادراً، إذا اختص بحالة يتهيأ له الفعل متى ا أراد، وهذا لا يتحقق بقدرة غيره، ولهذا قلنا: لو بذل الابن لأبيه المال والطاعة، لا يلزمه الحج، لما قلنا، وعندهما تثبت القدرة بالغير ) ، لأن آلته صارت كالته بإعانته واختار «حسام الدين» قولهما، وعن محمد: لا يتيمم في المصر، إلا أن يكون مقطوع اليدين، لأن الظاهر أنه يجد من يوض وضئه، والعجز على شرف الزوال، بخلاف مقطوعهما
Another note: The one unable to use water himself and does not find anyone to perform wudu for him, performs tayammum by agreement. If he finds a servant, like his slave, son, or hired worker, tayammum is not permissible for him, by agreement as in al-Muhit, based on the choice of some. If he finds someone other than his servant, if he seeks help, he will be assisted; even his wife, so the apparent school is that he does not perform tayammum, without disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions, due to his ability to perform wudu. And from Abu Hanifa [another narration] that he performs tayammum. And upon this, if he is unable to face the qibla or to move from a najis bed, and finds someone to turn him and move him, it is based on the principle that ability through another is not considered ability according to him, because a person is considered able if he has a state that prepares him for the action whenever he wants, and this is not realized by another's ability. Hence we said: If a son offers his father wealth and obedience, hajj is not obligatory upon him, for what we said. According to them (the two companions), ability is established through another, because his instrument becomes like his own with assistance. Husam al-Din chose their view. And from Muhammad: He does not perform tayammum in the city unless he has both hands cut off, because the apparent situation is that he will find someone to perform wudu for him, and the inability is about to disappear, unlike the one with both hands cut off.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This note deals with a person who cannot use water due to physical inability but can find someone to help him. By consensus, if he has no helper at all, he may perform tayammum. But if he has a helper like a servant, son, or hired worker, tayammum is not allowed because he is able to perform wudu through them. If the helper is not a servant (like a stranger or wife), the relied-upon view (zahir al-madhhab) is that he also cannot do tayammum, without disagreement among Abu Hanifa and his two companions. However, there is a weaker narration from Abu Hanifa allowing tayammum. The underlying principle is whether ability through another counts as ability. Abu Hanifa generally does not consider it, unlike the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Husam al-Din chose the companions' view. Muhammad further distinguishes: in the city, tayammum is not allowed unless the person has both hands cut off, because such a person is unlikely to find help. This shows the nuanced application of the principle of ability (qudra) in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
القدرة بالغير (al-qudrah bi al-ghayr): Ability through someone else's assistance to perform an act.
العجز (al-ʿajz): Inability; the condition of being unable to perform an act due to lack of physical capacity or means.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in this passage, which of the following is CORRECT?
A) A person with a broken arm who can have wudu performed by his son must do tayammum.
B) A person who cannot find any helper may do tayammum by consensus.
C) A person whose wife can help him may choose between wudu with help and tayammum.
D) A person with both hands cut off must do wudu with help even if no one is available.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the availability of assistance establishes ability to perform wudu, making tayammum impermissible; this is based on the preferred view of the two companions over Abu Hanifa's weaker narration.

Fear of Missing Funeral Prayer as Excuse for Tayammum
Ruling with proof: fear of missing funeral prayer permits tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which the fear of missing the funeral prayer permits tayammum, and distinguish between the correct view and the zahir al-riwayah position.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer has no substitute; tayammum is permitted even for a junub if he would miss it entirely.

This lesson examines a specific exception in the rules of tayammum: the fear of missing the funeral prayer. Because the funeral prayer cannot be repeated or made up, the Hanafi school grants a concession to perform tayammum even if one is in a state of major impurity. However, this concession has precise conditions regarding how much of the prayer would be missed, and there is an internal difference of opinion within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exceptional ruling
What is the general rule for a junub? He must perform ghusl or wudu to pray. The exception here permits tayammum.
2
Locate the rationale (sabab)
Why is the funeral prayer special? Because it has no substitute if missed entirely.
3
Determine the condition for the exception
When exactly does the fear of missing allow tayammum? When the person would miss all takbirs if he performed wudu or ghusl.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
What is the difference between the correct view (al-sahih) and the zahir al-riwayah? The correct view requires missing all takbirs; the zahir al-riwayah allows tayammum even to avoid delay.
5
Apply the rule to the guardian (wali)
Why is the wali not eligible for this concession? Because he can wait or repeat the prayer if someone else prays.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَخَوفِ فَوْتِ صَلاةِ جَنَازَةٍ، ولو جنباً؛ لأنها إذا فاتت لا خلف لها، وفيـه إشارة إلى أنه إذا توضأ لم يدرك شيئاً من تكبيراتها، فإن كان يدرك بعضها لو توضأ، لا يتيمم، وفيـه إشارة أيضاً إلى أن الولي لا يخاف الفوت، لأنه ينتظر، ويعيدها لو صلى غيره. قال في « الهداية » : هو الصحيح، وفي «ظاهر الرواية يجوز له أيضاً التيمم لكراهة تأخير الصلاة عـلـيـهـا، وصححه
And fear of missing the funeral prayer, even if one is junub; because if it is missed, there is no replacement for it. And in it is an indication that if he were to perform wudu and not catch any of its takbirs, [he performs tayammum]; if he would catch some of them if he performed wudu, he does not perform tayammum. And in it is also an indication that the guardian (wali) does not fear missing it, because he waits and repeats it if someone else prays. It is said in al-Hidayah: That is the correct view. And in the zahir al-riwayah, it is also permissible for him to do tayammum due to the dislike of delaying the prayer over it, and he (the author) corrected it.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage discusses the fear of missing the funeral prayer as a valid excuse for tayammum, even for a person in a state of major impurity (junub). The reason is that the funeral prayer cannot be made up if missed; it is a one-time obligation. If performing wudu would cause missing even one takbir, tayammum is allowed. However, if he can catch some takbirs by doing wudu, he must do wudu and cannot do tayammum. The wali (guardian) of the deceased is not considered to have the excuse of fear of missing because he can wait or repeat the prayer. The text quotes al-Hidayah stating that the correct view is that tayammum is allowed only if he would miss all takbirs, but the zahir al-riwayah includes the option of tayammum even to avoid delaying the prayer. The author seems to prefer the more lenient view.

Key Terms
صلاة الجنازة (salat al-janazah): Funeral prayer, an obligation (fard kifayah) that cannot be made up if missed.
تكبيرات الجنازة (takbirat al-janazah): The four takbirs said during the funeral prayer; missing one is missing part of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because janazah prayer is optional
B) Because it has no substitute if missed
C) Because a junub cannot pray anyway
D) Because water is usually unavailable

Key Takeaway
The fear of missing the funeral prayer is a unique excuse for tayammum because the prayer cannot be made up, but the concession only applies if the entire prayer would be missed, not just part.

Tayammum for Fear of Missing Funeral Prayer
Rulings on tayammum when fearing loss of funeral prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on tayammum for fear of missing a funeral prayer and apply the condition regarding catching some takbirs.

Core Idea
Tayammum is permitted for fear of missing a funeral prayer only if missing it entirely, and not if any part can be caught with wudu.

Imagine you are about to attend a funeral prayer but you are in a state of major impurity. You know that if you perform ablution, you will miss the entire prayer. The Hanafi school provides a concession: you may perform tayammum. However, this concession is precisely limited. In this lesson, we explore the ruling and its key condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that tayammum is permissible for fear of missing a funeral prayer. Determine the legal category: it is a rukhsah (concession), not a general rule.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites a hadith from Ibn Abbas and the practice of Ibn Umar. Identify that the dalil is Sunnah ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Examine the condition
The passage specifies: if by performing ablution one would catch some takbirs (even one), then tayammum is not allowed. Understand the threshold: fear of missing the entire prayer, not just part.
4
Consider the janabah case
The ruling applies even if one is in major impurity (janabah). This is because the necessity is even greater.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخوفِ فَوْتِ صلاة جنازة، ولو جنباً؛ لأنها إذا فاتت لا خلف لها، وفيه إشارة إلى أنه إذا توضأ لم يدرك شيئاً من تكبيراتها، فإن كان يدرك بعضها لو توضأ، لا يتيمم، وفيه إشارة أيضاً إلى أن الولي لا يخاف الفوت، لأنه ينتظر، ويعيدها لو صلى غيره. قال في « الهداية » : هو الصحيح، وفي «ظاهر الرواية يجوز له أيضاً التيمم لكراهة تأخير الصلاة عليها، وصححه السرخسي»، وإذا حضرت جنازة أخرى قبل أن يقدر على التوضؤ، جاز له الصلاة على الثانية بالتيمم للأولى، عندهما، وقال محمد عليه الإعادة، كما لو قدر ثم عجز. (أو) خوف فوت صلاة (عيد) لو اشتغل بالوضوء، لما حكاه « السرخسي »، عن ابن عباس أنه قال: « إِذَا فَاجَأَتْكَ صَلَاةُ جَنَازَةٍ، فَخشيت فوتَها، فَصَلِّ عَلَيْهَا بالتيمم )، وما أخرجه الدارقطني، عن ابن عمر : « أَنَّه أُتِـي بجنازة وهو على غير وضوء فتيمم، ثم صلى عليها ) (۳). ونقل عنهما في صلاة العيد كذلك، ولأن كلاً منهما يفوت لا إلى بدل، (ولو) كان ( بناء) فيهما، أي في صلاة الجنازة والعيد، بأن سبقه حدث، فإنه يتيمم ويبنى على ما مضى لفواتهما بغير بدل، واقتصار الشراح على كون البناء في العيد، وقع تصويراً لا احترازاً، لأن العلة فيهما واحدة، ولا يقال: في العيد يأمن الفوات بالذهاب للوضوء، بعد سبق الحدث؛ لمعارضة المفسد بعدم التمكن من الماء، للزحام، أو الضغينة الحاصلة لمنهيه، بامتناعه من كلامه، فلذا يبني بالتيمم مطلقاً. (وَلَيسَ مِنَ العُدْرِ خَوْفٌ) فوت ( الجُمُعَةِ والوقت) لو اشتغل بالتوضؤ؛ لأن لهما خلف، وهو الظهر في الجمعة، وإن لم يكن خلفاً حقيقة، فهو متصور بصورة الخلف، فكان لها ما يقوم مقامها والقضاء في الوقتية.

تنبيه: في «القنية » : التيمم لخوف فوت الوقت رواية عن مشايخنا، وفرع عليها لو كان على سطح ليلاً، وفي بيته ماء لكنه يخاف الظلمة؛ إن دخل البيت تيمم إن خاف فوت الوقت. وكذا يتيمم لخوف البق لو كان في كلة، أو مطر، أو حر شديد، إن خاف فوت الوقت. انتهى. وهذا كله خلاف ظاهر المذهب، وما عليه المتون والشراح، فذكرته للعلم به تتميماً للفائدة.
And fear of missing funeral prayer, even if one is in major impurity, because if it is missed there is no substitute. And it contains an indication that if he performs ablution he will not catch any of its takbirs, so if he would catch some of them if he performed ablution, he does not perform tayammum. And it also contains an indication that the guardian does not fear the loss, because he waits and repeats it if someone else prayed. He said in Al-Hidayah: it is the correct view, and in Zahir al-Riwayah it is also permissible for him to perform tayammum due to the dislike of delaying the prayer for her, and Al-Sarkhasi authenticated it. (Or) fear of missing the 'id prayer if he busied himself with ablution, due to what Al-Sarkhasi narrated from Ibn Abbas that he said: 'If a funeral prayer suddenly comes upon you and you fear missing it, pray for her with tayammum.' And what Al-Daraqutni narrated from Ibn Umar: 'A funeral was brought to him while he was without ablution, so he performed tayammum and then prayed for her.' And it is transmitted from them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding 'id prayer similarly, and because each of them is missed without substitute. (And) if there is (building) in them, i.e., in funeral and 'id prayer, such that a hadath occurs to him, then he performs tayammum and builds upon what passed because they are missed without substitute, and the restriction of the commentators to building being in 'id occurred as illustration not limitation, because the cause is the same in both. And it is not said: in 'id, he is safe from missing by going for ablution after the hadath, because of the corruption of not being able to access water due to crowding or the ill feeling occurring to the one who forbids him by his refraining from speech, so he builds with tayammum absolutely. (And it is not an excuse) fear of missing (Friday prayer and the time) if he busied himself with ablution, because they have a substitute: Zuhr for Friday, and if not a substitute in reality, it is conceived in the form of a substitute, so they have something that takes their place, and making up for time-bound prayers. A note: In Al-Qunyah: tayammum for fear of missing time is a narration from our scholars, and they derived from it: if he is on a roof at night and in his house there is water but he fears darkness, if he enters the house, he performs tayammum if he fears missing the time. And similarly he performs tayammum for fear of bedbugs if he is in a mosquito net, or rain, or severe heat, if he fears missing the time. End. And all of this is contrary to the apparent madhhab and what the texts and commentaries are upon, so I mentioned it for knowledge of it, completing the benefit.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Idah discusses cases where fear of missing a prayer permits tayammum. The primary ruling is: if one fears losing a funeral prayer, even in a state of janabah (major impurity), one may perform tayammum because the funeral prayer has no substitute if missed. The text clarifies that if by performing ablution one would miss all the takbirs, tayammum is permitted; if one would catch some, then ablution is required. Additionally, the guardian of the deceased does not fear the loss because he can wait or repeat the prayer if someone else prayed; however, in Zahir al-Riwayah, tayammum is also allowed for him due to the dislike of delaying. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding the guardian. The passage then applies the same ruling to 'id prayer, citing hadith from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. It also covers building upon the prayer after a hadath in funeral and 'id prayers, where tayammum suffices. Finally, it states that fear of missing Friday prayer or a time-bound prayer is not an excuse because they have substitutes (Zuhr for Friday, and qada for time-bound). The note from Al-Qunyah presents a minority view allowing tayammum for fear of missing the time due to obstacles like darkness, but the commentator notes this is against the apparent madhhab.

Key Terms
خوف فوت (khowf fawt): The fear that an act of worship will be completely missed if one does not perform tayammum now.
بدل (badal): A substitute prayer that can replace the missed one, such as Zuhr for Friday or qada for time-bound prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is tayammum permitted for fear of missing a funeral prayer?
A) Whenever one fears missing even one takbir.
B) Only if one fears missing the entire prayer and is in a state of major impurity.
C) Only if one fears missing the entire prayer, regardless of impurity status.
D) It is never permitted; wudu is always required.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum for fear of missing a funeral prayer is a concession only when the entire prayer would be missed; if any part can be caught with ablution, ablution is required.

The Guardian's Dilemma: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Tayammum for Funeral
Intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the guardian's tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the guardian's tayammum for fear of missing a funeral prayer and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The guardian cannot use tayammum for fear of loss because he can wait or repeat, unlike others.

What about the deceased's guardian? He has the duty to pray for the deceased, but also has the ability to wait for another funeral or repeat if someone else prayed. Does he share the same concession? The Hanafi school has an internal difference on this point. In this lesson, we examine the positions of Abu Hanifa, the two companions, and the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed party
The text explicitly refers to 'al-wali' (the guardian). Understand who this is: the person responsible for the funeral arrangements, often a close relative.
2
State the Hanafi difference
Abu Hanifa holds that the guardian does not fear loss because he can wait for a later funeral or repeat if someone else has prayed. Therefore, he should not perform tayammum. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, in Zahir al-Riwayah, permit tayammum for him due to the dislike of delaying the prayer.
3
Examine the evidence for each side
For Abu Hanifa: the guardian has the ability to avoid loss, so the condition of 'fear of loss' is not met. For the two companions: the dislike of delaying the prayer makes tayammum preferable to waiting.
4
Determine the preferred view
The text states that Al-Hidayah (through Al-Marghinani) declares Abu Hanifa's view as 'al-sahih' (the correct one). Al-Sarkhasi authenticated the opposing view, but the relied-upon fatwa is Abu Hanifa's.

Source Text

وخوفِ فَوْتِ صلاة جنازة، ولو جنباً؛ لأنها إذا فاتت لا خلف لها، وفيه إشارة إلى أنه إذا توضأ لم يدرك شيئاً من تكبيراتها، فإن كان يدرك بعضها لو توضأ، لا يتيمم، وفيه إشارة أيضاً إلى أن الولي لا يخاف الفوت، لأنه ينتظر، ويعيدها لو صلى غيره. قال في « الهداية » : هو الصحيح، وفي «ظاهر الرواية يجوز له أيضاً التيمم لكراهة تأخير الصلاة عليها، وصححه السرخسي»، وإذا حضرت جنازة أخرى قبل أن يقدر على التوضؤ، جاز له الصلاة على الثانية بالتيمم للأولى، عندهما، وقال محمد عليه الإعادة، كما لو قدر ثم عجز. (أو) خوف فوت صلاة (عيد) لو اشتغل بالوضوء، لما حكاه « السرخسي »، عن ابن عباس أنه قال: « إِذَا فَاجَأَتْكَ صَلَاةُ جَنَازَةٍ، فَخشيت فوتَها، فَصَلِّ عَلَيْهَا بالتيمم )، وما أخرجه الدارقطني، عن ابن عمر : « أَنَّه أُتِـي بجنازة وهو على غير وضوء فتيمم، ثم صلى عليها ) (۳). ونقل عنهما في صلاة العيد كذلك، ولأن كلاً منهما يفوت لا إلى بدل، (ولو) كان ( بناء) فيهما، أي في صلاة الجنازة والعيد، بأن سبقه حدث، فإنه يتيمم ويبنى على ما مضى لفواتهما بغير بدل، واقتصار الشراح على كون البناء في العيد، وقع تصويراً لا احترازاً، لأن العلة فيهما واحدة، ولا يقال: في العيد يأمن الفوات بالذهاب للوضوء، بعد سبق الحدث؛ لمعارضة المفسد بعدم التمكن من الماء، للزحام، أو الضغينة الحاصلة لمنهيه، بامتناعه من كلامه، فلذا يبني بالتيمم مطلقاً. (وَلَيسَ مِنَ العُدْرِ خَوْفٌ) فوت ( الجُمُعَةِ والوقت) لو اشتغل بالتوضؤ؛ لأن لهما خلف، وهو الظهر في الجمعة، وإن لم يكن خلفاً حقيقة، فهو متصور بصورة الخلف، فكان لها ما يقوم مقامها والقضاء في الوقتية.

تنبيه: في «القنية » : التيمم لخوف فوت الوقت رواية عن مشايخنا، وفرع عليها لو كان على سطح ليلاً، وفي بيته ماء لكنه يخاف الظلمة؛ إن دخل البيت تيمم إن خاف فوت الوقت. وكذا يتيمم لخوف البق لو كان في كلة، أو مطر، أو حر شديد، إن خاف فوت الوقت. انتهى. وهذا كله خلاف ظاهر المذهب، وما عليه المتون والشراح، فذكرته للعلم به تتميماً للفائدة.
And fear of missing funeral prayer, even if one is in major impurity, because if it is missed there is no substitute. And it contains an indication that if he performs ablution he will not catch any of its takbirs, so if he would catch some of them if he performed ablution, he does not perform tayammum. And it also contains an indication that the guardian does not fear the loss, because he waits and repeats it if someone else prayed. He said in Al-Hidayah: it is the correct view, and in Zahir al-Riwayah it is also permissible for him to perform tayammum due to the dislike of delaying the prayer for her, and Al-Sarkhasi authenticated it. And if another funeral prayer is attended before he is able to perform ablution, it is permissible for him to pray the second with the tayammum for the first, according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Muhammad said he must repeat, as if he was able and then became unable. (Or) fear of missing the 'id prayer if he busied himself with ablution, due to what Al-Sarkhasi narrated from Ibn Abbas that he said: 'If a funeral prayer suddenly comes upon you and you fear missing it, pray for her with tayammum.' And what Al-Daraqutni narrated from Ibn Umar: 'A funeral was brought to him while he was without ablution, so he performed tayammum and then prayed for her.' And it is transmitted from them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding 'id prayer similarly, and because each of them is missed without substitute. (And) if there is (building) in them, i.e., in funeral and 'id prayer, such that a hadath occurs to him, then he performs tayammum and builds upon what passed because they are missed without substitute, and the restriction of the commentators to building being in 'id occurred as illustration not limitation, because the cause is the same in both. And it is not said: in 'id, he is safe from missing by going for ablution after the hadath, because of the corruption of not being able to access water due to crowding or the ill feeling occurring to the one who forbids him by his refraining from speech, so he builds with tayammum absolutely. (And it is not an excuse) fear of missing (Friday prayer and the time) if he busied himself with ablution, because they have a substitute: Zuhr for Friday, and if not a substitute in reality, it is conceived in the form of a substitute, so they have something that takes their place, and making up for time-bound prayers. A note: In Al-Qunyah: tayammum for fear of missing time is a narration from our scholars, and they derived from it: if he is on a roof at night and in his house there is water but he fears darkness, if he enters the house, he performs tayammum if he fears missing the time. And similarly he performs tayammum for fear of bedbugs if he is in a mosquito net, or rain, or severe heat, if he fears missing the time. End. And all of this is contrary to the apparent madhhab and what the texts and commentaries are upon, so I mentioned it for knowledge of it, completing the benefit.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Idah discusses cases where fear of missing a prayer permits tayammum. The primary ruling is: if one fears losing a funeral prayer, even in a state of janabah (major impurity), one may perform tayammum because the funeral prayer has no substitute if missed. The text clarifies that if by performing ablution one would miss all the takbirs, tayammum is permitted; if one would catch some, then ablution is required. Additionally, the guardian of the deceased does not fear the loss because he can wait or repeat the prayer if someone else prayed; however, in Zahir al-Riwayah, tayammum is also allowed for him due to the dislike of delaying. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding the guardian. The passage then applies the same ruling to 'id prayer, citing hadith from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. It also covers building upon the prayer after a hadath in funeral and 'id prayers, where tayammum suffices. Finally, it states that fear of missing Friday prayer or a time-bound prayer is not an excuse because they have substitutes (Zuhr for Friday, and qada for time-bound). The note from Al-Qunyah presents a minority view allowing tayammum for fear of missing the time due to obstacles like darkness, but the commentator notes this is against the apparent madhhab.

Key Terms
ولي (wali): The guardian responsible for burying and praying over the deceased, typically a close relative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), why does the guardian not perform tayammum for fear of missing a funeral prayer?
A) Because he is usually in a state of purity.
B) Because he can wait for another funeral or repeat if someone else prayed.
C) Because tayammum is only for women.
D) Because funeral prayer does not require purity.

Key Takeaway
The guardian's ability to wait or repeat distinguishes him from others; the correct view is that he does not use tayammum for fear of missing the funeral prayer.
